SMART GLOVE ASSISTIVE ROBOT SYSTEM ‚Äî FULL TECHNICAL / SOFTWARE ARCHITECTURE REPORT
================================================================================

Scope: complete technical documentation of the two codebases that make up the
system ‚Äî

  1. OrangePI client  (c:\Users\user\Desktop\OrangePI\)
     The wearable/robot-side program. Runs on an OrangePi Zero 2W. Owns all
     physical hardware: glove (flex sensors + IMU + vibration motors over
     UART), USB camera, USB/serial MS200 LiDAR, microphone, speaker.

  2. Feature server  (c:\Users\user\Desktop\server_app\)
     The compute-side program. Runs on a separate (Windows) machine. Has no
     sensors; receives JSON requests over TCP, runs the heavy ML models
     (OCR, YOLO currency detection) and TTS synthesis, persists debug
     artifacts/session reports, and serves a small live HTTP dashboard.

Each section below covers one cohesive module group in full depth: purpose,
method-by-method pipeline walkthrough, every third-party library and exactly
what it is used for, key classes/functions (signatures, parameters, return
values, side effects), exact request/response data shapes, and a dedicated
"Concrete Scenarios" subsection enumerating the normal/happy path PLUS every
failure mode, edge case, and degraded/partial outcome actually implemented in
the code (empty results, malformed input, hardware absent, network down, low
confidence, repeated/rapid triggers, concurrency, abort/shutdown handling).

Every section ends with a ready-to-use "DIAGRAM GENERATION PROMPT" ‚Äî a
self-contained paragraph naming the real classes/functions/constants in that
module, meant to be pasted into an AI image/diagram generator (or turned into
a Mermaid diagram) to produce an accurate pipeline diagram for that subsystem.

================================================================================
SECTION 0 ‚Äî SYSTEM OVERVIEW, SHARED ARCHITECTURE & CLIENT-SERVER INTERFACE
================================================================================

SECTION 0 ‚Äî SYSTEM OVERVIEW, SHARED ARCHITECTURE & CLIENT-SERVER INTERFACE
===========================================================================

This section ties together everything documented in the rest of this report. 
It explains, in one place: what the two codebases are, how they physically/logically split responsibilities,
what is literally shared between them (the wire protocol), and how a message travels end-to-end from a gesture on the glove to a spoken answer 
in the user's ear.

0.1 THE TWO CODEBASES AT A GLANCE
----------------------------------

There are two independent Python programs that only ever talk to each other over one TCP socket:

1. **OrangePI client** (`c:\Users\user\Desktop\OrangePI\`) ‚Äî runs ON the wearable robot/glove hardware (an OrangePi Zero 2W). It owns every physical sensor and actuator: the UART-connected glove (flex sensors + IMU + 3 vibration motors), a USB camera, a USB/serial MS200 LiDAR, a microphone, and a speaker. Its job is: recognize what the user wants (gesture or voice), acquire whatever sensor data that requires (a photo, a LiDAR scan, a spoken sentence), and either process it fully on-device (LiDAR/SLAM, gesture recognition, Gemini vision calls) or ship it off to the server for heavier processing (OCR, currency recognition, TTS synthesis), then read the answer back to the user via speech and haptics.

2. **Feature server** (`c:\Users\user\Desktop\server_app\`) ‚Äî runs on a separate, more powerful machine (a Windows PC, given its `.venv` and the OCR/TTS handler comments referencing "server Windows voice (SAPI/Piper)"). It has no sensors and no direct user interaction; it exists purely to accept JSON requests over TCP, run the compute-heavy models (EasyOCR, a custom YOLOv8 currency detector, TTS synthesis), persist debug artifacts and session reports to disk, and reply with either text/structured data or pre-synthesized audio. It also runs a small embedded HTTP dashboard (via the LiDAR handler) for humans to watch mapping/navigation sessions live in a browser.

Everything the two sides agree on is confined to a handful of files: `OrangePI/net/client.py` (client-side wire implementation), `server_app/protocol.py` (server-side wire implementation), and the informal but consistent JSON message conventions (`feature`, `type`/`action`, `frame`, `tts`, `quit`) used by every feature/handler pair.

0.2 THE SHARED WIRE PROTOCOL ‚Äî THE ONE TRUE CONTRACT
------------------------------------------------------

Both sides implement the exact same low-level framing independently (this is intentional duplication, not a shared library import ‚Äî the two programs never import from each other):

  WIRE FORMAT: [4-byte big-endian unsigned length prefix][UTF-8 JSON body]

Client side ‚Äî `OrangePI/net/client.py`, class `ServerLink`:
  - `ServerLink(host, port, timeout=120.0)` ‚Äî one persistent socket, guarded by a `threading.Lock` so all features safely share it.
  - `connect()` ‚Äî `socket.create_connection((host, port), timeout=20)`, then sets a 120 s steady-state timeout.
  - `send(feature: str, msg: dict) -> dict | None` ‚Äî THE single method every feature module calls. It:
      1. Auto-reconnects if `self.sock is None` (returns `None` immediately if that reconnect also fails).
      2. Copies the caller's dict (never mutates the original) and injects `payload["feature"] = feature`.
      3. If `payload["frame"]` is raw `bytes`/`bytearray`, base64-encodes it in place so the whole payload is JSON-safe.
      4. Serializes to JSON, prefixes with `struct.pack(">I", len(data))`, and sends.
      5. Reads back a framed reply the same way and `json.loads`s it.
      6. On ANY failure (socket error, timeout, malformed JSON, peer disconnect) ‚Äî resets the socket to `None` and returns `None`. It never raises to the caller; every feature must null-check the return value.
  - Reconnection strategy is **lazy**: there is no heartbeat or background reconnect thread. The very next `send()` call after a failure is what re-establishes the connection.

Server side ‚Äî `server_app/protocol.py`:
  - `recv_exact(sock, n) -> bytes | None` ‚Äî loops `sock.recv()` until exactly `n` bytes are collected or the peer closes (`None`).
  - `recv_msg(sock) -> dict | None` ‚Äî reads the 4-byte length prefix, then that many bytes, `json.loads`s it; catches `JSONDecodeError`/`UnicodeDecodeError` and returns `None` on malformed payloads (logging `"[PROTO] recv_msg: malformed payload ... ‚Äî dropping message"`) rather than crashing the connection.
  - `send_msg(sock, payload: dict) -> None` ‚Äî mirrors the client's framing exactly; raises `ConnectionError` on `OSError` (this is caught further up in `feature_server.py`, documented in its own section).

This 4-byte-length-prefixed-JSON scheme is the **entire** interoperability surface between the two codebases. Every other design decision (which feature strings exist, what an individual payload contains, how errors are surfaced) is a convention, not an enforced contract ‚Äî which is why the report below calls out several places where the two sides have quietly drifted (e.g. `env_awareness.py` and all four LiDAR feature classes send everything under the literal string `"lidar"`, regardless of which Python class actually triggered it, relying on an `action`/`mode` sub-field to disambiguate server-side).

0.3 THE `feature` KEY ‚Äî HOW THE SERVER ROUTES A MESSAGE
----------------------------------------------------------

Every single message the OrangePi sends carries a top-level `"feature"` string, injected automatically by `ServerLink.send(feature, msg)`. The feature server's dispatch loop (`feature_server.py`) reads this string and looks it up in a handler registry to decide which Python object's `handle(msg)` method processes the request. The feature strings actually observed in this codebase, and their server-side counterpart handler:

  | Client `feature` string | Sent by (OrangePi)                                   | Handled by (server)         |
  |--------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------|------------------------------|
  | `"ocr"`                  | `features/ocr_reader.py` (`{"type":"scan","frame":...}`) | `handlers/ocr.py`            |
  | `"tts"`                  | `features/ocr_reader.py`'s `_srvspeak()` helper (`{"text":...}`) | inferred `handlers/tts.py` / `handlers/tts_handler.py` + `tts.py` |
  | `"money"`                | `features/money_recognition.py` (`{"type":"hello"|"voice","text":...,"frame":...}`) | `handlers/money.py`          |
  | `"lidar"`                | `features/lidar_nav.py` (all four LiDAR feature classes) AND `features/env_awareness.py` (fire-and-forget telemetry only) | `handlers/lidar.py`          |
  | `"programmable"`         | never actually sent (see `features/programmable.py`) | no handler exists            |

This table is the master cross-reference for "what is shared and how the interface works" between the two projects: it is the only place where a name/string must stay in sync across two independently-maintained codebases with no shared import, no schema file, and no automated contract test. A typo in either `Feature.name`/hardcoded string on the client, or in a handler's registered `name` on the server, would silently misroute or drop messages rather than raising a clear error at connection time.

0.4 THE COMMON RESPONSE SHAPE
--------------------------------

Nearly every handler returns a dict containing at minimum:
  - `"tts"` (str) ‚Äî text to be spoken; empty string means "say nothing" (used for silent telemetry acks like `map_update`/`pose_update`).
  - `"quit"` (bool) ‚Äî signals the calling feature's loop to end the session (used heavily by the stateful `money` handler's voice dialogue).

Some handlers (`ocr`) additionally return structured fields (`text`, `page`, `word_count`, `chunks`, `chunk_wavs`, `announcement_wav`) alongside `tts`, letting the client either play server-synthesized audio directly or fall back to local espeak-ng TTS using the raw text if synthesis wasn't available. The `money` handler, by contrast, communicates literally everything (denominations, totals, change-making instructions) as natural-language strings inside `tts` ‚Äî it has no structured "here are the bills" field at all, reflecting its voice-first, no-visual-feedback design for a blind user.

0.5 END-TO-END MESSAGE LIFECYCLE (THE CANONICAL EXAMPLE)
------------------------------------------------------------

Using OCR ("read this page to me") as the canonical trace, because it touches nearly every layer documented elsewhere in this report:

  1. User performs the gesture bound to `FEAT:Book reader` (or says a matching voice command). `GestureEngine`/`VoiceListener` (gesture_hub) fires an event into `HubStateMachine.dispatch()`.
  2. `HubStateMachine._launch_feature()` builds a `FeatureContext(link, abort, feedback, gesture_queue)` and calls `OCRReader.run(ctx)` (features/ocr_reader.py), blocking the hub's main loop until it returns.
  3. Inside `run()`, a voice/gesture command loop waits for "scan"; on trigger it captures a JPEG via OpenCV (with a Laplacian-sharpness quality gate), then calls:
         `ctx.link.send("ocr", {"type": "scan", "frame": <raw jpeg bytes>})`
  4. `ServerLink.send()` base64-encodes the frame, frames the JSON with the 4-byte length prefix, and blocks on the socket (up to 120 s) for a reply.
  5. Server-side, `feature_server.py`'s accept/read loop calls `protocol.recv_msg(sock)`, gets the dict, reads `msg["feature"] == "ocr"`, and dispatches to `OCRHandler.handle(msg)`.
  6. `OCRHandler._handle_scan()` decodes the base64 JPEG, writes two debug images to `ocr_debug/`, runs EasyOCR, detects a page number, chunks the text, synthesizes WAV audio per chunk (delegating to the shared `tts.py`/`handlers/tts_handler.py` machinery), and logs one line to `ocr_metrics.jsonl`.
  7. The handler returns a dict; `feature_server.py` calls `protocol.send_msg(sock, reply)`, framing and sending it back.
  8. `ServerLink.send()` on the OrangePi reads the framed reply, `json.loads`s it, and returns the dict to `OCRReader.run()`.
  9. `OCRReader` plays the pre-synthesized WAV chunks through `Feedback.play_raw()` (falling back to local espeak-ng if synthesis failed), driven by a page-reading sub-loop that also listens for pause/skip/rewind gestures.
  10. On any failure at steps 4-8 (`send()` returns `None`), the OrangePi never crashes ‚Äî it speaks "Server not reachable." locally and returns to its scan-wait loop; no partial state is persisted.

Every other feature (`money`, `lidar`) follows this same 10-step shape, differing only in payload contents, statefulness (money's server-side `Session` object persists across many messages on the same connection; OCR's handler is stateless per-request), and how aggressively the client guards each `send()` call with a try/except (OCR and env_awareness always guard; several `lidar_nav.py` call sites do not ‚Äî see that section's scenario notes for the safety implication).

0.6 WHAT IS TRULY "SHARED" BETWEEN THE TWO CODEBASES
---------------------------------------------------------

To directly answer "what is shared and how does the interface work":

  - **Shared, by design, at the protocol level**: the 4-byte length-prefix + JSON framing (independently implemented twice, must stay byte-for-byte compatible), the set of `feature` strings, and the informal `tts`/`quit`/`frame` field vocabulary.
  - **Shared, by convention, at the payload level**: each feature's exact JSON schema (e.g. OCR's `{"type":"scan","frame":...}`, LiDAR's `{"action": "...", ...}`) is agreed only by both sides' authors reading each other's code ‚Äî there is no schema file, protobuf, or OpenAPI spec enforcing it.
  - **Shared, incidentally, via constants that must match**: `server_app/handlers/lidar.py`'s `_MAP_RES`/`_MAP_ORIG` constants (0.05 m/px, 15.0 m origin) must numerically match whatever `slam_engine.py` on the OrangePi used to render its map PNGs, or the server's live pose-dot overlay will drift relative to the map image ‚Äî this is a silent, undetectable-at-runtime coupling.
  - **NOT shared**: no code, classes, or modules are imported across the two codebases. `orangepi_client.py` (the legacy monolithic client) independently re-implements the same wire framing a third time, confirming this project's pattern of duplicating the protocol rather than factoring it into a shared library ‚Äî acceptable given the two sides run on different machines/OSes and were likely developed at different times, but worth flagging as a source of drift risk (e.g., the `requirements_server.txt` vs. actual `handlers/ocr.py` OCR-library mismatch documented in that section is exactly this kind of drift, just on the dependency-declaration side rather than the wire-protocol side).

0.7 RESILIENCE POSTURE COMPARISON ACROSS FEATURES
------------------------------------------------------

A cross-cutting observation worth calling out once here rather than repeating per-feature: not every feature treats a `None` return from `ServerLink.send()` (or an unreachable/slow server) with equal care.

  - `features/ocr_reader.py` and `features/money_recognition.py`: every `send()` call site checks for `None` and degrades to a spoken local error message; the feature's loop continues cleanly.
  - `features/env_awareness.py`: wraps its server telemetry pings in a bare `try/except Exception: pass` ‚Äî the server is treated as purely optional/best-effort, and a failure there can never affect the user-facing Gemini-based description flow (which doesn't use the feature server at all).
  - `features/lidar_nav.py`: several call sites (`pose_update` sends, `_send_report`, some `_send_map` calls) are **not** wrapped in try/except and are not `None`-checked ‚Äî since `ServerLink.send()` can block for up to its full 120 s socket timeout on a dead/slow connection, an unreachable feature server can stall the safety-critical obstacle-avoidance haptics loop for the entire timeout window. This is the single most significant cross-feature inconsistency in the codebase's error-handling posture and is flagged in detail in the LiDAR-navigation section.

0.8 HOW TO READ THE REST OF THIS REPORT
--------------------------------------------

Each remaining section below documents one cohesive module group in full technical depth: purpose, full pipeline walkthrough (method-by-method, in execution order), every third-party library and exactly what it's used for, key classes/functions with signatures/side effects, exact request/response data shapes, and ‚Äî critically ‚Äî a dedicated "Concrete Scenarios" subsection enumerating the normal/happy path plus every failure mode, edge case, and degraded/partial outcome actually implemented in the code (empty results, malformed input, hardware absent, network down, low confidence, repeated/rapid triggers, concurrent access, and abort/shutdown handling). Each section closes with a ready-to-use "DIAGRAM GENERATION PROMPT" ‚Äî a self-contained paragraph naming the real classes, functions, and constants in that module, intended to be pasted into an AI image/diagram generator (or turned into a Mermaid diagram) to produce an accurate pipeline/architecture illustration for that specific subsystem.

================================================================================
SECTION 1 ‚Äî ORANGEPI CORE ORCHESTRATION
================================================================================

# OrangePI Core Orchestration Layer ‚Äî Detailed Section Report

This section documents the top-level orchestration files of the OrangePi-based assistive robot client: the main gesture-hub entry point (`hub.py`), a legacy monolithic voice client (`orangepi_client.py`), the network transport layer (`net/client.py`, `net/__init__.py`), the UART glove driver (`glove_controller.py`), a standalone hardware test utility (`motor_test.py`), the hardware-discovery shell script (`probe_devices.sh`), and the pinned dependency manifest (`requirements_orangepi.txt`).

‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
## 1. hub.py ‚Äî Gesture Hub Main Orchestrator
‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

### 1.1 Purpose & Role
`hub.py` is the current, actively-used entry point of the entire OrangePi subsystem. It is the process that a systemd unit or manual `python3 hub.py` invocation runs on the robot's OrangePi Zero 2W. It wires together the glove hardware driver, the gesture-recognition engine, the calibration/gesture persistence stores, the text-to-speech/voice-command feedback loop, the pluggable "feature" modules (money recognition, OCR, environment awareness, LiDAR navigation, programmable-gesture management), and the single TCP link to the remote Python feature server. Unlike `orangepi_client.py` (see Section 2), `hub.py` does not itself do speech-to-text, TTS synthesis, or camera capture ‚Äî those responsibilities are delegated to `gesture_hub/*` modules, `features/*` modules, and the server. `hub.py`'s job is pure orchestration: boot sequencing, CLI argument handling, wiring callbacks between components, and running the top-level state machine loop.

### 1.2 Control-Flow Walkthrough
Process start (line 1-76): imports `argparse`, `os`, `sys`, `threading`, `time` from stdlib; `GloveController` from `glove_controller.py`; six `gesture_hub` submodules (`store`, `cal_store`, `engine`, `recorder`, `registry`, `feedback`, `state_machine`, `voice`, `diagnostics`); `ServerLink` from `net.client`; and the feature classes (`MoneyRecognition`, `OCRReader`, `EnvAwareness`, `ProgrammableGestures`, four LiDAR feature classes, and `FeatureContext`). Module-level globals `HERE`, `DEFAULT_GESTURES_PATH`, `DEFAULT_CAL_PATH` are computed relative to the script's own directory (lines 77-79) so gestures.json/calibration.json resolve correctly regardless of CWD.

`_probe_devices(feedback, link)` (line 82-120) is a helper invoked once at normal-mode boot. It checks `link.sock is not None` to report server reachability, attempts to open `cv2.VideoCapture(0)` to test the camera, queries `sounddevice.query_devices()` for a microphone with `max_input_channels > 0`, and finally calls `feedback.speak(...)` with a single combined status sentence ‚Äî this is the audible self-test a blind user hears at every boot.

`main()` (line 123-384) is the entry point invoked from `if __name__ == "__main__"` (line 383-384). Execution order:
1. Build an `argparse.ArgumentParser` with connectivity flags (`--host` default `10.254.249.159`, `--port` default `9000`, `--uart` default `/dev/ttyS5`, `--baud` default `115200`, `--alsa`), path flags (`--gestures`, `--cal`), mode flags (`--monitor`, `--calibrate`, `--threshold`, `--no-voice`), a mutually-exclusive feature-bypass group (`--money`, `--ocr`, `--env`, `--lidar`, `--obstacles`, `--mapping`, `--navigate`), LiDAR-specific flags (`--lidar-port` default `"auto"`, `--navigate-room`), and `--reset-gestures`.
2. Constructs the `FEATURES` list (line 195-204): `MoneyRecognition()`, `OCRReader()`, `EnvAwareness()`, four LiDAR feature instances (`LidarNavigation`, `LidarObstacleTest`, `LidarMappingTest`, `LidarNavigateTest`, each given `.port = args.lidar_port`, and the navigate test additionally given `.room_name`), and `ProgrammableGestures()` (deliberately last).
3. Loads `GestureStore(args.gestures)` and `CalStore(args.cal)`, then prints the loaded gesture table with flex/IMU bitmasks.
4. `--reset-gestures` path: deletes all `store.gestures` keys prefixed `"FEAT:"`, calls `store.save()`, prints a summary, and returns ‚Äî process exits without ever opening the glove.
5. Opens the glove: `controller = GloveController(port=args.uart, baud=args.baud)`; `feedback = Feedback(controller, alsa=args.alsa)`; `controller.start(wait_ready=False)` ‚Äî on failure (`False` return, e.g. serial port missing) prints an error and calls `sys.exit(1)`. Sleeps 0.5 s to let first UART frames arrive.
6. `--monitor` mode: restores calibration if present (`cal_store.restore(controller)`), calls `diagnostics.run_monitor(controller, store.gestures, say=feedback.speak)` (blocking live view), then `controller.stop()` in a `finally` and returns ‚Äî process exits after monitor session ends.
7. `--threshold` override: `controller.set_threshold(args.threshold)` (validated 10-90 inside `GloveController`); catches `ValueError`.
8. Calibration branch: if `--calibrate`, runs `diagnostics.run_calibration(controller, say=feedback.speak)`; on success saves via `cal_store.save(rest=..., bent=..., thresh_pct=...)`, speaks confirmation, and immediately calls `cal_store.restore(controller)`. On abort, falls back to restoring any previously saved calibration. If not calibrating, restores saved calibration automatically if `cal_store.has_calibration()` is true, else prints a warning that no calibration exists.
9. Feature-bypass branch (line 287-338): if any of `--money/--ocr/--env/--lidar/--obstacles/--mapping/--navigate` was passed, hub looks up the matching `Feature` instance by `.name` in a dict built from `FEATURES`, creates a `threading.Event()` named `abort`, opens a fresh `ServerLink(args.host, args.port)` and calls `link.connect()`, starts a `VoiceListener(on_command=_voice_abort)` (unless `--no-voice` or the feature is one of the LiDAR modes, which manage their own listener to avoid a microphone conflict), speaks a test-mode announcement, and calls `feat.run(FeatureContext(link=link, abort=abort, feedback=feedback, gesture_queue=None))`. This is a direct, gesture-free invocation used purely for testing individual features. `KeyboardInterrupt` is caught around the `feat.run()` call; `finally` stops the voice listener, the glove controller, and closes the link, then returns.
10. Normal-run branch (line 340-380, the actual production path): builds `engine = GestureEngine(store.gestures, on_event=None)`, `recorder = GestureRecorder()`, `registry = FeatureRegistry(FEATURES)`, `link = ServerLink(args.host, args.port)`, then `sm = HubStateMachine(controller=controller, engine=engine, recorder=recorder, registry=registry, store=store, feedback=feedback, link=link)`. Callbacks are wired imperatively after construction: `engine.on_event = sm.dispatch` and `controller.on_frame = sm.on_frame` ‚Äî meaning every parsed UART sensor frame flows synchronously, from the glove's RX thread, into `GestureEngine`, and any matched gesture flows into `HubStateMachine.dispatch`. `link.connect()` is called best-effort (features/state machine reconnect on demand later). A `VoiceListener(on_command=sm.on_voice)` is started unless `--no-voice`. `_probe_devices(feedback, link)` runs the audible self-test. Finally `sm.run()` is called and blocks ‚Äî this is the actual "main loop" of the whole robot, living inside `HubStateMachine` (not shown in the files read, but externally referenced). `KeyboardInterrupt` around `sm.run()` triggers graceful shutdown: `voice.stop()`, `sm.stop()`, `controller.stop()`, `link.close()`, in that order, in a `finally` block so shutdown always happens even on unhandled exceptions escaping `sm.run()`.

### 1.3 External Libraries
`argparse`, `os`, `sys`, `threading`, `time` (stdlib only) at top level. Inside `_probe_devices`, `cv2` (OpenCV, camera-open test) and `sounddevice` (microphone enumeration) are imported lazily inside `try/except Exception` blocks so their absence does not crash the hub ‚Äî it only degrades the self-test message.

### 1.4 Key Functions
- `_probe_devices(feedback, link) -> None`: side effect only ‚Äî speaks a diagnostic sentence; no return value. Not thread-safe by design assumption (called once, synchronously, at boot).
- `main() -> None`: the entire orchestration; no return value; has many side effects (process exit via `sys.exit(1)`/`return`, hardware I/O, network I/O, spawned threads via `VoiceListener.start()` and inside `GloveController.start()`).
- No classes are defined in `hub.py` itself ‚Äî it is purely a composition root.

### 1.5 Data Structures / Message Formats
`hub.py` does not itself construct feature payload dicts ‚Äî that responsibility belongs to each `Feature.run()` implementation and to `HubStateMachine`. However it is the file that decides **which** `link: ServerLink` object every feature receives (either the bypass-mode link or the state-machine's link), and it never sets `msg["feature"]` itself ‚Äî that key is injected by `ServerLink.send()` (see Section 3) using the caller-supplied `feature` argument, which for bypass mode is `feat.name` matched from `FEATURES`.

### 1.6 Scenarios
- **Happy path**: glove opens, calibration restored, features registered, state machine runs, features toggle via gestures, TCP link stays open and features round-trip through it.
- **Serial port missing**: `controller.start(wait_ready=False)` returns `False` ‚Üí hub prints `"[HUB] Cannot open glove on {args.uart}"` and calls `sys.exit(1)` ‚Äî the whole process aborts; nothing else initializes.
- **ATmega not sending RDY**: `start(wait_ready=False)` skips waiting so hub proceeds even with a silent glove; frames simply never arrive and gestures never fire.
- **Server unreachable at boot**: `link.connect()` failure is non-fatal ‚Äî `link.sock` stays `None`; `_probe_devices` reports "not reachable, will retry when needed"; the state machine's per-feature use of `link` triggers implicit reconnect attempts inside `ServerLink.send()` later.
- **Malformed CLI args**: `--threshold` out of 10-90 raises `ValueError`, caught and printed, hub continues without applying it.
- **Ctrl+C during normal run**: caught around `sm.run()`; hub prints a shutdown message and cleanly tears down voice, state machine, controller, and link in `finally`.
- **Ctrl+C during bypass mode**: caught around `feat.run()`; same teardown pattern scoped to bypass-mode's local `voice`, `controller`, `link`.
- **`--reset-gestures`**: purely file-system side effect (gestures.json), never touches hardware.

### 1.7 Dependencies & Shared State
`hub.py` depends on essentially the entire `gesture_hub` package and `features` package (out of scope for this section, covered elsewhere), plus `glove_controller.GloveController` and `net.client.ServerLink` from this section's files. It is the sole owner/creator of the `ServerLink` instance(s) used for the whole process lifetime; it passes that same link object into `HubStateMachine` (normal mode) or into a `FeatureContext` (bypass mode), meaning every feature module shares one persistent TCP connection rather than opening its own. The `feature` string that tags every outbound message is always a `Feature.name` value taken from the `FEATURES` list built in `hub.py`.

‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
## 2. orangepi_client.py ‚Äî Legacy/Alternate Monolithic Voice Client
‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

### 2.1 Purpose & Role, and Relationship to hub.py
This 1159-line file is a **self-contained, older/alternate entry point** ‚Äî it is *not* imported by `hub.py`, `net/client.py`, or `glove_controller.py`, and none of its symbols appear anywhere in those files. It represents an earlier architecture where a single script did everything: microphone capture, VAD, Whisper transcription, command correction, TTS (Piper/PC-WAV/espeak fallback chain), camera capture, and raw socket framing to the server ‚Äî with **no glove/gesture involvement whatsoever**. Its own docstring-equivalent comments (e.g. line 442 `"RESTORED FUNCTION (was missing in the original...)"`) and the explicit note in `net/client.py`'s own docstring ‚Äî *"Wire format is identical to the original orangepi_client/server, so the server understands it"* ‚Äî confirm that `orangepi_client.py` is the **predecessor** whose wire protocol was later extracted and reused as `net/client.py`'s `ServerLink`. It is effectively superseded by `hub.py` + `gesture_hub/voice.py` + `features/*` for production use, but it remains in the repo as a standalone voice-only client (e.g., for a keyboard/mic-only deployment without the glove, or for isolated audio-pipeline testing/tuning) ‚Äî its CLI flags (`--metrics`, `--quiet-cues`, `--no-denoise`, `--piper-model`, camera/mic/speaker overrides) suggest it also functions as the primary tuning harness for STT/TTS/camera parameters before those parameters or techniques migrate into the gesture-hub features.

### 2.2 Control-Flow Walkthrough
Imports (line 1-9): stdlib `socket, json, threading, subprocess, collections, argparse, warnings, time, struct, base64, glob, re, os, difflib, inspect, shutil, tempfile, wave, io`; third-party `cv2`, `numpy as np`, `sounddevice as sd`, `webrtcvad`, `faster_whisper.WhisperModel`. `warnings.filterwarnings("ignore")` suppresses noisy library warnings. An optional `noisereduce` import is wrapped in `try/except` (line 15-20) setting `_NR_AVAILABLE`.

Module-level constants define server address (`SERVER_HOST`, `SERVER_PORT`, same default IP/port as `hub.py`), VAD/Whisper tuning constants (sample rate 16000, frame 30 ms, VAD aggressiveness 3, ring buffer 500 ms, max record 15 s, Whisper model "base"/int8/English/beam 1, and a domain-specific `WHISPER_INITIAL_PROMPT` biasing decoding toward currency-scanner vocabulary), Piper/espeak TTS constants, and camera constants (warmup frames, capture seconds, target FPS, JPEG quality, sharpness floor). Runtime globals `AUDIO_INPUT_DEVICE`, `ALSA_OUTPUT_DEVICE`, `CAM_DEVICE`, `whisper_model`, `vad`, `_supports_hotwords`, a `_tts_lock = threading.Lock()`, `_aplay_proc`, and a global `metrics` object are declared for later population.

Classes/functions in execution order as called from `main()`:
- `Metrics` class (line 102-156): `__init__(path)` touches the JSONL file to fail fast; `log(rec)` appends a timestamped dict to both an in-memory list and the file; `summary()` prints an aggregate report (avg record/transcribe/network/total latency, Whisper confidence, fuzzy-correction rate) at shutdown.
- Auto-detect helpers `detect_mic()`, `detect_speaker()`, `detect_camera()`, orchestrated by `auto_detect_all()` (line 266-274) ‚Äî scans `sounddevice.query_devices()` for Logitech/USB mic names, parses `aplay -l` output via regex to find a headset/Logi/USB playback card, and probes `/dev/video*` nodes with `v4l2-ctl` + OpenCV open tests to find a Logitech UVC camera, falling back to `/dev/video1` hard-coded.
- Audio-cue helpers `_tone_wav()`, `init_cues()`, `play_cue()` synthesize and play short sine-wave "earcons" (listen/ack/shot/think) via a piped `aplay` subprocess.
- `correct_transcript(text)` (line 379-404): deterministic STT correction ‚Äî first an exact `KNOWN_CONFUSIONS` dict lookup (e.g. "japanese"‚Üí"lebanese", a documented Whisper mishearing), then a `difflib.get_close_matches` fuzzy snap against a fixed `COMMAND_VOCAB` set with cutoff 0.74.
- TTS chain: `_preprocess_tts()` (abbreviation expansion/cleanup for espeak), `_play_wav_bytes()` (pipes WAV bytes into `aplay`), `_piper_ready()`/`_speak_piper()` (local neural TTS via the `piper` CLI), and `speak(text, wav_bytes=None)` (line 484-531) ‚Äî the central TTS dispatcher, guarded by `_tts_lock`, that tries local Piper first, then a server-provided PC-rendered WAV, then espeak-ng as last resort, tracking which engine fired in `LAST_TTS_ENGINE`. `is_speaking()`, `stop_speaking()`, `wait_speaking()` manage playback state/barge-in.
- `load_models()` (line 559-575): instantiates `webrtcvad.Vad(VAD_AGGRESSIVENESS)` and `WhisperModel(...)`, detecting via `inspect.signature` whether the installed faster-whisper version supports `hotwords`.
- `record_with_vad()` (line 586-660): opens a `sounddevice.InputStream`, reads fixed-size frames, computes RMS noise-gating, runs `vad.is_speech()` per frame, maintains a pre-roll ring buffer (`collections.deque`) and a voiced/unvoiced ratio state machine to detect speech start/end, handles `sd.PortAudioError` xruns with a retry cap, and returns a concatenated float32 numpy array or `None`.
- `transcribe(audio)` (line 690-723): normalizes and optionally denoises (`_denoise` via `noisereduce.reduce_noise`) audio, then calls `whisper_model.transcribe(...)` with domain `initial_prompt` and optional `hotwords`, returning `(text, stats)` with average logprob / no-speech probability.
- `listen(retries=5)` (line 726-792): loop combining record‚Üítranscribe‚Üícorrect, playing earcons at each stage, speaking "I didn't catch that" / "Sorry, I did not understand" fallback prompts, and returning `(corrected_text, audit_dict)`.
- `voice_listen_loop(voice_q, stop_ev, abort_ev)` (line 795-812): a reusable daemon-thread worker (documented as shared by OCR/EnvAwareness-style features) that calls `listen()` in a loop and pushes results into a queue until a stop/abort `threading.Event` fires.
- `capture_best_frame_local()` (line 819-888): opens the webcam via a fallback chain of OpenCV backends (`V4L2`‚Üí`GStreamer`‚Üí`ANY`‚Üíraw node scan), warms up, captures for `CAM_CAPTURE_SEC` at `CAM_FPS`, scores each frame's sharpness via `cv2.Laplacian(...).var()`, keeps the sharpest, and JPEG-encodes it ‚Äî returning `None` if all frames are too blurry (`MIN_SHARPNESS`) or no camera opens.
- Network layer `_recv_exact()`, `_send()`, `connect_to_server()`, `_speak_resp()` (line 895-949) ‚Äî this is the **exact same wire protocol** later encapsulated by `ServerLink` in `net/client.py`: 4-byte big-endian length prefix + JSON, with `frame` bytes base64-encoded before serialization.
- `main()` (line 966-1157): parses CLI args (host/port/model/beam/mic/alsa/cam/piper-model/speed/pitch/amplitude/voice/cam-warmup/cam-sec/cam-fps/cam-quality/metrics/quiet-cues/no-denoise), applies overrides to globals, prints a devices-in-use banner, calls `load_models()`, speaks a ready message, calls `connect_to_server()`, sends a `{"type": "hello"}` handshake, then enters the main loop: `listen()` ‚Üí build `payload = {"type": "voice", "text": text}` ‚Üí if any `SCAN_TRIGGERS` word is present, capture and attach a base64 `frame` (JPEG bytes) after a spoken prompt ‚Üí `_send(sock, payload)` ‚Üí speak the response (`_speak_resp`) ‚Üí log `Metrics` ‚Üí loop until `resp.get("quit")`. On `resp is None` (connection lost), it speaks "Connection lost. Reconnecting.", closes the socket, sleeps 2 s, calls `connect_to_server()` again, and on success re-sends the hello handshake; on repeated failure it speaks "Could not reconnect. Exiting." and breaks. `finally` closes the socket, speaks "Goodbye.", and prints the `Metrics.summary()`.

### 2.3 External Libraries
`cv2` (camera capture, backend selection, sharpness scoring, JPEG encode), `numpy` (audio buffer math, tone synthesis, sharpness Laplacian), `sounddevice` (mic input stream, device enumeration), `webrtcvad` (frame-level voice-activity detection), `faster_whisper.WhisperModel` (CPU int8 speech-to-text), optional `noisereduce` (spectral-gating denoise), stdlib `socket`/`struct`/`json`/`base64` (wire protocol identical to `ServerLink`), `subprocess` (aplay/espeak-ng/piper/v4l2-ctl/aplay-l invocations), `threading` (TTS lock only ‚Äî no worker threads spawned in `main()` itself, though `voice_listen_loop` is designed to be run in one by callers), `difflib` (fuzzy vocabulary correction), `inspect` (feature-detects the Whisper API), `shutil.which` (locates the `piper` CLI).

### 2.4 Data Structures / Message Formats
Outbound: `{"type": "hello"}` on connect/reconnect; `{"type": "voice", "text": <str>, "frame": <raw bytes, base64-encoded by `_send`>}` per utterance. This differs structurally from the `ServerLink`/`hub.py` protocol, which always injects a `"feature"` key instead of `"type"` ‚Äî confirming these are two distinct, non-interoperable message shapes even though the length-prefixed JSON framing itself is identical. Inbound: `{"tts": <str>, "audio": <base64 wav, optional>, "quit": <bool, optional>}`.

### 2.5 Scenarios
- **Happy path**: mic/speaker/camera auto-detected, models loaded, hello handshake succeeds, loop transcribes/sends/speaks indefinitely.
- **No mic found**: `detect_mic()` returns `None` ‚Üí falls back to system default device; `record_with_vad()` may still fail to open the stream (caught, returns `None`, logged).
- **Server unreachable**: `connect_to_server()` catches `ConnectionRefusedError`, `TimeoutError`, `OSError` individually with distinct log messages, returns `None`; `main()` speaks "Cannot reach server..." and returns immediately (process exits) ‚Äî unlike `hub.py`'s `ServerLink`, this only retries mid-session on drop, not at initial connect.
- **Connection drop mid-session**: `_send()` returns `None` on `OSError`/`TimeoutError`; `main()`'s loop explicitly closes, sleeps, reconnects, and re-sends hello, warning the user the session was reset.
- **Malformed/undecodable server response**: `_send()`'s `json.loads` is inside the same `try/except (OSError, TimeoutError)` ‚Äî note `json.JSONDecodeError` is *not* caught here (unlike `ServerLink`, which explicitly catches `json.JSONDecodeError`/`UnicodeDecodeError`), so a malformed JSON reply would raise an uncaught exception and crash `main()`.
- **Camera error during scan**: `capture_best_frame_local()` returns `None` ‚Üí speaks "Camera error...", logs `outcome: "camera_error"`, continues the loop without sending a frame.
- **Ctrl+C**: not explicitly caught in `main()` (no try/except KeyboardInterrupt around the loop) ‚Äî relies on the `finally` block still running to close the socket and speak goodbye; an interrupt during `sd.InputStream` or `subprocess` calls could behave inconsistently since no gesture/glove teardown exists here (there is none to tear down).

### 2.6 Notes on Relationship to net/client.py
The docstring of `net/client.py` explicitly states its wire format is "identical to the original orangepi_client/server" ‚Äî this is a direct textual acknowledgment that `ServerLink` is a refactor/extraction of the networking logic duplicated in `orangepi_client.py`'s `_send`/`_recv_exact`/`connect_to_server`. The two files are otherwise functionally unrelated at runtime: `orangepi_client.py` is a standalone script never imported elsewhere in the codebase; it duplicates its own length-prefix framing rather than depending on `net.client.ServerLink`.

‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
## 3. net/client.py ‚Äî ServerLink (TCP Transport)
‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

### 3.1 Purpose & Role
This is the single, shared, persistent TCP connection every feature and the hub itself uses to talk to the remote Python feature server. Its docstring is explicit: "the single socket link the hub keeps open to the server... Every feature sends through here." It centralizes framing, feature-name tagging, binary-frame base64 encoding, and reconnect-on-failure logic in one small (91-line) class, `ServerLink`.

### 3.2 Control-Flow / API Walkthrough
Imports: stdlib only ‚Äî `base64`, `json`, `socket`, `struct`, `threading`.

`ServerLink.__init__(self, host, port, timeout=120.0)` (line 18-23): stores `host`, `port`, `timeout`; sets `self.sock = None`; creates `self._lock = threading.Lock()` ‚Äî this lock is the concurrency guard for the entire class.

`connect(self) -> bool` (line 25-36): calls `socket.create_connection((host, port), timeout=20)` (20 s connect timeout, distinct from the 120 s default steady-state timeout applied via `s.settimeout(self.timeout)` after connecting), stores the socket in `self.sock`, prints status, and returns `True`/`False`. On `OSError` it prints the error, sets `self.sock = None`, returns `False`. This method is idempotent and safe to call repeatedly (e.g., for reconnect).

`send(self, feature: str, msg: dict) -> dict | None` (line 38-71): the primary public entry point, entirely guarded by `with self._lock:` making it thread-safe for concurrent callers (though in practice `hub.py`'s architecture uses one link from one state machine/feature at a time). Logic: if `self.sock is None`, attempts `self.connect()` inline ‚Äî if that also fails, returns `None` immediately (no exception raised to caller). Copies the input dict (`payload = dict(msg)`) ‚Äî the caller's original dict is never mutated ‚Äî and injects `payload["feature"] = feature`. If `payload["frame"]` is `bytes`/`bytearray`, it is base64-encoded to a string in place so the payload remains JSON-serializable. Sends via `struct.pack(">I", len(data)) + data` (this is the 4-byte big-endian length prefix, exactly mirrored by `server_app/protocol.py` on the receiving end per the task context). Reads the response the same way: 4-byte length prefix via `_recv_exact(4)`, then that many bytes via `_recv_exact(n)`. Any of: prefix read fails (peer closed) ‚Üí `self._reset()` + return `None`; response JSON malformed (`json.JSONDecodeError`/`UnicodeDecodeError`) ‚Üí prints, resets, returns `None`; any `OSError`/`TimeoutError` during send/recv ‚Üí prints, resets, returns `None`. In all failure modes the function degrades to returning `None` rather than raising ‚Äî callers must always null-check the return value.

`_recv_exact(self, n) -> bytes | None` (line 73-80): loops `self.sock.recv(n - len(buf))` until `n` bytes collected or the socket returns empty bytes (peer disconnected), in which case returns `None` early.

`_reset(self) -> None` (line 82-88): closes `self.sock` if present (swallowing `OSError`), then sets `self.sock = None` ‚Äî this is what forces the *next* `send()` call to transparently reconnect via the `if self.sock is None and not self.connect()` check at the top of `send()`. This is the entire reconnect strategy: **lazy, on-demand, triggered only by the next attempted send**, not by any background thread or heartbeat.

`close(self) -> None` (line 90-91): thin wrapper around `_reset()`, called at process shutdown.

### 3.3 External Libraries
Only stdlib: `socket` (TCP connection), `struct` (big-endian `>I` length-prefix pack/unpack), `json` (payload serialization), `base64` (binary frame encoding), `threading` (the `Lock` protecting concurrent `send()` calls).

### 3.4 Data Structures / Message Format
Every message sent through `ServerLink.send(feature, msg)` becomes, on the wire: a JSON object equal to `msg` plus a mandatory `"feature"` key (the string identifying which server-side feature handler should process it ‚Äî e.g. `"Money Recognition"`, `"OCR Reader"`, `"Environment Awareness"`, `"Lidar Navigation"`, or whichever `Feature.name` is passed by the calling feature module), with any `"frame"` key holding base64 text instead of raw bytes if a camera/image frame is included. This is a generic envelope ‚Äî this file imposes no constraint on what other keys accompany `feature` (e.g. `text`, `command`, `room`, etc. are entirely feature-defined and set by the `features/*` modules covered in another section); `net/client.py`'s only universal contract is the `feature` tag itself plus the framing/encoding mechanics. The reply dict returned by `send()` is whatever JSON object the server sent back ‚Äî its shape (e.g. `tts`, `audio`, custom feature-specific keys) is likewise feature-defined and consumed by the calling feature code, not by `ServerLink`.

### 3.5 Scenarios
- **Happy path**: `connect()` succeeds at hub boot; every subsequent `send()` reuses the socket.
- **Server unreachable at boot**: `connect()` fails, `self.sock` stays `None`; hub continues running (per `hub.py`'s comment "best-effort; features reconnect on demand"); first feature that calls `link.send(...)` triggers an inline reconnect attempt.
- **Connection drop mid-session**: any recv/send failure mid-`send()` resets `self.sock` to `None` and returns `None` to the caller ‚Äî the *next* `send()` call (whenever the next feature interaction happens) transparently reconnects; there is no automatic retry within the same `send()` call, so the triggering call's data is lost and the calling feature is responsible for deciding whether to retry, error out, or notify the user.
- **Malformed server response**: caught explicitly, socket reset, `None` returned ‚Äî same recovery path as a dropped connection.
- **Concurrent access**: the `threading.Lock` serializes all `send()` calls; if two features (in theory) called `send()` from different threads simultaneously, one blocks until the other completes rather than corrupting the shared socket's read/write interleaving.
- **Shutdown**: `hub.py`'s `finally` block always calls `link.close()`.

### 3.6 Dependencies
`ServerLink` has zero dependencies on the rest of the codebase ‚Äî it is a leaf networking primitive. It is depended upon by `hub.py` (constructs and owns the instance(s)), `HubStateMachine` (uses it internally, per `hub.py`'s constructor wiring ‚Äî file not read in this section but referenced), and every `features/*.Feature.run(ctx)` implementation via `ctx.link.send(feature_name, msg)` inside `FeatureContext`.

‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
## 4. net/__init__.py
‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

This file is **empty** (a bare package marker with no content, not even a docstring). It exists solely so `net` is importable as a Python package, enabling `from net.client import ServerLink` in `hub.py`. It exposes no symbols, defines no `__all__`, and has no side effects on import.

‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
## 5. glove_controller.py ‚Äî GloveController (UART Glove Driver)
‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

### 5.1 Purpose & Role
This module is the hardware abstraction layer between the OrangePi and an ATmega microcontroller embedded in the wearable glove, communicating over a UART serial link (`/dev/ttyS5` at 115200 baud by default). It parses the glove's periodic sensor telemetry (3-axis accelerometer + 5 flex sensors + derived bend/tilt bitmasks) into structured `SensorFrame` objects, drives an asynchronous command channel for calibration and vibration-motor feedback, and exposes callback hooks (`on_frame`, `on_cal_event`) that `hub.py`'s `HubStateMachine` and diagnostics code attach to. It is the sole hardware-facing "input device" of the whole system ‚Äî everything gesture-related downstream starts here.

### 5.2 Control-Flow Walkthrough
Imports (line 26-33): `serial` (pyserial, the UART driver), `threading`, `queue`, `time`, `logging`, `re`, `dataclasses.dataclass`/`field`, `typing.Optional`/`Callable`.

Module constants: `UART_DEV = "/dev/ttyS5"`, `BAUD = 115200`, `TIMEOUT_S = 0.1` (serial read timeout), `LOG_LEVEL = logging.INFO`, `FINGER_NAMES = ["Thumb","Index","Middle","Ring","Pinky"]`.

Dataclasses: `IMUData` (aX/aY/aZ floats), `SensorFrame` (an `IMUData`, `raw_flex` list of 5 ints, `flex_bits`/`imu_bits` ints, `timestamp` defaulting to `time.time()`; computed properties `finger_bent` ‚Äî a 5-bool list decoded from `flex_bits` ‚Äî and `imu_flags` ‚Äî a dict of six named tilt/rotate booleans decoded from `imu_bits` via bitmasks 1<<0 through 1<<5 ‚Äî plus a human-readable `__str__`), and `CalibrationState` (active flag, current finger index, wait_bent flag, and 5-element `rest_vals`/`bent_vals` lists).

`_V_RE` (line 92-95): a compiled regex matching the ATmega's `V:<aX>,<aY>,<aZ>,<r0>..<r4>|<fb_hex><ib_hex>` line format. `parse_frame(line) -> Optional[SensorFrame]` (line 97-107) applies this regex and constructs a `SensorFrame`, returning `None` on no match (malformed line).

`GloveController` class (line 110-341):
- `__init__(port, baud, on_frame=None, on_cal_event=None)`: stores config and callbacks; initializes `self._ser = None`, `self._tx_q = queue.Queue()`, `self._stop = threading.Event()`, `self._ready = threading.Event()`, thread handles `self._rx_thread`/`self._tx_thread` (both `None` initially), `self.cal = CalibrationState()`, `self.last_frame = None`; configures module logging and creates `self.log`.
- `start(wait_ready=True, timeout=5.0) -> bool` (line 152-178): opens `serial.Serial(self.port, self.baud, timeout=TIMEOUT_S, write_timeout=1.0)`, catching `serial.SerialException` and returning `False` on failure (this is the exact failure path `hub.py` checks). On success, clears the stop/ready events, spawns two **daemon** threads ‚Äî `glove-rx` running `self._rx_loop` and `glove-tx` running `self._tx_loop` ‚Äî and starts them. If `wait_ready=True`, blocks up to `timeout` seconds on `self._ready.wait(timeout)`, logging a warning (but not failing) if the ATmega's `"RDY"` line never arrives; `hub.py` always calls with `wait_ready=False` so this wait never actually blocks hub boot.
- `stop()` (line 180-190): sets `self._stop`, pushes a `None` sentinel into `self._tx_q` to unblock `_tx_loop`, joins both threads with a 2 s timeout each, closes the serial port if open, logs "Controller stopped". Note: if a thread doesn't join within 2 s (e.g., blocked in a `serial.read()` call), `stop()` proceeds anyway and closes the port underneath it ‚Äî a potential race, though in practice `serial.read()` has its own 0.1 s timeout so this rarely blocks long.
- `send(cmd)`, `calibrate()`, `cal_confirm()`, `set_threshold(percent)` (validates 10-90, raises `ValueError` otherwise), `status()`, `vibrate(motor, ms)` (validates `motor in (1,2,3)` and `ms > 0`, raises `ValueError` otherwise) ‚Äî all public commands are just convenience wrappers that format a string and push it onto `self._tx_q`; actual transmission happens asynchronously in `_tx_loop`.
- `_rx_loop(self)` (line 224-239): runs in the `glove-rx` daemon thread; loops reading up to 256 bytes at a time from the serial port (catching `serial.SerialException` to break the loop entirely on hard errors), accumulating into `buf`, splitting on `b"\n"`, decoding ASCII with `errors="replace"`, and dispatching each non-empty line to `self._dispatch(line)`.
- `_tx_loop(self)` (line 241-254): runs in the `glove-tx` daemon thread; blocks on `self._tx_q.get(timeout=0.5)`, breaking on the `None` sentinel, otherwise writes+flushes the command to the serial port, catching `serial.SerialException` per-write (does not crash the thread, just logs).
- `_dispatch(line)` (line 256-289): the protocol demultiplexer ‚Äî `"RDY"` sets `self._ready`; lines starting `"V:"` are parsed via `parse_frame()` and, if valid, stored as `self.last_frame` and forwarded to `self.on_frame(frame)` if a callback is registered (this is the exact callback `hub.py` wires to `sm.on_frame`, meaning **every valid sensor frame synchronously calls into the state machine from the RX thread**, not the main thread); malformed `"V:"` lines are logged as a warning and dropped silently (no callback fires); `"CAL:"` lines go to `_handle_cal`; `"CFG:"` lines log and optionally call `on_cal_event("CFG", {...})`; `"MOT:"` lines log motor-fire confirmations; anything else logs an "Unknown line" warning.
- `_handle_cal(line)` (line 291-340): state machine for the multi-step finger calibration protocol ‚Äî `CAL:START` resets `self.cal` to a fresh active `CalibrationState` and fires `on_cal_event("START", {})`; `CAL:OPEN:<n>`/`CAL:BENT:<n>` update `self.cal.finger`/`wait_bent` and fire `on_cal_event("OPEN"/"BENT", {...})`; `CAL:R:<n>:<val>`/`CAL:B:<n>:<val>` record per-finger rest/bent raw values into `self.cal.rest_vals`/`bent_vals` and fire `on_cal_event("REST"/"BENT_VAL", {...})`; `CAL:DONE` clears `active`, logs the final rest/bent arrays, and fires `on_cal_event("DONE", {"rest": ..., "bent": ...})` ‚Äî this final event dict is exactly what `hub.py`'s `diagnostics.run_calibration()` presumably consumes to build the `cal_store.save(rest=result["rest"], bent=result["bent"], ...)` call seen in `hub.py` line 263-267.

A small embedded CLI (`_on_frame`, `motor_test_cli`, and an `if __name__ == "__main__":` block, line 344-451) lets `glove_controller.py` be run standalone: it parses `--port`/`--baud`/`--verbose`, opens a `GloveController`, and runs an interactive prompt supporting motor fire commands (`1`/`2`/`3`/`all` with optional custom ms), `cal` (start calibration), blank-enter (confirm calibration step), `thresh <n>`, `status`, and `q`/`quit`/`exit`. This is functionally near-identical to the separate `motor_test.py` file (Section 6) ‚Äî effectively a duplicated test harness embedded in the driver module itself.

### 5.3 External Libraries
`serial` (pyserial) ‚Äî the only third-party dependency, used exclusively for `serial.Serial(...)` (the UART handle) and catching `serial.SerialException`. All others (`threading`, `queue`, `time`, `logging`, `re`, `dataclasses`, `typing`) are stdlib.

### 5.4 Key Classes/Functions Summary
- `IMUData`, `SensorFrame`, `CalibrationState`: plain dataclasses, no side effects, immutable-by-convention value objects.
- `parse_frame(line: str) -> Optional[SensorFrame]`: pure function, no side effects.
- `GloveController`: the only stateful class; thread-safety notes ‚Äî `self._tx_q` (a `queue.Queue`) is inherently thread-safe for producer (`send()`, called from any thread) / consumer (`_tx_loop`) use; `self.last_frame` and `self.cal` are mutated only from the `_rx_loop` thread but *read* from arbitrary caller threads (e.g., `diagnostics.run_monitor`), with **no lock protecting them** ‚Äî a benign race in practice since these are simple attribute assignments/reads in CPython, but worth flagging as not formally thread-safe. Callbacks `on_frame`/`on_cal_event` execute **synchronously on the RX thread**, so any slow or blocking code in `HubStateMachine.on_frame` or `dispatch` would stall UART reception.

### 5.5 Data Structures / Message Formats
This module has no direct interaction with `ServerLink` or JSON payloads ‚Äî its "protocol" is entirely the ATmega UART text protocol documented at the top of the file (`RDY`, `V:...`, `CAL:...`, `CFG:...`, `MOT:...` from the ATmega; `cal`, `thresh <n>`, `status`, `mt<n> <ms>`, bare newline from the OrangePi). Its output (`SensorFrame` objects and `on_cal_event` dicts) feeds into `GestureEngine`/`HubStateMachine` in `hub.py`, which is what eventually produces the JSON feature messages sent over `ServerLink`.

### 5.6 Scenarios
- **Happy path**: `start()` opens the port, RX/TX threads run, 10 Hz `V:` frames stream continuously into `on_frame`.
- **Serial port missing/wrong**: `serial.Serial(...)` raises `serial.SerialException`, caught in `start()`, which logs an error and returns `False` ‚Äî `hub.py` treats this as fatal (`sys.exit(1)`).
- **ATmega never sends RDY**: with `wait_ready=True` (only used by the standalone CLI, not `hub.py`), `start()` logs a warning after `timeout` seconds but still returns `True` and continues.
- **Malformed `V:` line**: `parse_frame` regex fails to match, returns `None`, `_dispatch` logs `"Bad V frame"` and does not call `on_frame` ‚Äî no crash, frame is simply dropped.
- **Serial read error mid-session** (e.g., cable unplugged): `serial.SerialException` in `_rx_loop` breaks the RX loop entirely (permanently stops receiving frames until `stop()`/`start()` cycle) ‚Äî this is a hard failure with no automatic reconnect logic in this file.
- **Concurrent access**: multiple callers invoking `send()`/`calibrate()`/`vibrate()` etc. concurrently is safe because they all funnel through the thread-safe `queue.Queue`; concurrent *reads* of `last_frame`/`cal` are not lock-protected (see 5.4).
- **Calibration failure/abort**: if the user aborts partway, `self.cal.active` remains `True` and `rest_vals`/`bent_vals` stay partially filled with `None`s ‚Äî `hub.py`'s `diagnostics.run_calibration` (not read in this section) is presumably responsible for detecting an incomplete result and returning a falsy value, which `hub.py` line 272-279 explicitly handles by restoring the previous calibration or warning none exists.
- **Shutdown (Ctrl+C)**: `hub.py`'s `finally` always calls `controller.stop()`, which cleanly joins both daemon threads and closes the serial port.

### 5.7 Shared State / Dependencies
`glove_controller.py` has no dependency on any other file in this codebase ‚Äî it is a standalone hardware driver. It is depended upon by `hub.py` (constructs the single `GloveController` instance, wires `controller.on_frame = sm.on_frame`) and by `motor_test.py` (Section 6), and it exposes `GloveController` and `SensorFrame` as its public API surface (both explicitly imported by `motor_test.py`).

‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
## 6. motor_test.py ‚Äî Standalone Hardware Test Utility
‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

### 6.1 Purpose & Role
A minimal, standalone CLI script for bench-testing the glove's three vibration motors and observing live sensor frames, independent of the full gesture/hub/feature stack. It imports only `GloveController` and `SensorFrame` from `glove_controller.py` ‚Äî no `hub.py`, no `net`, no features. It is a diagnostic tool for hardware bring-up/wiring verification, not part of the production runtime pipeline.

### 6.2 Control-Flow Walkthrough
Imports: `sys`, `threading` (imported but unused directly ‚Äî no thread is spawned in this file itself; threading happens inside `GloveController`), `time`, `argparse`, and `from glove_controller import GloveController, SensorFrame`.

`on_frame(f: SensorFrame)` (line 29-44): a module-level callback (mutating module globals `frame_count`, `last_print` ‚Äî not thread-locked, but since it's invoked from the single RX thread only, this is safe) that throttles console output to once per second, printing accelerometer values, raw flex readings, bent-finger indices, and active IMU flags.

`run_cli(ctrl)` (line 47-84): an interactive `input()` loop supporting `1`/`2`/`3` (fire motor N for 300 ms default or custom ms), `all` (fire 1‚Üí2‚Üí3 in sequence with a `time.sleep((ms/1000)+0.1)` pacing delay between each), and `q`/`quit`/`exit` to break. `EOFError`/`KeyboardInterrupt` on `input()` also breaks the loop.

`if __name__ == "__main__":` (line 87-105): parses `--port` (default `/dev/ttyS5`) and `--baud` (default 115200), constructs `GloveController(port=args.port, baud=args.baud, on_frame=on_frame)`, calls `ctrl.start(wait_ready=False)` ‚Äî on `False` prints an error and `sys.exit(1)` ‚Äî then runs `run_cli(ctrl)` inside a `try/finally` that always calls `ctrl.stop()` on exit (including via Ctrl+C, which is caught inside `run_cli`'s own `input()` handling, not here).

### 6.3 External Libraries
No third-party libraries imported directly by this file ‚Äî all hardware access is delegated to `glove_controller.GloveController`, which itself uses `pyserial`.

### 6.4 Data Structures
None beyond what `glove_controller.py` defines (`SensorFrame`). No network/JSON involvement at all.

### 6.5 Scenarios
- **Happy path**: connects, streams frame summaries once/sec, fires motors on command.
- **Port missing**: `ctrl.start(wait_ready=False)` returns `False`, script prints an error and exits with code 1.
- **Ctrl+C / EOF at prompt**: cleanly breaks the input loop; `finally` calls `ctrl.stop()`.
- **Invalid motor/ms input**: `ctrl.vibrate(motor, ms)` raises `ValueError` for invalid motor number or non-positive ms ‚Äî this file does **not** catch that exception (unlike the embedded CLI in `glove_controller.py`'s `motor_test_cli`, which also doesn't catch it for `vibrate` calls either, only for `thresh`), so a bad `int(parts[1])` parse (e.g., non-numeric ms) would raise an uncaught `ValueError` and crash the script.

### 6.6 Relationship to Rest of Codebase
This file is nearly a duplicate of the embedded `motor_test_cli`/`_on_frame` functions inside `glove_controller.py` itself (Section 5.2), differing only in that the embedded version additionally supports `cal`, blank-enter confirm, `thresh`, and `status` commands, while `motor_test.py` supports only motor firing. It is not imported by, nor does it import, `hub.py`, confirming its role as an isolated bench-test tool.

‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
## 7. probe_devices.sh ‚Äî Hardware/Device Discovery Script
‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

### 7.1 Purpose & Role
A Bash diagnostic script meant to be run directly on the OrangePi (`bash probe_devices.sh 2>&1 | tee probe_out.txt`) to enumerate all audio and video hardware so the correct device paths/indices can be hard-coded or passed as CLI flags to `hub.py` and `orangepi_client.py`. It performs no Python-hub integration itself ‚Äî it is a manual, human-in-the-loop bring-up tool whose output is meant to be pasted back for a developer/AI to read.

### 7.2 Control-Flow Walkthrough
Sequential sections, each guarded to degrade gracefully if a tool is missing:
1. `cat /proc/asound/cards` ‚Äî lists ALSA sound cards (falls back to "(not available)").
2. `aplay -l` ‚Äî lists ALSA playback devices.
3. `arecord -l` ‚Äî lists ALSA capture (microphone) devices.
4. `aplay -L | grep -E "^(plughw|hw:|default|sysdefault)"` ‚Äî verbose device-name listing filtered to relevant prefixes.
5. An embedded Python heredoc (`python3 - << 'PYEOF' ... PYEOF`) that imports `sounddevice as sd`, calls `sd.query_devices()`, and prints each device's index, name, input/output channel counts, plus the default input/output device names ‚Äî this is the same `sounddevice` API used by `hub.py`/`orangepi_client.py` for mic detection, so this script directly validates what those Python files will see.
6. `v4l2-ctl --list-devices` ‚Äî lists video capture hardware (falls back to an apt-install hint if `v4l2-ctl` is missing).
7. A loop over `/dev/video*` nodes (sorted with `-V` natural/version sort) calling `v4l2-ctl --device "$node" --info` and grep-filtering to Card type/Driver name/Bus info lines, printed per node.
8. A hard-coded speaker test looping over `plughw:3,0` and `plughw:4,0`: generates a raw 1-second 440 Hz sine wave via an inline Python `struct.pack` one-liner (no numpy dependency here) piped directly into `aplay -D "$dev" -f S16_LE -r 44100 -c 1 -q`, reporting OK/FAILED per device.
9. A hard-coded mic test: another Python heredoc records 3 seconds from `sounddevice` device index 2 at 16 kHz via `sd.rec(...)`/`sd.wait()`, computes RMS and peak with `numpy`, and warns if RMS is below `0.0001` (likely muted/wrong device) ‚Äî note the hard-coded `MIC_INDEX = 2` and the hard-coded `plughw:3,0`/`plughw:4,0` speaker indices are almost certainly leftover values specific to whatever hardware configuration the script's author last tested on, meaning a future user must edit these constants for their own board's device enumeration before this section is meaningful.
10. Final "DONE" banner.

### 7.3 External Tools/Libraries Invoked
Shell utilities: `cat`, `aplay`, `arecord`, `grep`, `v4l2-ctl`, `ls`, `sed`. Python (invoked as a subprocess via heredocs, not a Python import in the file itself): `sounddevice` and `numpy`, matching exactly the libraries `hub.py`/`orangepi_client.py` depend on for audio.

### 7.4 Scenarios
- **All tools present**: full report printed section by section.
- **Missing tool** (`aplay`, `arecord`, `v4l2-ctl` not installed): each section's `||` fallback prints a "(not available)"/"(not found)" placeholder rather than aborting the whole script ‚Äî the script has no `set -e`, so it always runs to completion regardless of individual command failures.
- **No devices connected**: `sounddevice`/`v4l2-ctl` sections print empty or minimal listings; the hard-coded speaker/mic test sections will simply report FAILED / very low RMS with a warning.
- **Wrong hard-coded indices** (very likely on a fresh board): the speaker test (`plughw:3,0`/`plughw:4,0`) and mic test (`MIC_INDEX = 2`) sections may test the wrong or nonexistent device ‚Äî this is a known limitation requiring manual edits per deployment.

### 7.5 Relationship to Rest of Codebase
Purely a standalone diagnostic; not imported/executed by any Python file. Its output directly informs the `--uart`, `--alsa`, `--mic`/`--cam` style CLI overrides accepted by `hub.py` and `orangepi_client.py`, and validates the same auto-detection logic (`sounddevice.query_devices`, `v4l2-ctl`) that `orangepi_client.py`'s `detect_mic()`/`detect_speaker()`/`detect_camera()` and `hub.py`'s `_probe_devices()` perform programmatically at runtime.

‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê
## 8. requirements_orangepi.txt ‚Äî Dependency Manifest
‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê‚ïê

### 8.1 Purpose
Pins the Python package set for the OrangePi Zero 2W deployment, with extensive inline comments documenting *why* each package is needed and which file(s) consume it ‚Äî effectively a dependency-to-file cross-reference embedded as comments. It also documents required system (`apt`) packages installed once as a prerequisite: `espeak-ng`, `alsa-utils`, `portaudio19-dev`, `libsndfile1`, `python3-pip`, `python3-dev`, `build-essential`, `python3-opencv`.

### 8.2 Declared Packages and File Mapping
- `pyserial==3.5` ‚Äî UART driver for `glove_controller.py` (and, per its own comment, also `lidar_adapter.py`, a LiDAR feature module outside this section's scope but sharing the same serial dependency).
- `faster-whisper==1.1.1` ‚Äî CTranslate2 int8 Whisper backend, used by `orangepi_client.py`'s `load_models()`/`transcribe()` (and presumably `gesture_hub/voice.py`, out of scope).
- `webrtcvad==2.0.10` ‚Äî frame-level VAD, used by `orangepi_client.py`'s `record_with_vad()`.
- `sounddevice==0.5.1` ‚Äî mic capture and earcon playback, used by `orangepi_client.py` and referenced by `probe_devices.sh`'s embedded Python.
- `SpeechRecognition>=3.10` plus `PyAudio` ‚Äî explicitly commented as used by `gesture_hub/voice.py`'s `VoiceListener` (the voice-command listener wired into `hub.py`'s `sm.on_voice`/`_voice_abort` callbacks) ‚Äî this is a **different** speech pipeline from the Whisper-based one in `orangepi_client.py`, confirming `hub.py`'s voice-command recognition (short command words) and `orangepi_client.py`'s full STT (free-form sentences) are architecturally separate speech stacks in this codebase.
- `numpy>=1.24,<3.0` ‚Äî required transitively by faster-whisper, OpenCV keyframe work, and audio math (used directly in `orangepi_client.py`'s `_tone_wav`, `_to_pcm`, `_normalize_audio`, camera sharpness scoring).
- `requests` ‚Äî explicitly commented as used by `ServerLink` (`net/client.py`) "for the money / OCR server connection" ‚Äî notably, this comment appears **inaccurate/stale** relative to the actual `net/client.py` source read in this review, which uses only raw `socket`/`struct`/`json`/`base64` and never imports `requests`; this is either vestigial documentation from an earlier HTTP-based transport or refers to usage inside `features/money_recognition.py`/`features/ocr_reader.py` (out of this section's scope) rather than `net/client.py` itself.
- `google-genai>=1.0.0` ‚Äî Gemini vision API client for `features/env_awareness.py` (out of scope, referenced for completeness).
- `scipy>=1.11` ‚Äî used by LiDAR feature modules (`lidar_adapter.py`'s `medfilt`, `slam_engine.py`'s `least_squares`/`KDTree`) ‚Äî out of scope but flagged with a strong ARM-board build warning (must use piwheels prebuilt wheels, not source builds, to avoid OOM on a 512 MB board).
- Optional/commented-out: `cupy-cuda12x` (GPU acceleration, inapplicable to this board), `noisereduce` (optional denoise for `orangepi_client.py`'s `_denoise()`), and a commented `opencv-python-headless` pip fallback (apt's `python3-opencv` is strongly preferred to avoid source-build OOM).

### 8.3 Scenarios
- **Fresh board setup**: apt packages installed first, then `pip3 install --break-system-packages -r requirements_orangepi.txt` ‚Äî the `--break-system-packages` flag is called out because Debian/Armbian-based OrangePi images use PEP 668 externally-managed Python environments.
- **Missing `noisereduce`**: gracefully degrades ‚Äî `orangepi_client.py` wraps the import in `try/except`, sets `_NR_AVAILABLE = False`, and `_denoise()` becomes a no-op; no crash.
- **PyAudio build failure**: the file explicitly warns to use a piwheels prebuilt wheel rather than building from source (requires PortAudio headers), which would otherwise fail without `portaudio19-dev`.
- **scipy build failure**: same piwheels warning ‚Äî building from source on a 512 MB board risks OOM or 30+ minute builds.

### 8.4 Relationship to Rest of Codebase
This is a pure documentation/dependency-declaration artifact ‚Äî it has no executable behavior of its own ‚Äî but it is the authoritative index of every third-party library referenced across `hub.py`, `orangepi_client.py`, `glove_controller.py`, `net/client.py`, and the `features`/`gesture_hub` packages, and its inline comments are a valuable (if occasionally slightly stale, per the `requests`/`ServerLink` note above) cross-reference for understanding which file owns which dependency.

================================================================================
SECTION 2 ‚Äî GESTURE HUB SUBSYSTEM
================================================================================

# Gesture Hub Subsystem ‚Äî Detailed Engineering Documentation

## 0. Package Overview

`gesture_hub/` is the OrangePi-side subsystem that turns a 10 Hz stream of `SensorFrame` objects (bit-packed flex/IMU state from an ATmega glove controller) into named, discrete gesture events, and drives a stateful control loop (`HubStateMachine`) that maps those events onto feature activation, gesture (re-)recording, voice interaction, and audio/haptic feedback. The package has no `__init__.py` content beyond a docstring (`"""net package ‚Äî framed JSON link from the OrangePi hub to the server."""` ‚Äî note: this docstring text is actually mismatched/inherited, since `gesture_hub/__init__.py` contains it but the description belongs to a networking package; the file otherwise exports nothing and performs no imports). The package is consumed by a top-level `hub.py` (not read in this pass) and by `features/*` modules (referenced via `features.base.FeatureContext` and `features.programmable.ProgrammableGestures`).

---

## 1. specs.py ‚Äî Gesture Definitions & Bit-Mask Vocabulary

**Purpose.** Defines the canonical vocabulary of hardware bit positions and the `GestureSpec` dataclass that every other module (engine, recorder, store, state machine) speaks in. It is the single source of truth for the 6 hardcoded "system gestures."

**Key constants.**
- `FINGER_NAMES = ["Thumb","Index","Middle","Ring","Pinky"]`, and `FINGER_INDEX` (lowercase name ‚Üí bit index 0-4).
- `IMU_BIT_NAMES` ‚Äî 6 semantic flags: `tilt_right`(0), `tilt_left`(1), `tilt_forward`(2), `tilt_backward`(3), `rotate_cw`(4), `rotate_ccw`(5), plus `IMU_BIT_INDEX` reverse map.
- `Motion(str, Enum)` ‚Äî `STATIC = "static"`, `FLICK = "flick"`.

**`GestureSpec` dataclass** ‚Äî fields: `name:str`, `flex_mask:int`, `imu_mask:int`, `motion:Motion`, `hold_frames:int=3`, `flex_exact:bool=False`. Methods:
- `finger_names()` / `imu_names()` ‚Äî decode bitmasks to human-readable lists.
- `describe()` ‚Äî builds spoken-friendly text used pervasively by `feedback.speak()` (e.g. "Thumb + Pinky [exact], hold tilt_right").
- `to_dict()` / `from_dict()` ‚Äî JSON (de)serialization; `from_dict` defensively coerces ints and defaults missing keys (`hold_frames=3`, `flex_exact=False`) for forward-compatibility with older JSON files.

**`DEFAULT_GESTURES`** ‚Äî a `dict[str, GestureSpec]` hardcoding 6 system gestures, all with `flex_exact=True` so that a full fist or superset of bent fingers never spuriously fires them:
- `START`: flex 0x11 (Thumb+Pinky), imu 0x01 (tilt_right), STATIC, hold=3.
- `NEXT`: flex 0x10 (Pinky), imu 0x01, FLICK, hold=2.
- `EDIT`: flex 0x05 (Thumb+Middle), imu 0x00 (any), STATIC, hold=3.
- `OCR_PAUSE`: flex 0x19 (Thumb+Ring+Pinky), imu 0x08 (tilt_backward), STATIC, hold=3.
- `OCR_FWD`: flex 0x01 (Thumb), imu 0x01 (tilt_right), FLICK, hold=2.
- `OCR_BWD`: flex 0x01 (Thumb), imu 0x02 (tilt_left), FLICK, hold=2.

No third-party imports; uses only `dataclasses` and `enum` from the standard library.

---

## 2. engine.py ‚Äî Frame-to-Event Recognition (`GestureEngine`)

**Purpose.** The real-time classifier: converts each incoming `SensorFrame` into zero-or-more fired gesture names by comparing `frame.flex_bits`/`frame.imu_bits` against every `GestureSpec` in its table, every frame, at 10 Hz.

**Pipeline walkthrough (per frame, per gesture spec in `self.gestures`):**
1. **Cooldown check** ‚Äî if a per-gesture refractory counter (`self._cooldown[name]`) is >0, decrement it, reset the static-hold counter, and `continue` (skip further evaluation for that gesture this frame). Cooldown length = `refractory_frames = max(1, int(0.7 * fps))` (‚âà7 frames at 10 Hz ‚âà0.7 s), set on every fire ‚Äî this is the anti-burst mechanism.
2. **Pose check** ‚Äî `flex_exact=True` ‚Üí exact equality `flex == spec.flex_mask`; else subset check `(flex & spec.flex_mask) == spec.flex_mask` (extra bent fingers tolerated).
3. **Motion evaluation**, branching on `spec.motion`:
   - `STATIC`: `imu_ok` is true if `imu_mask==0` (don't care) or the IMU bits are a superset of `imu_mask`. If `pose_ok and imu_ok`, increment `self._static_count[name]`; fire when the count reaches `spec.hold_frames`. Any failure resets the counter to 0.
   - `FLICK`: computes `rising = (prev_imu_bits & imu_mask)==0 AND (current imu superset check)` ‚Äî i.e., the IMU condition must transition from fully-clear to fully-set within one frame while the pose is already held. Fires immediately on that transition (no multi-frame hold, though `hold_frames` is stored on the spec, it's unused in the FLICK branch of `feed()`).
4. **On fire**: reset static counter, arm the cooldown, and invoke `self.on_event(name)` inside a `try/except` so a crashing callback cannot break frame processing (logs `[ENGINE] event handler error: {e}`).
5. `self._prev_imu_bits = imu` is updated once per frame after all gestures are evaluated (shared across all specs ‚Äî this is why FLICK detection is edge-triggered globally rather than per-spec history).

**Key methods:** `__init__(gestures, on_event=None, fps=10)`; `set_gestures(gestures)` ‚Äî hot-swaps the spec table and calls `_reset_counters()` (used after saving a newly recorded gesture, so the engine immediately recognizes it); `feed(frame)` ‚Äî the main entry point called once per received frame; `_reset_counters()` ‚Äî reinitializes `_static_count`, `_cooldown` dicts and `_prev_imu_bits`.

**No external libraries** ‚Äî pure stdlib-free logic, importing only `gesture_hub.specs`.

---

## 3. state_machine.py ‚Äî `HubStateMachine`, the Control FSM (647 lines... actually shown ~648)

**Purpose.** The central orchestrator. Owns the top-level state, routes frames either to the recorder or the engine, serializes gesture events through a queue processed on the main thread, and drives all user-facing announcements via `feedback.speak()`.

**States (`State(Enum)`, via `auto()`):**
- `INACTIVE` ‚Äî glove considered off; only `START` is acted upon (everything else silently dropped by `dispatch()`).
- `ENROLL` ‚Äî first-boot/ongoing walk through features lacking an assigned gesture; `NEXT` skips to the next unassigned feature, `EDIT` triggers two-sample recording for the current one.
- `ACTIVE` ‚Äî idle-armed; listening for a feature's assigned gesture (`FEAT:<title>`) to launch it.
- `RUNNING` ‚Äî one feature is executing (blocking call to `feat.run(...)`); the same gesture that opened it closes it; all *other* gestures are forwarded to the feature via `self._feature_gesture_q`.
- `PROGRAMMABLE` ‚Äî a special "gesture management panel" feature (`ProgrammableGestures`) is open, allowing cursor-based browsing/re-recording of any feature's gesture.

**Threading model.** Frames arrive on an RX thread and call `on_frame(frame)`, which routes to `recorder.feed()` if `self.recording` is True, else `engine.feed()`.
