The engine's `on_event` callback presumably is bound to `dispatch(name)` (wired in `hub.py`, not shown) which also runs on the RX thread. `dispatch()` pushes gesture names onto `self._queue` (a `queue.Queue`), decoupling recognition (RX thread) from state transition and blocking side-effects (main thread running `run()`). `dispatch()` has three special cases:
  - `START` is subject to a 2 s lockout (`START_LOCKOUT_S`) measured against `_last_start_ts` to debounce accidental re-triggers.
  - In `RUNNING`, if the fired gesture equals the currently active feature's key, it sets `self._abort` (a `threading.Event`) to signal the feature to stop; otherwise it's forwarded into `_feature_gesture_q` for the feature to consume internally (e.g., OCR_PAUSE/FWD/BWD inside a Book Reader feature).
  - Everything else is enqueued for `_handle()`.

**Main loop `run()`**: announces "Ready. `<START description>` to activate." via `feedback.speak()`, then loops `queue.get(timeout=0.2)` until `_shutdown` Event is set, dispatching each name to `_handle()`. `stop()` sets `_shutdown` and aborts any running feature.

**`_handle(name)`** dispatches `START` to `_activate()`/`_deactivate()` (toggle), else routes by current state to `_handle_enroll`, `_handle_active`, or `_handle_programmable`.

**Activate/Deactivate:**
- `_activate()`: pulses haptic `confirm()`, checks `registry.unassigned(store)`. If any features lack gestures ‚Üí state=`ENROLL`, speaks the list, calls `registry.start_enrollment(store)` and `_announce_enroll(feat)`. Else ‚Üí state=`ACTIVE`, speaks a full per-feature gesture summary plus voice-query instructions.
- `_deactivate()`: aborts any running feature, resets to `INACTIVE`, drains the queue, plays an `error()` haptic buzz (used generically as an "off" cue), and speaks a context-appropriate closing message.

**Enrollment (`_handle_enroll`)**: `NEXT` ‚Üí `registry.next_enrollment(store)`, either advances to ACTIVE (all done) or re-announces; `EDIT` ‚Üí `_record_feature_gesture(feat)` then drains queue (to swallow accidental bounce events during the ~10+ second recording window); a name matching an *already-assigned* feature's key launches that feature immediately (mid-enrollment activation), then resumes enrollment if features remain unassigned.

**Active (`_handle_active`)**: ignores OCR-only and NEXT/EDIT gestures (meaningless while idle, via `_FEATURE_ONLY_GESTURES` frozenset), otherwise matches the fired name against every `registry.gesture_key(feat)` and calls `_launch_feature`.

**Programmable (`_handle_programmable`)**: closing gesture (same key that opened it) exits to ACTIVE; `NEXT` advances `registry.advance()` and announces the newly-selected feature; `EDIT` re-records the current feature's gesture via `_record_prog_gesture`. All other gestures are silently ignored.

**`_launch_feature(feat, key)`**: lazy-imports `features.programmable.ProgrammableGestures` to avoid circular imports; if `feat` is that special sentinel type, transitions to `PROGRAMMABLE` and announces the panel. Otherwise it plays a `select()` haptic, speaks an "Opening X" message, creates a fresh `threading.Event` abort flag and a fresh `_feature_gesture_q`, sets state=`RUNNING`, and **blocks the main thread** calling `feat.run(FeatureContext(link, abort, feedback, gesture_queue))`. On exception, marks `crashed=True`, plays `error()`, announces the crash. In `finally`, restores state to `ACTIVE` unless the user already deactivated mid-run (`deactivated` flag derived from `self.state != State.RUNNING`), clears the abort/active-feature/queue references, drains the pending gesture queue, and announces "closed" if not deactivated/crashed.

**Record-by-example flow (two-sample confirmation).** Two variants:
- `_record_enroll_gesture`: speaks instructions, calls `feedback.wait(timeout=12)` (blocks until TTS finishes), sleeps 5 s to let the user prepare, calls `_capture_sample()` (sample1). If `None` ‚Üí error/retry. Otherwise builds a `preview` `GestureSpec` via `recorder.build_spec("preview", sample1)`, speaks its description, waits again, captures `sample2`. **Only if `sample1 == sample2` exactly** (tuple equality of `(flex_mask, imu_mask, motion)`) does it accept: builds the real spec under key `FEAT:<title>`, calls `store.set(key, spec)`, `store.save()`, `engine.set_gestures(store.gestures)` (hot-reload), plays a `select()` haptic, speaks confirmation, and calls `_advance_enroll()`.
- `_record_prog_gesture`: same capture-and-preview mechanics but allows a richer confirmation step via `_wait_prog_confirm(sample1)`, which polls a dedicated `_prog_confirm_q` queue (fed by voice commands `PROG_CONFIRM`/`PROG_DISCARD` arriving via `on_voice()`) for up to 30 s, *while simultaneously* accepting a "do the gesture twice" fallback path (captures `s2`, must equal `sample1`; if so, prompts "one more," captures `s3`, must also equal `sample1`) ‚Äî either channel (voice or repeated-gesture) can confirm or the loop times out after 30 s. On confirm: same store/engine hot-reload sequence, then auto-advances `registry.advance()` and announces the next feature in the Programmable panel.

**`_capture_sample()`**: resets the recorder, calls `feedback.silence()` (kill any TTS so only the haptic is heard), `feedback.beep()` ("go" cue), sleeps 0.4 s, sets `self.recording = True` for `record_window_s` (default 2.5 s) during which `on_frame()` routes raw frames to `recorder.feed()` instead of the engine, then sets `recording=False` and returns `recorder.analyze()`.

**Voice integration (`on_voice(cmd)`)** ‚Äî called from the `VoiceListener` background thread. `QUERY:<text>` commands are answered synchronously via `_handle_query()` (word-overlap scoring between spoken text and each `feature.title`, speaking either the matched feature's gesture description or a fallback list of feature names). `PROG_CONFIRM`/`PROG_DISCARD` are routed to `_prog_confirm_q` only while `_prog_confirm_mode` is true; otherwise (and for all other recognized voice commands like `NEXT`, `EDIT`, `START`) they're funneled through the same `dispatch()` path as glove-originated gestures ‚Äî meaning voice and gesture inputs are fully interchangeable at the state-machine boundary.

**External imports**: `queue`, `re`, `threading`, `time`, `enum` (stdlib only), plus the project-local `features.base.FeatureContext`.

---

## 4. registry.py ‚Äî `FeatureRegistry`

**Purpose.** Holds the ordered, static list of feature objects (money detector, book reader/OCR, programmable panel, etc. ‚Äî defined elsewhere in `features/`) and manages two independent cursors: one for first-run/ongoing enrollment of gesture-less features, one for browsing in the Programmable panel. It explicitly does **not** store gesture assignments ‚Äî those live in `GestureStore` keyed by `"FEAT:<title>"` (via the static method `gesture_key(feature)`), so gesture assignments survive independently of feature-list changes.

**Key methods:**
- `__init__(features: list)` ‚Äî raises `ValueError` if empty.
- `features` (property) ‚Äî stable-order list.
- `unassigned(store)` ‚Äî list comprehension filtering features whose `gesture_key` is absent from `store.gestures`.
- `start_enrollment(store)` / `next_enrollment(store)` ‚Äî manage `_enroll_feat`, `_enroll_list`, `_enroll_idx`; `next_enrollment` re-queries `unassigned()` each call (so a feature enrolled out-of-band is dropped from the walk) and wraps cyclically via modulo so the user can revisit skipped items rather than enrollment silently terminating.
- `current` / `advance()` ‚Äî a separate `_cursor` for the Programmable panel, independent of the enrollment cursor, wrapping via modulo over `self._features`.

No third-party imports.

---

## 5. cal_store.py ‚Äî `CalStore` (ATmega Finger Calibration Persistence)

**Purpose.** Persists raw per-finger analog calibration (`REST`/`BENT` ADC values from the ATmega, one pair per of the 5 fingers) to `calibration.json`, separate from `gestures.json`, and replays it to the firmware on boot so a fresh power-cycle doesn't require re-calibration.

**Schema** (`calibration.json`): `{"rest": [int√ó5], "bent": [int√ó5], "thresh_pct": int, "fingers": ["Thumb",...,"Pinky"]}`.

**Key methods:**
- `save(rest, bent, thresh_pct=35)` ‚Äî stores in-memory copies and writes JSON with `indent=2`; catches `OSError` and prints rather than raising.
- `restore(controller) -> bool` ‚Äî if calibration was loaded, builds a firmware command string `"setcal r0 b0 r1 b1 r2 b2 r3 b3 r4 b4"` by interleaving `rest`/`bent`, sends it via `controller.send(cmd)`, then calls `controller.set_threshold(thresh_pct)` to force firmware recomputation of the `THRESH[]` array from the restored values. Returns `False` if no calibration is on file.
- `has_calibration()` ‚Äî simple presence check.
- `_load()` ‚Äî silently no-ops if the file doesn't exist; wraps `json.load` in try/except so a corrupt file degrades to "no calibration" rather than crashing the hub.

The module's docstring also documents the exact Arduino-side `.ino` snippet needed to implement the `setcal` serial command, which is useful cross-reference for firmware maintainers even though it's not executable Python.

Only stdlib imports (`json`, `os`).

---

## 6. recorder.py ‚Äî `GestureRecorder` (Record-by-Example Analysis)

**Purpose.** During a capture window (driven by the state machine's `_capture_sample()`), accumulates raw `(flex_bits, imu_bits)` tuples per frame and statistically distills them into a `GestureSpec`-compatible triple.

**`feed(frame)`**: tracks bit-transition state ‚Äî `_risen_imu` accumulates (via bitwise OR) every IMU bit that transitioned 0‚Üí1 at any point in the window (`(~prev_imu & imu) & 0xFF`), and appends the raw `(flex, imu)` pair to `_frames`.

**`analyze() -> tuple | None`**:
1. Filters to `posed` frames where `flex != 0` (some finger bent); returns `None` if none.
2. `flex_mask` = the most frequent exact `flex_bits` value among posed frames (`Counter.most_common(1)`).
3. Restricts to `pose_frames` ‚Äî frames whose flex is a superset of `flex_mask` (falls back to all posed frames if none match exactly, guarding against a degenerate empty set).
4. Counts per-bit IMU occurrence across pose frames; `pose_imu_bits` includes any bit present in **>50%** of pose frames.
5. `risen_filtered = risen_during_pose & pose_imu_bits` ‚Äî a bit only counts as "risen" if it also independently qualifies as a majority-held bit during the pose.
6. Classification: if `risen_filtered` is non-zero ‚Üí `(flex_mask, risen_filtered, Motion.FLICK)`; elif `pose_imu_bits` non-zero ‚Üí `(flex_mask, pose_imu_bits, Motion.STATIC)`; else ‚Üí `(flex_mask, 0, Motion.STATIC)` (pose-only, IMU don't-care).

**`build_spec(name, sample)`** (`@staticmethod`) ‚Äî unpacks the analyzed triple into a `GestureSpec`, with `hold_frames` heuristically set to 2 for FLICK, 3 for STATIC. Note this always constructs with `flex_exact` defaulting to `False` ‚Äî user-recorded gestures are therefore **subset**-matched, unlike the exact-matched system gestures, meaning recorded gestures tolerate extra incidentally-bent fingers.

Imports only `collections.Counter` and `gesture_hub.specs`.

---

## 7. feedback.py ‚Äî `Feedback` (Audio/Haptic Output Layer)

**Purpose.** All non-visual UX for a blind/low-vision user: TTS speech via `espeak-ng` + `aplay`, and vibration-motor haptic patterns via the glove `controller`. Designed so speech is always interruptible and gestures are never delayed by ongoing audio ("gesture priority").

**External tools invoked as subprocesses (not Python libraries):** `amixer` (ALSA mixer control, unmute/volume), `aplay -l` / `aplay -D <dev>` (playback + device enumeration), `espeak-ng` (offline TTS synthesis to WAV).

**Third-party/stdlib Python imports**: `array` (build a raw PCM test tone sample buffer), `math` (sine wave synthesis for a 440 Hz test tone), `os`, `re` (regex-parsing `aplay -l` output and `amixer scontents` control names), `subprocess` (all external process invocation), `tempfile` (WAV scratch files), `threading` (daemon monitor threads for async audio playback and locking), `time`, `wave` (WAV file read/write, both for the synthesized test tone and for `play_raw`'s duration probing).

**Startup device selection (`_auto_alsa()`)**: parses `aplay -l` via regex `card\s+(\d+):\s*(\S+)[^,]*,\s*device\s+(\d+)`, unmutes every discovered card via `_unmute_all(card)` (which brute-force `amixer sset`s a hardcoded list of common control names, then additionally regex-scrapes `amixer scontents` for every control the card actually exposes and unmutes/90%'s all of them), then builds a synthetic 0.5 s 440 Hz test WAV and probes devices in priority order: all non-HDMI devices in **reverse** card-number order (so a later-enumerated USB/Bluetooth headset wins over the onboard codec, card 0), then HDMI devices last. The first device that successfully plays the test WAV (`_test_device`) is selected; the test WAV is deleted afterward regardless of outcome.

**`Feedback.__init__(controller, alsa=None, speed=150)`**: auto-detects the ALSA device unless overridden, probes for `espeak-ng --version` (prints found/not-found ‚Äî non-fatal), and initializes `_audio_proc`/`_audio_tmp`/`_audio_lock` for cross-thread audio-process bookkeeping.

**Haptics** ‚Äî thin wrappers around `controller.vibrate(motor, ms)`, each wrapped in try/except so a controller failure never propagates: `confirm()` (motor 1, 120ms), `tick()` (motor 2, 60ms), `select()` (motor 1, double-pulse 90ms/90ms with 120ms gap), `error()` (motor 3, 400ms), `beep()` (motor 2, 150ms).

**Speech (`speak(text)`)**: prints to console, calls `_stop_audio()` to kill any in-flight playback (gesture priority), synthesizes synchronously via `espeak-ng -s <speed> -w <tmpfile> <text>` (typically <1s), then launches `aplay` asynchronously via `subprocess.Popen` (immediately registers the Popen under the lock so `_stop_audio()` can kill it from another thread at any moment), and spawns a daemon monitor thread that waits on the process, classifies "normal kill" (`returncode in (0,-15,-9)` or "Interrupted system call" in stderr) versus real errors, retries once with a larger `--buffer-size` on unexpected non-xrun errors, and always deletes the temp WAV in `finally`. `play_raw(wav_bytes)` is the analogous method for server-generated audio (used for TTS/audio pushed from the Python feature server), computing playback duration from WAV header metadata (falling back to a byte-count heuristic on parse failure) and returning that duration to the caller. `silence()` exposes `_stop_audio()` publicly for callers needing pre-recording silence. `is_speaking()` checks `_audio_proc.poll() is None` under the lock. `wait(timeout=12.0)` blocks the calling thread (sleeping 0.15s first to let `aplay` actually start) polling `is_speaking()` every 50ms until it stops or timeout ‚Äî used by the state machine before haptic "go" cues so instructions are always fully heard.

---

## 8. voice.py ‚Äî `VoiceListener` (Speech-to-Command Bridge)

**Purpose.** A background daemon thread that continuously listens on the microphone and translates recognized short phrases into the same gesture-name vocabulary (`NEXT`, `EDIT`, `START`, `OCR_SCAN`, `OCR_CLOSE`, `PROG_CONFIRM`, `PROG_DISCARD`) or a `QUERY:<text>` passthrough, delivered via an injected `on_command` callback (wired to `HubStateMachine.on_voice` in `hub.py`).

**Third-party import**: `speech_recognition` (the `SpeechRecognition` PyPI package), imported defensively inside `try/except ImportError` setting `_SR_OK = False` on failure ‚Äî the module degrades gracefully (prints install instructions, `start()` becomes a no-op) rather than crashing the hub if voice isn't installed. Internally, `speech_recognition` depends on PyAudio/portaudio for microphone capture and calls Google's free web speech API (`recognizer.recognize_google`) for STT (requires network connectivity ‚Äî a possible failure point noted below).

**`_COMMAND_MAP`** ‚Äî dict of trigger words ‚Üí command strings, including intentional synonyms (`next/skip/forward`‚ÜíNEXT, `edit/change/modify`‚ÜíEDIT, `start/stop`‚ÜíSTART toggle, `scan/capture/take`‚ÜíOCR_SCAN, `close`‚ÜíOCR_CLOSE, `confirm/yes/save`‚ÜíPROG_CONFIRM, `discard/cancel/no`‚ÜíPROG_DISCARD). `_QUERY_TRIGGERS = {"gesture","move","how","what"}` ‚Äî checked first, so "what is the gesture for money" is routed as a query even though it also contains no command words.

**`start()`**: spawns `self._thread` running `_run()` as a named daemon thread ("VoiceListener"). **`_run()`**: configures a `sr.Recognizer()` with `energy_threshold` (default 3000, configurable), `dynamic_energy_threshold=True`, `pause_threshold=0.6`; opens `sr.Microphone()` (catches `OSError` if no mic device); performs 1.5s ambient noise calibration (`adjust_for_ambient_noise`); then loops `r.listen(source, timeout=5, phrase_time_limit=7)` until `_stop` is set, catching `WaitTimeoutError` (silently continues ‚Äî this is the normal "no speech" case) and swallowing all other exceptions to keep the thread alive indefinitely. **`_recognise()`** calls `recognize_google`, silently returns on `UnknownValueError` (unintelligible audio ‚Äî expected/frequent), prints other errors (e.g., network failure hitting Google's API), and forwards recognized lowercase text to `_dispatch()`. **`_dispatch()`** tokenizes into a word-set via regex `[a-z]+`, checks query triggers first, else does a **first-match-wins** scan over `_COMMAND_MAP.items()` (dict insertion order in Python 3.7+, so `next` is checked before `edit`, etc.) and fires the first word found in the utterance.

---

## 9. store.py ‚Äî `GestureStore` (Gesture Persistence)

**Purpose.** Owns the in-memory `dict[str, GestureSpec]` (`self.gestures`) that both the engine and state machine treat as ground truth, and its JSON persistence to `gestures.json`.

**Load behavior (`load()`)** ‚Äî critical resilience logic:
- If the file doesn't exist, calls `_write_defaults()` (writes `DEFAULT_GESTURES` verbatim) and keeps the in-memory defaults.
- If it exists, parses each entry via `GestureSpec.from_dict`. Then **merges**: starts from a fresh copy of `DEFAULT_GESTURES` and overlays only *non-system* keys (`FEAT:*` and any custom names) from the loaded file ‚Äî meaning system gesture definitions (`START`/`NEXT`/`EDIT`/`OCR_*`) are always taken from the current code's `specs.py`, never from a stale JSON file. This is explicitly to prevent renamed/retired system gestures (the docstring cites a hypothetical `BACK ‚Üí OCR_BWD` rename) from persisting incorrectly across code upgrades. If the loaded file lacked any current system-gesture keys, it immediately calls `save()` to rewrite the file with the new complete set. Any exception during load (corrupt JSON, missing keys, etc.) is caught and logged, falling back to the defaults already in memory ‚Äî the hub can never be locked out by a bad `gestures.json`.

**`save()`** ‚Äî serializes every spec via `to_dict()` plus an extra `_desc` field (`spec.describe()`, human-readable, explicitly ignored on reload ‚Äî for the convenience of anyone reading the raw JSON file) and writes with `indent=2`; catches `OSError`.

**`set(name, spec)`** ‚Äî simple in-memory dict assignment (no auto-save; callers must call `save()` themselves, as `state_machine.py` does immediately after every `set()`).

---

## 10. gestures.json ‚Äî On-Disk Schema

A flat JSON object keyed by gesture name (system names or `FEAT:<feature title>`), each value an object with fields: `name` (string, redundant with the key), `flex_mask` (int, 0‚Äì31), `imu_mask` (int, 0‚Äì63), `motion` (`"static"`|`"flick"`), `hold_frames` (int), `flex_exact` (bool), and `_desc` (string, human-readable, write-only/advisory ‚Äî regenerated on every save, ignored by `from_dict` on load). The file shown contains only the 6 system gestures (no `FEAT:*` entries yet), meaning in this snapshot no application feature has had a gesture recorded/assigned.

---

## 11. Concrete Scenarios

**A. Successful recognition, end-to-end.** ATmega streams a frame with `flex_bits=0x11`, `imu_bits=0x01` held for 3+ consecutive frames while in `ACTIVE` state ‚Üí `GestureEngine.feed()` detects `START`'s STATIC hold-count reaching `hold_frames=3` ‚Üí fires `on_event("START")` ‚Üí this is wired (in `hub.py`) to `HubStateMachine.dispatch("START")` ‚Üí lockout check passes ‚Üí queued ‚Üí main loop's `_handle()` calls `_deactivate()` or `_activate()` depending on current state ‚Üí feedback speaks and haptic fires.

**B. Feature gesture recognized in ACTIVE state.** A `FEAT:Money Detector` gesture fires ‚Üí `dispatch()` puts it on the queue (state isn't RUNNING) ‚Üí `_handle_active()` matches `registry.gesture_key(feat)==name` ‚Üí `_launch_feature()` ‚Üí blocks main thread inside `feat.run(FeatureContext(...))` until the feature completes or the same gesture (forwarded straight to `_abort.set()` from `dispatch`, since state is now RUNNING) or a crash occurs.

**C. Ambiguous/unrecognized gesture.** In `ACTIVE`, a name not matching any feature key falls through to `print(f"[SM] Unrecognised gesture in ACTIVE: {name!r}")` ‚Äî silently logged, no user-facing feedback (a UX gap: a blind user gets no audio cue that their gesture wasn't understood in this state, unlike PROGRAMMABLE/ENROLL which explicitly re-announce).

**D. Calibration missing or stale.** `CalStore._load()` finds no `calibration.json` ‚Üí `has_calibration()` returns `False` ‚Üí `restore()` short-circuits printing `"[CAL] No saved calibration found ‚Äî skipping restore."`, returning `False` ‚Äî presumably `hub.py` then triggers `diagnostics.run_calibration()` to perform a fresh open/bent capture per finger via `controller.on_cal_event` callbacks (`START`/`OPEN`/`BENT`/`REST`/`BENT_VAL`/`DONE` events), then `CalStore.save()` persists it.

**E. Recording a brand-new gesture end-to-end.** User performs `EDIT` while `ENROLL`'d on an unassigned feature ‚Üí `_record_enroll_gesture` speaks instructions ‚Üí `feedback.wait()` blocks until TTS ends ‚Üí 5s prep delay ‚Üí `_capture_sample()` (silences audio, haptic beep, flips `self.recording=True` so `on_frame` routes to `recorder.feed()` for 2.5s) ‚Üí `recorder.analyze()` returns a `(flex_mask, imu_mask, motion)` triple or `None` ‚Üí previewed via `recorder.build_spec("preview", sample1)` and spoken back ‚Üí second capture must match exactly ‚Üí on match, `recorder.build_spec(key, sample1)` builds the real `GestureSpec`, `store.set()`+`store.save()` persist it to `gestures.json`, `engine.set_gestures(store.gestures)` hot-reloads the live matcher without restarting the process.

**F. Concurrent/threaded access.** Three threads touch shared state: the RX thread (`on_frame`/`dispatch`, mutating `engine`/`recorder` internals and pushing to `self._queue`), the main thread (`run()`/`_handle()` consuming the queue and mutating `self.state`), and the `VoiceListener` daemon thread (calling `on_voice()` which either pushes to `_prog_confirm_q` or calls `dispatch()`). Synchronization relies on `queue.Queue` (thread-safe) for gesture events and `_prog_confirm_q`, a `threading.Event` (`_abort`) for feature cancellation, and a `threading.Lock` (`_audio_lock` in `Feedback`) protecting the Popen handle. `self.state` and `self.recording` are plain attributes read/written across threads without an explicit lock ‚Äî correctness depends on Python's GIL and the fact that transitions are coarse and infrequent; a race exists in principle (e.g., `self.recording` toggled by the main thread while RX thread reads it in `on_frame`), but is benign given CPython's atomic bytecode-level attribute access.

**G. Voice feedback failure.** If `espeak-ng` binary is missing, `speak()` catches `FileNotFoundError`, prints an install hint, unlinks the temp file, and returns ‚Äî the gesture/state transition itself still completed; only the audio announcement is lost (silently, from the blind user's perspective ‚Äî a notable accessibility risk). If `aplay` fails to open the selected ALSA device mid-stream (xrun), the monitor thread retries once with a larger buffer before giving up.

**H. Diagnostics/error reporting.** `diagnostics.run_monitor()` provides a live CLI dashboard (5 Hz throttled) printing per-finger bent/open state, active IMU flags, and an OK/`..` match column per gesture ‚Äî a developer tool for tuning thresholds, not used in production flight. All modules follow a consistent `print(f"[TAG] ...")` convention (`[ENGINE]`, `[CAL]`, `[STORE]`, `[SM]`, `[AUDIO]`, `[VOICE]`, `[MONITOR]`, `[CAL]`) for greppable log output; there is no structured logging framework.

---

## 12. Cross-Module Exposure

`hub.py` (not read directly, but referenced throughout) is the composition root: it presumably instantiates `GestureStore`, `CalStore`, `FeatureRegistry(features)`, `GestureEngine`, `GestureRecorder`, `Feedback`, `VoiceListener`, and `HubStateMachine`, wiring `controller.on_frame = state_machine.on_frame`, `engine.on_event = state_machine.dispatch` (inferred), and `voice_listener = VoiceListener(on_command=state_machine.on_voice)`. `features/base.FeatureContext` is the object handed to every feature's `run()` method, bundling `link` (the JSON/TCP link to the Python feature server, per `gesture_hub/__init__.py`'s docstring reference to a "framed JSON link"), `abort` (Event), `feedback` (for in-feature haptic/speech), and `gesture_queue` (for receiving forwarded gestures like `OCR_PAUSE`/`OCR_FWD`/`OCR_BWD` while running). `features/programmable.ProgrammableGestures` is a sentinel feature type detected via `isinstance()` to switch into the `PROGRAMMABLE` state rather than the generic `RUNNING` state. The "event mechanism" connecting gesture recognition to the rest of the system is therefore a plain **callback chain**: ATmega bytes ‚Üí controller ‚Üí `SensorFrame` ‚Üí `engine.feed()` ‚Üí `on_event(name)` callback ‚Üí `state_machine.dispatch(name)` ‚Üí internal `queue.Queue` ‚Üí `_handle()` ‚Üí either internal state transition or `feat.run(FeatureContext)` ‚Äî i.e., a synchronous callback for recognition, backpressured through a thread-safe queue for the actual FSM/feature-launch side effects, with feature code communicating back out to the wider system (presumably the TCP feature server) via `FeatureContext.link`.

---

## DIAGRAM GENERATION PROMPT ‚Äî Gesture Hub Pipeline

Create a technical pipeline/state-machine diagram (Mermaid flowchart + state diagram combo, or an equivalent layered architecture illustration) showing: (1) a "Glove ATmega" box emitting raw byte frames at 10 Hz into a "SensorFrame (flex_bits, imu_bits)" node; (2) that frame splitting to two parallel consumers depending on a `recording` boolean flag ‚Äî `GestureRecorder.feed()` (into an "analyze() ‚Üí flex_mask/imu_mask/motion" box) versus `GestureEngine.feed()` (which checks each `GestureSpec` for pose-match, STATIC-hold-frames, or FLICK-rising-edge, using a per-gesture cooldown/refractory counter); (3) `GestureEngine` firing an `on_event(name)` callback into `HubStateMachine.dispatch()`, which pushes onto an internal `queue.Queue` consumed by the main-thread `run()`/`_handle()` loop; (4) a state diagram with five states ‚Äî INACTIVE, ENROLL, ACTIVE, RUNNING, PROGRAMMABLE ‚Äî with START toggling INACTIVE‚Üî(ENROLL or ACTIVE depending on unassigned features), ENROLL transitioning to ACTIVE once all `FeatureRegistry` features have a stored gesture, ACTIVE transitioning to RUNNING when a `FEAT:<title>` gesture matches, RUNNING returning to ACTIVE on the same gesture or feature completion, and ACTIVE/RUNNING transitioning to/from PROGRAMMABLE via a dedicated ProgrammableGestures feature; (5) side annotations showing `GestureStore` (backed by gestures.json) and `CalStore` (backed by calibration.json) as persistent data stores feeding `GestureSpec` objects into the engine, and a `Feedback` module (espeak-ng TTS + aplay + haptic motor pulses) and `VoiceListener` (speech_recognition, feeding the same dispatch/queue path as gestures) as peripheral I/O boxes connected bidirectionally to the state machine. Label arrows with the actual method names (`feed`, `dispatch`, `on_event`, `analyze`, `build_spec`, `store.set/save`, `engine.set_gestures`) and use a clean left-to-right data-flow layout with the five-state FSM as an inset panel.

================================================================================
SECTION 3 ‚Äî FEATURE CONTRACT + ENVIRONMENT AWARENESS & LIDAR NAVIGATION FEATURES
================================================================================

# Section: Feature Contract and the Environmental-Awareness / LiDAR-Navigation Features

## 1. features/base.py ‚Äî The Feature Contract

### 1.1 Purpose

`base.py` is an 29-line module that defines the minimal interface every OrangePi "feature" must satisfy so that `hub.py` (the top-level menu/state-machine, documented elsewhere) can launch, run, and tear down any feature uniformly, regardless of what the feature actually does (OCR, money recognition, environmental description, LiDAR SLAM, programmable gestures, etc.).

### 1.2 Structures

`FeatureContext` (a `@dataclass`) is the single object the hub constructs and hands to a feature's `run()` method. Its fields:

- `link` (typed loosely as `object`, actually a `net.client.ServerLink`) ‚Äî the one persistent TCP socket connection to the Python feature server, shared across all features so a fresh reconnect is not needed for every action.
- `abort` (a `threading.Event`) ‚Äî a cooperative cancellation flag. It is set by the hub when the user performs a global "panic"/abort gesture, and every feature's main loop is expected to poll `ctx.abort.is_set()` frequently and unwind cleanly (stopping worker threads, releasing hardware, flushing reports) when it fires.
- `feedback` (a `gesture_hub.feedback.Feedback` instance) ‚Äî the single audio/haptic output channel. Concretely used methods across these two files: `speak(text: str)` (TTS via local espeak-ng, no server round trip), `wait(timeout: float = 12.0)` (blocks/yields while TTS or a UI pause happens), `confirm()` (a short acknowledgement cue/vibration), and `_pulse(motor: int, ms: int)` (fires one of the three glove vibration motors for `ms` milliseconds).
- `gesture_queue` (`queue.Queue | None`, defaults to `None`) ‚Äî supplied only to features that need in-session gesture control (OCR reader, env awareness, LiDAR family). Per the docstring, the hub's own gesture state machine forwards every gesture name that is *not* the global START gesture and *not* a top-level menu toggle into this queue while the feature is in the RUNNING state; the feature is responsible for interpreting the tokens it cares about and ignoring the rest.

`Feature` is the base class:

- `name: str = "base"` ‚Äî the routing key used as the `feature` field of every message sent to the server via `ServerLink.send(feature, msg)`. This is what a server-side dispatcher uses to pick a handler module.
- `title: str = "Base feature"` ‚Äî the human-readable name spoken/shown in the hub's menu.
- `run(self, ctx: FeatureContext) -> None` ‚Äî abstract; raises `NotImplementedError` in the base class. This is the single contract method. It is expected to be **synchronous and blocking**: the hub calls it once, and the call does not return until the feature is done (user said "close"/"stop"/"done", or `ctx.abort` got set externally). Internally a feature is free to spin up its own daemon threads (voice listeners, scan workers) as long as `run()` joins/stops them before returning.

### 1.3 Lifecycle driven by hub.py (inferred)

1. User selects/triggers a feature from the menu or a bypass CLI flag (e.g. `--lidar`, `--obstacles`, `--mapping`, `--navigate`).
2. Hub instantiates the corresponding `Feature` subclass and builds a `FeatureContext` with the shared `link`, a fresh/shared `abort` Event, the shared `feedback` object, and a `gesture_queue` if the feature declared it needs one.
3. Hub calls `feature.run(ctx)` and blocks (or manages this on its own thread) until it returns.
4. While RUNNING, the hub's gesture recognizer routes recognized gesture tokens into `ctx.gesture_queue`, and sets `ctx.abort` on the panic/abort gesture.
5. When `run()` returns, control returns to the hub's menu loop; `ctx.abort` may be cleared for the next feature invocation.

This contract is intentionally thin ‚Äî no `stop()`, `pause()`, or `handle_frame()` methods exist; all responsiveness is achieved by each feature's own polling loop checking `ctx.abort` and draining `ctx.gesture_queue` at a tight cadence (tens to hundreds of milliseconds, see below).

## 2. features/env_awareness.py ‚Äî Environmental Awareness

### 2.1 Purpose for the end user

Gives a blind/visually-impaired user an on-demand, spoken description of their immediate surroundings: "what's in front of me right now." Unlike the LiDAR features, this one is vision/LLM-based rather than range-sensor-based, and it explicitly runs **entirely on the OrangePi with no feature-server round trip** for the core describe function ‚Äî it talks directly to Google's Gemini 2.5 Flash API over the internet. It also supports multi-turn follow-up questions ("what color is the door?") answered from conversation history without a new capture, and persists each conversation as a named "session" on local disk so a user can resume a previous walkthrough after a restart.

### 2.2 Relationship to the base.py contract

`EnvAwareness(Feature)` sets `name = "env"`, `title = "Environmental awareness"`, and implements `run(ctx)`. It uses `ctx.feedback` for all TTS/haptic output, `ctx.gesture_queue` to receive `ENV_SCAN`, `ENV_CLOSE`, and `NEXT` gesture tokens (mapped via `_GMAP_ENV` to synthetic voice-equivalent tokens `"scan"`/`"close"`), and `ctx.abort` polled in the main `while` loop and inside the blocking waits. Interestingly, it uses `ctx.link` only for lightweight **status telegrams**, not for the core workload (see 2.3).

### 2.3 Pipeline walkthrough

**Startup / dependency gating.** `run()` first calls `_ensure_mc(fb)` to lazily initialize the shared voice/whisper stack (`orangepi_client`, aliased `mc`) exactly once per process ‚Äî it opportunistically checks whether `MoneyRecognition._models_ready` is already `True` (cross-feature reuse of the loaded Whisper model) before calling `mc.init_cues()`, `mc.auto_detect_all()`, and `mc.load_models()` itself. It then hard-fails with spoken guidance if `google-genai` isn't installed (`_GENAI_OK` guard) or if no `GEMINI_API_KEY` can be found (checked via `os.environ`, then `~/.env`, then `~/keys.env` ‚Äî `_load_api_key()`), and constructs a `genai.Client(api_key=...)`.

**Server notification (fire-and-forget).** Immediately after client construction, and at several other points, the feature calls `ctx.link.send("lidar", {...})` ‚Äî note the routing key is the **literal string `"lidar"`**, not `"env"`. The payload shape is `{"action": "feature_state", "feature_name": "env", "state": "started"|"scan_done"|"stopped", ...}`, with additional keys (`session`, `reply_words`, `keyframes`, `exchanges`) depending on state. The call is wrapped in a bare `try/except Exception: pass` ‚Äî the return value (a dict or `None` from `ServerLink.send`) is **never inspected**. This tells us env_awareness treats the server purely as a passive telemetry/dashboard sink for cross-feature status, reusing whatever handler already exists for the `"lidar"` feature key (inferred as `handlers/lidar.py`) rather than defining its own server route.

**Voice input.** A `_LidarVoice`-independent mechanism is used here: `mc.voice_listen_loop(voice_q, stop_ev, ctx.abort)` runs on a daemon thread (`_voice_on()`), started 1 second after each activation to avoid ALSA races; `_voice_off()` sets `stop_ev` to kill it before any blocking foreground action (recording, listening for a session name). `_get_input()` merges `voice_q` (STT transcripts) and `gesture_queue` (mapped tokens) with a 0.4 s gesture poll window, returning whichever text/token arrives first.

**Command classification.** Raw text goes through `_classify_env()`, a keyword-set matcher against `_CLOSE_W`, `_LOAD_W`, `_SCAN_W` (checked in that priority order); anything not matching becomes a free-form Gemini question.

**SCAN pipeline (the core loop):**
1. `_record_frames()` opens the first working camera among `CAMERA_INDICES = [0,1,2]` via OpenCV (`cv2.VideoCapture`, preferring `CAP_V4L2` backend), probes it with a test read, and if successful records for `VIDEO_DURATION_S = 3` seconds at `VIDEO_FPS = 10` (nominally 30 raw BGR frames), with a hard deadline of duration+2s to avoid hanging.
2. `_extract_keyframes(frames)` reduces those frames to at most `MAX_KEYFRAMES = 5` representative images via a three-stage pipeline: (a) scene-change detection using HSV-histogram Bhattacharyya distance (`cv2.compareHist(..., cv2.HISTCMP_BHATTACHARYYA)`) against a `SCENE_THRESHOLD = 0.30` cut, always keeping first/last frame; (b) if fewer than 3 distinct scenes were found, pad with up to 4 uniformly-spaced samples (`np.linspace`) to guarantee coverage; (c) if still more than 5 candidates, keep only the sharpest by Laplacian variance (`cv2.Laplacian(...).var()`), re-sorted back into temporal order.
3. Each keyframe is JPEG-encoded by `_frame_to_jpeg()` (resized to `MAX_IMG_WIDTH = 1024` px wide if larger, `JPEG_QUALITY = 75`).
4. `_ask_gemini(client, history, user_text, frames)` builds a `contents` list of alternating `"[Frame i of N]"` text markers and `types.Part.from_bytes(data=jpeg, mime_type="image/jpeg")` parts, appends `f"User: {user_text}"`, and calls `client.models.generate_content(model="gemini-2.5-flash", contents=..., config=GenerateContentConfig(system_instruction=_build_system(history), max_output_tokens=512, temperature=0.3))`. `_build_system()` re-injects the last `MAX_HISTORY_TURNS = 16` conversation turns as plain text into the system prompt on every call, since the SDK call itself is stateless per-turn.
5. This is **not** sent through `ServerLink` at all ‚Äî Gemini is called directly from the OrangePi over the internet. Only a post-hoc status ping (`action: "scan_done"`) goes to the server afterward, carrying `reply_words` and `keyframes` counts but not the description text or images themselves.
6. The reply text is spoken via `fb.speak(reply)`; on the very first scan of a session the user is prompted to name the session (or say a `_SKIP_W` word to auto-name it `env_YYYYMMDD_HHMM`), then history is appended and `_autosave()` persists `{name, history}` as JSON under `~/env_sessions/<sanitized_name>.json`.

**LOAD pipeline:** turns off voice, asks for a session name, does an approximate case-insensitive containment match (`_find_session`) against saved session JSON files, and restores `history` in place.

**Free-form question pipeline:** if `history` is empty, the user is told to scan first; otherwise `_ask_gemini(client, history, raw, [])` is called with **no images**, relying purely on the injected history text, and the reply is spoken and appended/saved as above.

**CLOSE / exit:** breaks the main loop; the `finally` block always turns off voice, sends a final `"stopped"` status telegram (with `exchanges` count) to the server, and ‚Äî if there is unsaved history ‚Äî persists the session one more time and speaks a confirmation.

**Idle handling:** if `IDLE_REMIND_S = 60` seconds pass with no input, the feature speaks a contextual reminder of available commands and resets the idle timer ‚Äî a lightweight nudge rather than a timeout/exit.

### 2.4 External libraries

- `cv2` (OpenCV, optional/guarded) ‚Äî camera capture (`VideoCapture`), colorspace conversion (`cvtColor` to HSV/gray), histograms (`calcHist`, `compareHist`, `normalize`) for scene-cut detection, `Laplacian` for sharpness scoring, `resize`, and `imencode` for JPEG.
- `numpy` (optional, paired with cv2) ‚Äî `np.linspace` for uniform frame padding; implicit array ops on frames/histograms.
- `google.genai` / `google.genai.types` (optional) ‚Äî the Gemini SDK client, `Part.from_bytes`, `GenerateContentConfig`.
- `orangepi_client` (aliased `mc`, optional) ‚Äî shared voice stack: `init_cues()`, `auto_detect_all()`, `load_models()`, `voice_listen_loop()`, `listen()`.
- `threading` ‚Äî `Lock` guarding one-time model init, `Event` for voice stop signaling, `Thread` for the voice-start delay wrapper.
- `queue` ‚Äî `Queue` for voice transcripts; `Empty` exception used for non-blocking polling.
- `time` ‚Äî `time.time()`/`sleep()` for deadlines, idle timers, and pacing.
- `os` ‚Äî env var / home-dir path handling, `os.makedirs`, file existence checks, `os.devnull`/`dup`/`dup2` for stderr suppression around noisy camera opens.
- `re` ‚Äî regex word tokenization (`[a-z]+`) for command classification and filename sanitization (`[^\w\-]`).
- `json` ‚Äî session persistence (`dump`/`load`).
- `datetime` ‚Äî auto-generated session name timestamps.
- `contextlib` ‚Äî `@contextmanager` implementing `_quiet_stderr()` to silence OpenCV/V4L2 stderr spam while probing camera indices.

### 2.5 Key classes/functions summary

- `EnvAwareness.run(ctx)` ‚Äî the entire feature; no return value; side effects: spoken output, motor haptics (indirectly via `fb.confirm()`), disk writes under `~/env_sessions/`, two categories of network I/O (Gemini HTTPS, and fire-and-forget `ServerLink` status pings), and a background voice thread lifecycle.
- `_extract_keyframes(frames: list) -> list` ‚Äî pure function, deterministic given identical frame sequence and thresholds.
- `_ask_gemini(client, history, user_text, frames) -> str` ‚Äî the only function that can raise on network/API failure; all call sites wrap it in `try/except Exception`.
- `_ensure_mc(fb) -> bool` ‚Äî module-level singleton guarded by `_mc_lock`/`_mc_ready`, shared with `money_recognition.py`.
- `_classify_env(text) -> str|None` and `_parse` equivalents are pure keyword classifiers, not NLP models ‚Äî brittle but fast and offline.

### 2.6 Concrete scenarios

- **Normal successful scan:** user says "describe" ‚Üí 3 s recording ‚Üí 3‚Äì5 keyframes ‚Üí Gemini responds in under the implicit HTTP timeout ‚Üí description spoken, session named/saved, `"scan_done"` telegram sent.
- **No obstacles / nothing distinctive in view:** not specially handled ‚Äî Gemini simply describes whatever the frames contain (e.g. a blank wall); there is no local "nothing detected" branch, since this feature does no local object detection.
- **Camera unavailable / empty frames:** `_record_frames()` returns `[]` (either `cv2` missing, no camera opens, or all reads fail/return all-zero frames); the SCAN branch immediately speaks "Camera error. Check the USB camera and try again." and re-enables voice without contacting Gemini or the server.
- **Gemini unreachable/timeout:** any exception from `_ask_gemini` is caught; the user hears "Could not reach Gemini. Check your internet connection." (for scans) or "Gemini did not respond. Please try again." (for follow-ups); no partial state is saved for that turn.
- **Feature-server unreachable while sending a status telegram:** silently swallowed (`except Exception: pass`) ‚Äî this cannot block or fail the user-facing flow at all, by design.
- **Malformed/missing voice input:** `_get_input` simply returns `None` on timeout, driving the idle-reminder path rather than an error path; a session-name request with no speech recognized falls back to "No name heard."
- **Feature toggled on while another active:** not itself guarded in this file ‚Äî assumed to be enforced by hub.py's menu semantics (only one `Feature.run()` active at a time on the calling thread).
- **Repeated/spammy triggers:** `_drain()` empties the `voice_q` before/after blocking operations (recording, prompting) to discard stale utterances; there is no explicit cooldown/debounce timer beyond the sequential nature of the loop (each SCAN takes several seconds end-to-end, naturally rate-limiting repeats), and gesture tokens `ENV_SCAN`/`NEXT` both map to the same `"scan"` action so duplicates just re-trigger a fresh scan rather than compounding state.

### 2.7 Shared/server-side implications

`env_awareness.py` imports nothing from `lidar_adapter.py`/`slam_engine.py`. Its only cross-feature coupling is (a) opportunistic reuse of `MoneyRecognition._models_ready`/the shared Whisper loader in `orangepi_client`, and (b) piggybacking all of its server telemetry onto the `"lidar"` feature channel via `ServerLink.send("lidar", {...})`. On the server side this implies a single dispatcher (plausibly `handlers/lidar.py`, given the shared `feature` tag with the LiDAR features below) that recognizes `action: "feature_state"` messages carrying an arbitrary `feature_name` field (here `"env"`) and updates some kind of live dashboard/log of which glove feature is active, rather than a dedicated `handlers/env.py`. The server is not expected to return anything meaningful for these calls ‚Äî replies are never read.

## 3. features/lidar_nav.py ‚Äî LiDAR SLAM: Mapping, Saving, Navigation, Obstacle Avoidance

### 3.1 Purpose for the end user

This is the largest and most safety-critical feature: it turns the glove-mounted LiDAR into (a) an always-on haptic obstacle-avoidance aid (front/left/right proximity buzzing), (b) a room-mapping and voice-labelling tool ("save kitchen"), and (c) a point-to-point indoor navigation guide ("take me to kitchen") that steers the user with directional vibration and periodic spoken distance/bearing updates until arrival. It is exposed as four distinct `Feature` subclasses launched via different hub bypass flags, sharing nearly all of their machinery.

### 3.2 Relationship to base.py

All four classes ‚Äî `LidarNavigation` (`name="lidar"`, full mapping+navigation), `LidarObstacleTest` (`name="obstacles"`, sensor-only), `LidarMappingTest` (`name="mapping"`, SLAM-only), `LidarNavigateTest` (`name="navigate"`, navigate-to-saved-room) ‚Äî implement `run(ctx)` per the base contract, use `ctx.feedback` for speech and haptics, `ctx.gesture_queue` for `NEXT`/`EDIT` backups to voice commands, and `ctx.abort` as the master stop signal checked in every loop iteration and propagated into the two background threads each spawns (a scan-reader thread and a voice thread). `LidarNavigateTest` additionally reads a `room_name` class attribute populated from a `--navigate-room` CLI argument.

### 3.3 Dependency shape on lidar_adapter.py / slam_engine.py

```
from lidar_adapter import MS200Adapter
from slam_engine   import SLAMEngine, ROOMS_DIR
```
guarded by `_LIDAR_OK`; every `run()` method bails out early with a spoken error if the import failed. Usage:
- `MS200Adapter.find_port(baud=230400, timeout=2.0)` ‚Äî auto-detect the serial port (`_resolve_port`).
- `MS200Adapter(port, baud=230400, median_kernel=5, max_jump_m=0.5).start()` ‚Äî construct+start the sensor driver (`_new_adapter`); `adapter.get_scan(timeout=1.0)` polled by `_scan_worker` on a daemon thread into a bounded `queue.Queue(maxsize=2)` (drops scans when full ‚Äî a deliberate freshness-over-completeness policy).
- `MS200Adapter.to_xy(scan)` ‚Äî converts a raw scan into Cartesian points for SLAM.
- `SLAMEngine(map_resolution=0.05, map_size_m=30.0, db_dir=ROOMS_DIR, debug=False)` constructed by `_new_slam()`, which also **monkey-patches** an instance attribute `slam.ICP_MAX_ROT_DEG = 20.0` to override the engine's default (documented as 6¬∞) so that in-place body turns aren't clamped/rejected by the scan-matcher.
- `slam.update(pts, rpm=scan.rpm)` ‚Äî the core SLAM step, returns a `result` object exposing `.pose` (with `.x`, `.y`, `.yaw`), `.room_match`, and `.loop_closed`.
- `slam.keyframes` ‚Äî list of keyframe objects with `.id`, `.timestamp`, `.pose`.
- `slam.occ_map.grid` / `.occ_map.to_image()` ‚Äî occupancy grid array and rendered image for map PNG export.
- `slam.list_rooms()`, `slam.save_room(name)`, `slam.load_room(name)`, `slam.direction_to_room(target) -> (?, ?, dist_m, bearing_deg) | None` ‚Äî the room database API.

This file treats `slam_engine.py` purely as a black-box SLAM/room-database service and `lidar_adapter.py` purely as a black-box serial sensor driver ‚Äî all of the code here is orchestration, thresholds, voice/gesture UX, haptics, and network reporting layered on top.

### 3.4 Pipeline walkthrough (common skeleton, then per-feature deltas)

**Startup (all four):** check `_LIDAR_OK`; resolve serial port via `_resolve_port` (spoken "Searching for lidar." / "Lidar not found. Check the USB cable." / "Lidar found."); construct the adapter (any exception ‚Üí spoken `f"Lidar error: {e}"` and abort); construct SLAM (except `LidarObstacleTest`, which skips SLAM entirely); start `_scan_worker` daemon thread; start `_LidarVoice(voice_q)` and, for the full-featured `LidarNavigation`, block up to 10 s on `voice._ready` before announcing whether voice is available ("Voice ready." vs "Voice unavailable. Use gestures.").

**Voice command parsing (`_parse_voice`)** recognizes, from raw lowercased Whisper text: `stop/abort/quit/exit` ‚Üí `("abort",)`; `"list"` or `"what room"` ‚Üí `("list",)`; `"save [name]"` (regex) or bare `"save"`/`"save room"` ‚Üí `("save", name_or_None)`; five phrasings of "take/bring/navigate/go/head [me] to X" ‚Üí `("navigate", name)` with leading articles stripped. `_match_room` fuzzy-matches spoken room names against saved rooms using `difflib.get_close_matches(cutoff=0.4)` on space-normalized strings.

**Server messages ‚Äî always tagged `"lidar"` regardless of which subclass sent them** (`ctx.link.send("lidar", {...})` is hardcoded at every call site, not `ctx.link.send(self.name, ...)`), meaning a single server-side `"lidar"` handler is expected to branch on the `action` field:
- `{"action": "map_save", "room_name": str, "frame": <base64 PNG>, "connected_to": str|None}` ‚Äî sent by `_send_map()`/`_do_save()` whenever a room is voice-saved, and also by `LidarNavigateTest` at start to re-upload the target room's map for a live viewer.
- `{"action": "map_update", "room_name": "live_map"|"live_obstacles", "frame": <base64 PNG>}` ‚Äî periodic live map/radar snapshots (mapping test every `MAP_LIVE_UPDATE_S = 15` s; obstacle test every 1.0 s using the full 360¬∞ radar PNG from `_make_radar_png`).
- `{"action": "pose_update", "room_name": str, "x": float, "y": float}` ‚Äî sent during navigation every `POSE_UPDATE_S = 2.0` s so a server-side viewer can animate the user's dot on the map.
- `{"action": "report", "mode": "mapping"|"navigate"|"obstacles", "session_id": str, "data": {...}}` ‚Äî end-of-session structured summaries (see 3.6 for exact payload contents per mode) sent by `_send_report()`.

Note: `ServerLink.send()` (from `net/client.py`) is a **blocking, synchronous, JSON-over-length-prefixed-TCP call** with a default 120 s socket timeout, and it returns the server's decoded reply dict or `None` on any connection/timeout/JSON error. Every single call site in `lidar_nav.py` (`_send_map`, `_send_report`, the `pose_update` sends) either ignores the return value outright or is not wrapped in `try/except` at all for the `pose_update` and `_send_report`/`_send_map` calls ‚Äî meaning **a slow or unreachable server can stall the main SLAM/haptics loop for up to the full timeout window**, unlike env_awareness.py which wraps every send in `try/except Exception: pass`. This is a materially different (and riskier) failure-handling posture and worth flagging: an obstacle-avoidance-critical loop can block on network I/O.

**Obstacle haptics ‚Äî the shared safety layer**, `_obstacle_haptics(scan, ctx, last_haptic, nav_target=None, slam=None)`, runs every scan cycle across all four features. It self-throttles to at most once per `HAPTIC_INTERVAL = 0.22` s. It computes the minimum in-range distance in three ¬±`SECTOR_HALF_DEG = 45¬∞` sectors centered on sensor angles 0¬∞ (front, MT3), 90¬∞ (left, MT2), 270¬∞ (right, MT1), each masked to ignore returns closer than `MIN_OBSTACLE_M = 0.10` m (filtering the sensor's own stabilizer housing). `_dist_ms(d)` maps distance to pulse duration via `_DIST_LEVELS = [(0.30,420),(0.60,300),(1.00,160),(1.50,70)]` ‚Äî i.e. **< 0.30 m ‚Üí 420 ms (strongest/emergency), 0.30‚Äì0.60 m ‚Üí 300 ms, 0.60‚Äì1.00 m ‚Üí 160 ms, 1.00‚Äì1.50 m ‚Üí 70 ms, ‚â• 1.50 m ‚Üí silent (0 ms, no pulse)**. Priority order is front > left > right: if front has any nonzero pulse duration it fires MT3 and returns immediately, never checking left/right that cycle. Only if all three sectors are clear does it fall through to a directional "steer toward destination" haptic when navigating: `slam.direction_to_room(nav_target)` gives a bearing; `>15¬∞` pulses MT2 (turn-left cue), `<-15¬∞` pulses MT1 (turn-right cue), using `_bearing_ms`: `‚â•60¬∞ ‚Üí 220 ms, ‚â•30¬∞ ‚Üí 130 ms, otherwise 70 ms`.

**Feature 1 ‚Äî `LidarNavigation` (full flow, `--lidar`).** Starts in `mode="mapping"`. Voice/gesture commands: `"save [name]"` (or bare "save", auto-named `room_{n+1}`) calls `_do_save`, which requires `len(slam.keyframes) >= MIN_KF_TO_SAVE = 5` or refuses with "Not enough data ‚Äî N keyframes. Walk more."; on success it speaks confirmation (mentioning `connected_to` the previous room saved this session, tracked in `_session_rooms`) and uploads the map PNG. `"take me to X"` fuzzy-matches a saved room and switches `mode="navigation"`, `nav_target=matched`. `"list rooms"` speaks all saved names. `"stop"` sets `ctx.abort`. Gesture `NEXT` mirrors save (mapping mode) or cycles to the next saved room (navigation mode); `EDIT` returns to mapping mode. Every scan cycle: `slam.update()` runs; haptics fire; if navigating, a `pose_update` is sent every 2 s and a spoken distance/bearing update ("kitchen: 2.3 m, turn left.") every `NAV_SPEAK_S = 6.0` s via `_bearing_str` (`>15¬∞` "turn left", `<-15¬∞` "turn right", else "straight ahead"); if mapping and `slam.update()` reports a `room_match` (loop-closure/relocalization against a known room), it speaks "Recognised: X." On exit (`finally`), threads are stopped, adapter released, and ‚Äî provided at least `MIN_KF_TO_SAVE` keyframes exist ‚Äî a full session report is always sent regardless of save state, with `keyframe_log` (id, timestamp, x, y per keyframe), total path length (`_path_length`, Euclidean sum over consecutive keyframe positions), duration, and the list of rooms saved this session.

**Feature 2 ‚Äî `LidarObstacleTest` (`--obstacles`).** No SLAM at all ‚Äî pure sensor+haptics+logging for fast bring-up/testing. Every scan appends an event record (`t`, `front_m`, `left_m`, `right_m`, `motor`, `motor_ms`) to an in-memory list; a full 360¬∞ radar PNG (`_make_radar_png`, see 3.5) is uploaded as `map_update`/`room_name: "live_obstacles"` once per second. On stop, `_build_obstacle_report` aggregates per-sector min/max/avg distance stats and motor-fire counts (`MT1`/`MT2`/`MT3`) across the whole session and sends it as `action: "report", mode: "obstacles"`.

**Feature 3 ‚Äî `LidarMappingTest` (`--mapping`).** SLAM without navigation; voice "save X" persists the room (subject to the same 5-keyframe minimum) and immediately sends a `_send_mapping_report` (keyframe log with yaw in degrees, occupied-cell count from thresholding `slam.occ_map.grid > 0.5`, loop-closure count incremented whenever `slam.update().loop_closed` is true, path length, duration); voice "stop" quits without saving. A live map (`room_name="live_map"`) is uploaded every `MAP_LIVE_UPDATE_S = 15` s regardless of saves, and once more unconditionally in the `finally` block; if the user never explicitly saved, an "unsaved_session" report is still sent as long as the keyframe minimum was met.

**Feature 4 ‚Äî `LidarNavigateTest` (`--navigate`).** Requires a pre-set `room_name` (from CLI); refuses to start if unset or unmatched against `slam.list_rooms()` (fuzzy match). Loads the saved room's occupancy grid (`slam.load_room`) and immediately re-uploads its map so a server-side live viewer has it before movement starts. Requires the user to start at the SLAM origin (0,0) ‚Äî i.e., the same physical spot as when mapping began. Every scan cycle computes `direction_to_room`; sends `pose_update` every 2 s (also appending to a local `pose_log` with distance/bearing for the eventual report); fires the shared obstacle+directional haptics; speaks distance/bearing every 6 s; and ‚Äî the one hard stopping condition unique to this feature ‚Äî declares arrival and **terminates the session** the moment `dist_m < 0.5` (metres) to the target, speaking `f"Arrived at {room}!"`. Gesture `EDIT` or `NEXT` also aborts navigation early (used as a manual "give up" control). The final report includes `arrived: bool`, `start_dist_m`/`end_dist_m` (first/last logged distances), `path_length_m`, and the full `pose_log`.

### 3.5 The live radar visualization (`_make_radar_png`)

Worth calling out as a distinct rendering pipeline: builds a 400√ó400 px polar plot (`numpy`+`cv2`) with compass spokes every 30¬∞, four labelled distance rings at 0.30/0.60/1.00/1.50 m, and every valid scan point (beyond the 0.10 m housing-ignore radius) plotted with urgency coloring ‚Äî red `<0.3m`, orange `<0.6m`, yellow `<1.0m`, green `<1.5m`, dark grey beyond 1.5 m (clamped display range `DISP_MAX_M = 1.5`). It also corrects for the sensor being physically mounted 90¬∞ rotated on the glove (`ROT = -œÄ/2`, with an explicit angle-mapping table in the docstring: sensor 0¬∞‚Üíphysical LEFT, 90¬∞‚ÜíFRONT, 180¬∞‚ÜíRIGHT, 270¬∞‚ÜíBACK), and overlays live per-direction distance text (FRONT/BACK/LEFT/RIGHT). This PNG is what backs the `map_update`/`live_obstacles` telemetry from `LidarObstacleTest`.

### 3.6 External libraries

- `math` ‚Äî trigonometry for sector masks (`radians`), haptic bearing/degree conversions, Euclidean distance (`hypot`) in `_path_length`, radar plotting geometry (`sin`/`cos`).
- `queue` ‚Äî bounded `Queue(maxsize=2)` for scan buffering (drop-oldest-by-fullness policy since `put_nowait` is skipped when full), unbounded queues for voice commands and gestures, `Empty` for polling.
- `threading` ‚Äî `Thread` (scan worker, voice `_run`/`_asr_worker`), `Event` (`ctx.abort`, `_LidarVoice._stop`, `_ready`).
- `time` ‚Äî `time.time()` pacing for all interval-based sends (`HAPTIC_INTERVAL`, `POSE_UPDATE_S`, `NAV_SPEAK_S`, `MAP_LIVE_UPDATE_S`), `time.strftime` for session IDs, `time.sleep` in the voice stream idle loop.
- `re` ‚Äî voice command regex parsing (`_parse_voice`) and room-name normalization.
- `difflib` ‚Äî `get_close_matches` for fuzzy room-name matching.
- `io` ‚Äî `BytesIO` for the PIL PNG-encoding fallback path in `_map_to_png`.
- `typing.Optional` ‚Äî type hints only.
- `cv2` (imported lazily/optionally inside `_map_to_png`, `_make_radar_png`) ‚Äî PNG encoding, drawing primitives (`line`, `circle`, `putText`) for the map/radar images.
- `numpy` (lazy, inside `_make_radar_png` and `_LidarVoice._asr_worker`) ‚Äî image buffer allocation, PCM int16‚Üífloat32 normalization for Whisper.
- `PIL.Image` (lazy fallback inside `_map_to_png`, only if `cv2` PNG encode fails) ‚Äî alternate PNG encoder.
- `sounddevice` (lazy, inside `_LidarVoice._run`) ‚Äî `InputStream` microphone capture with a callback-based, non-blocking design.
- `faster_whisper.WhisperModel` (lazy) ‚Äî `"tiny"` model, CPU, int8 quantization, used for STT transcription of each captured utterance.
- `webrtcvad` (lazy, optional ‚Äî falls back to "always speech" if missing) ‚Äî voice-activity detection (`Vad(2)`, aggressiveness mode 2) gating when to start/stop buffering an utterance.

### 3.7 Key classes/functions

- `_LidarVoice` ‚Äî the always-on background voice listener shared by all four features. Constants: `SAMPLERATE=16000` Hz, `FRAME_MS=30` ms (480-sample frames), `SPEECH_LEAD=4` consecutive speech frames to open an utterance, `SILENCE_TAIL=25` silent frames (~0.75 s) to close it, `MAX_FRAMES=333` (~10 s) hard cap. Architecture is deliberately two-threaded: the `sounddevice` callback thread (`_cb`) only classifies frames via VAD and accumulates PCM bytes into a rolling pre-roll `ring` buffer plus an in-progress `speech` buffer, pushing completed utterances onto `_utt_q`; a separate `_asr_worker` thread pulls from `_utt_q` and runs Whisper transcription (0.3‚Äì1 s), so the mic callback is never blocked by inference and cannot drop audio. Recognized text is parsed by `_parse_voice` and, if it matches a known command, pushed onto the feature's `cmd_q`. `self.failed`/`self._ready` communicate init success/failure back to the owning feature without blocking indefinitely (guarded by `_ready.wait(timeout=10.0)` in `LidarNavigation`).
- `_scan_worker(adapter, scan_q, abort)` ‚Äî trivial polling loop bridging the blocking `adapter.get_scan(timeout=1.0)` calls into a queue consumed by the main loop; drops a scan if the queue is already full rather than blocking, favoring freshness.
- `_obstacle_haptics`, `_sector_min`, `_dist_ms`, `_bearing_str`, `_bearing_ms` ‚Äî the safety/UX geometry layer described above; all pure/stateless except the throttling timestamp passed in and returned explicitly (no hidden globals).
- `_do_save(slam, ctx, room_name, prev_room=None) -> bool` ‚Äî the shared "commit a room" operation with the 5-keyframe gate.
- `_send_map`, `_send_report` ‚Äî thin wrappers around `ctx.link.send("lidar", ...)`.
- `_build_obstacle_report`, `_send_mapping_report` ‚Äî per-mode report assemblers producing the `data` payload of the `"report"` action.

### 3.8 Concrete scenarios

- **Normal mapping+navigation session:** user walks the mapping route, says "save kitchen" (‚â•5 keyframes present) ‚Üí map PNG uploaded, confirmation spoken; later says "take me to kitchen" ‚Üí mode switches, periodic pose updates and 6 s spoken bearings, haptic front/left/right cues throughout; arrival (`LidarNavigateTest` only) at <0.5 m ends the session with a spoken confirmation and a report.
- **No obstacles detected:** all three sector distances exceed 1.5 m (or are `inf` from an empty sector mask) ‚Üí `_dist_ms` returns 0 for all, no motor pulses fire that cycle; in navigation mode the loop falls through to the directional steering haptic instead.
- **Obstacle too close (emergency case):** any sector distance drops below `MIN_OBSTACLE_M=0.10` m is treated as *no return* (filtered as housing noise, not as an obstacle) ‚Äî so genuinely there is a "blind zone" under 10 cm where nothing fires. The strongest real alert band is **0‚Äì0.30 m ‚Üí 420 ms pulses at up to ~4.5 Hz** (throttled by the 0.22 s haptic interval), front sector always taking priority over left/right so a user is never left un-alerted to a frontal collision risk by a simultaneous side cue.
- **Server unreachable/timeout while awaiting a response:** because `ServerLink.send` blocks up to the 120 s socket timeout and most call sites here (`pose_update`, `_send_report`, some `_send_map` calls) are **not** wrapped in try/except, an unreachable feature-server can stall the SLAM/haptics main loop mid-session ‚Äî a materially different (weaker) resilience posture than `env_awareness.py`. Practically this means loss of obstacle-avoidance responsiveness for however long the TCP call is trying to complete/timeout on a dead link.
- **Malformed/missing sensor data:** an empty/`None` scan from `adapter.get_scan()` is simply not queued (`_scan_worker` only puts non-`None` results); the main loop's `queue.get(timeout=0.05)` then raises `Empty` and it just `continue`s ‚Äî effectively a no-op cycle, not a crash. `_sector_min` returns `float("inf")` for an empty mask (no points in a sector), which `_dist_ms` maps to silence.
- **Feature toggled on while another active:** not handled in-file; relies on hub.py allowing only one `run()` at a time, though a subtlety exists ‚Äî because all four subclasses hardcode `ctx.link.send("lidar", ...)`, the server cannot distinguish, from the `feature` tag alone, which of the four local classes sent a given message; it must rely on the `action`/payload shape instead (e.g., `report.mode` disambiguates `"mapping"` vs `"navigate"` vs `"obstacles"`).
- **Repeated/spammy voice or gesture triggers:** haptics are hard-throttled to one decision per `HAPTIC_INTERVAL=0.22`s regardless of how fast scans arrive; spoken navigation updates are throttled to once per `NAV_SPEAK_S=6`s; live map/radar uploads are throttled to 15 s / 1 s respectively; repeated "save" commands are inherently rate-limited by requiring 5 new keyframes to accumulate again (SLAM keyframes are not reset per save, so a duplicate immediate "save" would likely succeed again by reusing already-accumulated keyframes ‚Äî there is no explicit re-save cooldown or duplicate-name guard).

### 3.9 What is shared with the rest of the codebase

- Imports `MS200Adapter` from `lidar_adapter.py` (serial sensor driver: port discovery, scan acquisition, `to_xy` conversion) and `SLAMEngine`, `ROOMS_DIR` from `slam_engine.py` (pose estimation, occupancy mapping, room persistence, loop-closure/room-recognition, bearing/direction queries) ‚Äî both treated as opaque, already-documented subsystems.
- Shares the `ctx.feedback._pulse(motor, ms)` three-motor haptic API and `ctx.feedback.speak/confirm/wait` with every other feature in the codebase (including env_awareness.py).
- Shares the `_LidarVoice`/`sounddevice`+`faster-whisper`+`webrtcvad` architecture pattern with the OCR reader feature (per env_awareness.py's docstring reference) and, at a design level, mirrors env_awareness.py's earlier `orangepi_client`-based voice approach, though `lidar_nav.py`'s implementation is self-contained (its own `_LidarVoice` class) rather than reusing `orangepi_client.voice_listen_loop`.
- All server-bound traffic funnels through the single shared `net.client.ServerLink` instance (`ctx.link`), always tagged `feature="lidar"`, with `action` values `map_save`, `map_update`, `pose_update`, `report`, and (from env_awareness.py) `feature_state` ‚Äî strongly implying one consolidated server-side module, most plausibly `handlers/lidar.py`, that persists/forwards room map PNGs, live pose dots, and JSON session reports to whatever dashboard or storage the "server_app" maintains, and that also doubles as a generic feature-activity tracker for other features (env) that piggyback on the same channel.

## DIAGRAM GENERATION PROMPT ‚Äî Environment Awareness & LiDAR Navigation Features

Draw two side-by-side vertical swimlane pipeline diagrams on one canvas for an OrangePi assistive-robot glove system. Left lane, titled "EnvAwareness (features/env_awareness.py)": show a loop starting at "Voice/gesture input (ENV_SCAN, ENV_CLOSE, NEXT via gesture_queue; mc.voice_listen_loop)" ‚Üí "_classify_env() keyword router" branching three ways to "SCAN: _record_frames() OpenCV camera (3s @ 10fps)" ‚Üí "_extract_keyframes(): HSV Bhattacharyya scene-cut @ threshold 0.30, pad to 3, keep top 5 by Laplacian sharpness" ‚Üí "_frame_to_jpeg() resize 1024px, JPEG q=75" ‚Üí "_ask_gemini(): Gemini 2.5 Flash API (direct HTTPS, not through feature server)" ‚Üí "fb.speak(reply) + save session JSON in ~/env_sessions/"; and "LOAD"/"CLOSE" branches; with a dashed side-arrow labeled 'ctx.link.send("lidar", {action: feature_state, feature_name: env, state: started/scan_done/stopped}) ‚Äî fire-and-forget, exceptions swallowed' pointing to a small "Feature Server (handlers/lidar.py?)" box. Right lane, titled "LiDAR family (features/lidar_nav.py: LidarNavigation, LidarObstacleTest, LidarMappingTest, LidarNavigateTest)": show "MS200Adapter (lidar_adapter.py) @ 230400 baud" feeding a "_scan_worker thread ‚Üí bounded scan_q(maxsize=2)" into "SLAMEngine.update() (slam_engine.py, ICP_MAX_ROT_DEG overridden to 20¬∞)" which forks into "_obstacle_haptics(): sectors ¬±45¬∞ at 0¬∞/90¬∞/270¬∞ (front/left/right), ignore <0.10m housing, pulse ms by distance band 0.30m‚Üí420ms, 0.60m‚Üí300ms, 1.00m‚Üí160ms, 1.50m‚Üí70ms, else silent, throttled to one decision per 0.22s, priority front>left>right, driving glove motors MT3/MT2/MT1" and "navigation branch: slam.direction_to_room() ‚Üí bearing >15¬∞ turn-left / <-15¬∞ turn-right haptic and speech every 6s, pose_update sent every 2s, arrival declared and session ends when distance < 0.5m". Add a shared "_LidarVoice: sounddevice mic callback ‚Üí webrtcvad ‚Üí faster-whisper 'tiny' ASR worker thread ‚Üí _parse_voice() commands save/take me to/list/stop" box feeding voice commands into the SLAM lane. Show all four LiDAR classes converging on one outbound arrow labeled 'ctx.link.send("lidar", {action: map_save/map_update/pose_update/report, room_name, frame: PNG, x, y, data:{...}})' into the same "Feature Server" box, and annotate that unlike EnvAwareness, several of these sends are NOT exception-guarded and can block the safety loop on a slow/dead server connection. Use warning-red coloring on the <0.30m obstacle band and the "server send unguarded" annotation to emphasize risk areas.

================================================================================
SECTION 4 ‚Äî OCR READER, MONEY RECOGNITION & PROGRAMMABLE FEATURES
================================================================================

## OCR Reader, Money Recognition & Programmable Features

### 0. Shared Contract: features/base.py (brief, for self-containedness)

`features/base.py` defines the minimal interface every feature module implements so `hub.py` can drive them uniformly through a state machine.

- `FeatureContext` (a `@dataclass`): the bundle of dependencies injected into every feature at invocation time.
  - `link` (`net.client.ServerLink`): the single persistent TCP socket to the Python feature server; all outbound messages go through `link.send(feature_name, payload_dict)`.
  - `abort` (`threading.Event`): set asynchronously by the hub when the user performs a panic/abort gesture; every blocking loop in a feature must poll it to exit promptly.
  - `feedback` (`gesture_hub.feedback.Feedback`): local audio/haptic output object exposing at least `speak()`, `play_raw()`, `wait()`, `confirm()`, `silence()`.
  - `gesture_queue` (`queue.Queue | None`): populated by the state machine with raw gesture-name strings while the feature is in the RUNNING state, for features (like OCR) that need in-session gesture control beyond simple menu navigation.
- `Feature` base class: a plain class (not ABC, but enforced by convention) exposing two class attributes, `name` (the routing key sent to the server as the `"feature"` field) and `title` (the spoken/display name in the menu), plus one instance method `run(self, ctx: FeatureContext) -> None` that raises `NotImplementedError` in the base ‚Äî every concrete feature owns the interaction loop until it returns normally or `ctx.abort` fires.

This is the entire contract: no `stop()`, no lifecycle hooks beyond `run()`. Concrete features are expected to loop, check `ctx.abort` frequently, and clean up (autosave, "goodbye" TTS) in their own `finally` blocks before returning.

---

### 1. features/ocr_reader.py ‚Äî Book Reader Feature

#### 1.1 Purpose and Role

`OCRReader` (`name="ocr"`, `title="Book reader"`) implements a full "camera-to-speech book reading" experience for a visually-impaired user: point a wearable/handheld camera at a printed page, capture it, have the server OCR the image and synthesize speech, then listen to the page read back chunk-by-chunk with gesture-based pause/skip/rewind controls. It supports multi-page reading sessions that are named, auto-saved to disk as JSON, and can later be reloaded ("load `<name>`") or appended to ("add `<name>`"). It is by far the most complex feature file (978 lines), implementing a nested nested-state machine of its own (idle/scan-wait loop ‚Üí capture ‚Üí result ‚Üí page-reading loop ‚Üí pause sub-loop) layered on top of the hub's own state machine.

#### 1.2 End-to-End Pipeline Walkthrough

**Activation**: The hub instantiates `OCRReader` and calls `run(ctx)` when the user's gesture/menu selection routes to `"ocr"`. On entry, the gesture queue is drained (`_drain(gq)`), `_ensure_mc(fb)` lazily initializes the shared `orangepi_client` (`mc`) module ‚Äî cues, device auto-detection, and Whisper model loading ‚Äî reusing an already-initialized instance if `MoneyRecognition._models_ready` is already `True` (cross-feature optimization to avoid loading Whisper twice).

**Opening announcement**: Voice listening is started early (`_voice_on()`) so that Whisper/model warm-up overlaps with the TTS announcement. The feature speaks a summary of existing saved sessions (`_startup_summary()`, reading each session's `.json` file under `~/ocr_sessions` and reporting name/pages/word-count) followed by the command menu, via `_srvspeak()`.

**Voice/gesture command loop** (outer "scan-wait" loop): `_get_cmd()` polls, in priority order, the voice-recognition queue (populated by a background thread running `mc.voice_listen_loop`) then the gesture queue, mapping raw gesture names through `_GMAP` (e.g. `OCR_SCAN`‚Üí`SCAN`, `OCR_PAUSE`‚Üí`PAUSE`, `NEXT`‚Üí`NEXT`, `OCR_CLOSE`‚Üí`CLOSE`) and raw voice transcripts through `_classify()` (keyword-set matching against `_SCAN_W`, `_LOAD_W`, `_ADD_W`, `_NEXT_W`, `_CLOSE_W`, `_YES_W`, `_NO_W`). An idle-timeout reminder fires every `IDLE_REMIND_S` (60s) if no command is recognized.

**Capture** (triggered by `SCAN`/`NEXT` commands): voice is muted (`_voice_off()`), TTS says "Hold the page flat and steady. Capturing now.", then `_capture_frame(fb)` is called:
- First tries `mc.capture_best_frame_local()` (the shared client's OpenCV capture routine: opens `/dev/video{CAM_DEVICE}` trying V4L2/GStreamer/ANY backends, falls back to scanning all `/dev/video*` nodes, warms up `CAM_WARMUP_FRAMES` frames, then samples frames for `CAM_CAPTURE_SEC` at `CAM_FPS`, scoring each with Laplacian-variance sharpness (`cv2.Laplacian(gray, cv2.CV_64F).var()`) and keeping the sharpest; rejects the whole capture if `best_score < MIN_SHARPNESS`) ‚Äî returns raw JPEG bytes or `None`.
- Falls back to the local `_capture_jpeg_cv2()` (module-private OpenCV routine trying `CAMERA_INDICES = [0,1,2]`, warming autofocus, taking 5 frames and keeping the sharpest by the same Laplacian-variance metric, encoding with `cv2.imencode(".jpg", best, [cv2.IMWRITE_JPEG_QUALITY, 92])`) if `mc` capture fails or is unavailable.
- On success, calls `fb.confirm()` (haptic/audio cue).

**Message sent to server**: `resp = ctx.link.send("ocr", {"type": "scan", "frame": jpeg})`. The `jpeg` value is raw `bytes`; `ServerLink.send()` (in `net/client.py`) detects that `payload["frame"]` is `bytes`/`bytearray` and base64-encodes it to an ASCII string before JSON-serializing and sending over the length-prefixed TCP frame. The outer envelope becomes `{"type": "scan", "frame": "<base64>", "feature": "ocr"}`.

**Expected server response fields** (inferred, consumed from `resp`):
- `text` (str): OCR'd page text; empty/whitespace-only means "no text found".
- `page` (int|None): detected page number parsed by the server (e.g. via a printed page-number heuristic).
- `chunks` (list[str]|None): server-pre-split reading chunks (paragraph/sentence-sized); if absent, the client falls back to local `_chunk_text()`.
- `chunk_wavs` (list[str|None]|None): parallel list of base64-encoded WAV audio per chunk, pre-synthesized server-side (avoids per-chunk TTS round trips during reading).
- `announcement_wav` (str|None): a single pre-synthesized base64 WAV announcing "Page N, X words" (or similar), played directly if present.
This strongly implies a server-side handler ‚Äî most plausibly `handlers/ocr.py` ‚Äî that: decodes the base64 frame, runs OCR (e.g. Tesseract/EasyOCR/cloud OCR), attempts page-number detection, chunks the text for TTS pacing, and pre-renders WAV audio per chunk plus a summary announcement using a Windows-side TTS engine (SAPI/Piper, matching the docstring "server Windows voice (SAPI/Piper)").

**Handling "no text found"**: if `text_body` is empty after `.strip()`, the feature speaks "No text found. Hold page 30 to 40 centimetres from camera with good lighting, then scan again." and returns to the scan-wait loop ‚Äî no page is stored.

**Page-number resolution**: if `detected_page` is `None`, the feature optionally asks the user via voice ("Say the page number, or say skip.") and parses the reply with `_parse_number()` (regex digit extraction, falling back to a word-number dictionary `_WORD_NUMS` covering zero‚Äìtwenty and multiples of ten to ninety) unless the reply matches `_SKIP_W`.

**Storage**: pages are stored in a `dict` keyed by `("num", page_number)` or `("idx", running_index)` tuples ‚Äî this dual-keying lets numbered pages be read back in numeric order and unnumbered pages appended by capture order (`_reading_order()` sorts `"num"` keys numerically then appends `"idx"` keys). Rescanning an already-seen page number replaces it in place with an announcement.

**Session naming**: on the very first successful scan of a session, if `session_name` is unset, the user is asked to say a name; unrecognized/skip/failure falls back to an auto-generated `f"reading_{self._session_counter}"`.

**Reading loop** (`_read_pages(start_key)`): iterates pages in `_reading_order()`, chunk by chunk, playing pre-synthesized WAV audio (`_play_wav_b64`) when available or falling back to local `fb.speak(chunks[i])` with an estimated duration `_chunk_dur()` (`len(words)/WORDS_PER_SEC + 0.4`, `WORDS_PER_SEC=2.5`). During each chunk's playback window, gesture polls check for `OCR_PAUSE` (pause), `OCR_FWD`/`OCR_BWD` (skip/rewind `SKIP_CHUNKS=3` chunks), `NEXT`/`OCR_SCAN` (jump to next page), `OCR_CLOSE` (abort+close). While paused, voice is re-enabled and the same command set plus `YES`/`NO`(resume) is accepted. Returns one of `"scan"`, `"close"`, `"done"` to the outer loop.

**Session persistence**: `_autosave()` fires after every `_read_pages()` return that isn't a close, writing `~/ocr_sessions/{sanitized_name}.json` (`_save_session`) with `{"name": ..., "pages": [...]}`. On final exit (the `finally` block), the feature computes `_missing_pages()` (gaps in the numeric sequence) and warns the user before speaking a final "Saved as `<name>`. N pages, X words." summary.

**Server TTS convention** (`_srvspeak`): every spoken announcement in this feature (except a few pure-local fallback messages, e.g. "Server not reachable" and "Camera error") goes through `_srvspeak(ctx, fb, text)`, which sends `{"feature": "tts", "text": text}` to the server (note: bypasses `ServerLink`'s auto-injection convenience since it calls `ctx.link.send("tts", {"text": text})`, i.e. the `feature` string argument is `"tts"`), expects `{"ok": True, "audio": "<base64 wav>"}`, decodes and plays it via `fb.play_raw()`. Any exception, missing response, `ok is not True`, or missing `audio` silently falls back to local `fb.speak(text)` (offline espeak-ng equivalent). This implies a generic `handlers/tts.py`-style handler on the server dedicated to text-to-speech synthesis, shared by any feature (used identically by this file's `_srvspeak`).

#### 1.3 External / Third-Party Libraries

- `base64` ‚Äî encode/decode WAV audio and (indirectly, inside `ServerLink`) JPEG frames.
- `contextlib` ‚Äî `@contextlib.contextmanager` used for `_quiet_stderr()`, a context manager that temporarily redirects OS-level file descriptor 2 (stderr) to `os.devnull` to suppress noisy OpenCV/V4L2 warnings during camera probing.
- `json` ‚Äî reading/writing session files (`~/ocr_sessions/*.json`) and implicitly relied upon inside `ServerLink`/`mc` for wire protocol (not called directly here for network I/O).
- `os` ‚Äî path expansion (`os.path.expanduser`), directory listing/creation (`os.makedirs`, `os.listdir`, `os.path.isdir`), and raw fd manipulation (`os.open`, `os.dup`, `os.dup2`, `os.close`) for the stderr-quieting trick.
- `queue` ‚Äî `queue.Queue` for both the voice-transcript queue and (via `ctx.gesture_queue`) gesture events; `queue.Empty` exception used for non-blocking polling patterns.
