- `re` ‚Äî regex-based tokenization/classification of voice commands (`_classify`, `_parse_number`), sentence/clause splitting for local text chunking (`_chunk_text`), and filesystem-safe name sanitization (`_save_session`).
- `threading` ‚Äî `threading.Lock` (`_mc_lock`, guarding lazy model init against races), `threading.Event` (`_cur_stop`, per-voice-session stop flag), `threading.Thread` (daemon threads for the voice worker and its 1-second delayed start).
- `time` ‚Äî `time.sleep`, `time.time()` for timeouts/deadlines throughout (idle reminders, gesture-poll deadlines, chunk playback pacing).
- `cv2` (OpenCV, imported defensively with `_CV2_OK` flag) ‚Äî local fallback camera capture: `cv2.VideoCapture`, `cv2.CAP_V4L2`/`cv2.CAP_ANY` backend constants, `cv2.cvtColor` (BGR‚Üígray), `cv2.Laplacian` (sharpness/focus scoring via variance of the Laplacian), `cv2.imencode` (JPEG encoding with explicit quality parameter).
- `orangepi_client` (imported as `mc`, defensively with `_MC_OK` flag) ‚Äî not third-party but an internal shared library reused unchanged: supplies `capture_best_frame_local`, `voice_listen_loop`, `listen`, `init_cues`, `auto_detect_all`, `load_models`.

No `numpy` or `PIL` is imported directly in this file (OpenCV frames are handled as raw `ndarray`/`bytes` without explicit numpy calls in this module).

#### 1.4 Key Classes / Functions

- `OCRReader(Feature)` ‚Äî `name="ocr"`, `title="Book reader"`; `__init__` sets `self._session_counter = 0` (incremented once per `run()` invocation, used to name unnamed sessions uniquely across repeated feature activations); `run(ctx)` is the entire feature body (no return value; side effects: TTS speech, camera capture, network I/O, disk writes to `~/ocr_sessions`).
- `_srvspeak(ctx, fb, text) -> None` / `_play_wav_b64(fb, b64) -> float` ‚Äî server-TTS helpers with local fallback, described above.
- `_ensure_mc(fb) -> bool` ‚Äî idempotent, thread-safe lazy loader for the shared voice/camera client; returns whether it succeeded.
- `_capture_jpeg_cv2() -> bytes | None`, `_capture_frame(fb) -> bytes | None` ‚Äî capture fallback chain.
- `_parse_number(text) -> int|None`, `_classify(text) -> str|None` ‚Äî voice NLU helpers.
- `_voice_worker(abort, voice_q, stop_ev) -> None` ‚Äî thread target delegating to `mc.voice_listen_loop`.
- `_wait_gesture(ctx, timeout) -> str|None`, `_drain(q) -> None` ‚Äî queue polling utilities.
- `_chunk_text(text) -> list[str]`, `_chunk_dur(chunk) -> float` ‚Äî local text chunking/timing fallback when the server doesn't supply `chunks`/`chunk_wavs`.
- `_reading_order`, `_next_key`, `_page_label`, `_missing_pages` ‚Äî page-ordering/bookkeeping helpers over the `pages` dict.
- `_save_session(name, pages_list) -> str` (path), `_find_session(query) -> dict|None`, `_pages_from_session(data) -> (pages, next_idx)`, `_startup_summary() -> str` ‚Äî session persistence layer, pure file/JSON I/O under `SESSIONS_DIR = ~/ocr_sessions`.
- Nested closures inside `run()`: `_voice_on/_voice_off`, `_get_cmd`, `_session_stats`, `_autosave`, `_after_read`, and the nested function `_read_pages(start_key) -> str` (the page-reading sub-state-machine).

#### 1.5 Concrete Scenarios

- **Normal successful read**: user says "scan" ‚Üí capture succeeds ‚Üí server returns `text`, `page`, `chunks`, `chunk_wavs`, `announcement_wav` ‚Üí announcement plays ‚Üí page stored and read chunk-by-chunk with WAV audio; gestures allow pause/skip; page-complete triggers autosave and "Page done, next is page N" transition, or "All pages read" if session is exhausted.
- **No text/blank page**: empty `text` field ‚Üí "No text found. Hold page 30 to 40 centimetres..." ‚Üí no page stored, returns to scan-wait loop; separately, inside `_read_pages`, if a loaded page has an empty `chunks` list, it announces "Page appears blank." and skips to the next stored page.
- **Blurry/poor image quality**: handled upstream inside `mc.capture_best_frame_local()` via `MIN_SHARPNESS` rejection (returns `None` if the best of several sampled frames is still below the sharpness threshold) ‚Äî surfaces to the user identically to "camera unavailable" ("Camera error. Check USB camera.").
- **Camera unavailable**: both `mc.capture_best_frame_local()` and `_capture_jpeg_cv2()` return `None` (no device opens across `CAMERA_INDICES`/`/dev/video*` or all read attempts fail) ‚Üí `_capture_frame` returns `None` ‚Üí feature speaks "Camera error. Check USB camera." and loops back to voice-on/scan-wait without consuming a page slot.
- **Server timeout/unreachable**: `ctx.link.send("ocr", ...)` returns `None` (per `ServerLink.send`'s documented `-> dict | None` contract, e.g. on `OSError`/`TimeoutError` or connect failure) ‚Üí local-only `fb.speak("Server not reachable.")` (deliberately not routed through `_srvspeak`, since the server is known to be down) ‚Üí returns to scan-wait loop, page not stored, no crash.
- **Repeated triggers / debounce**: the gesture queue is drained (`_drain(gq)`) at feature entry and again immediately before each capture/read segment to discard stale gestures (e.g. the very gesture that opened the feature); voice is explicitly muted (`_voice_off()`) during capture/processing so a stray "scan" utterance mid-processing can't re-trigger; rescanning an already-seen page number is detected via the `("num", n)` key collision and explicitly announced ("Page N rescanned. Replacing.") rather than silently duplicating.
- **Abort gesture mid-session**: `ctx.abort` is checked at nearly every loop boundary (outer scan-wait loop, page-reading loop, chunk-playback deadline loop, paused sub-loop); the `finally` block still runs, autosaving and announcing the save summary (with missing-page warnings) even on abort, so an interrupted session is not lost.

#### 1.6 Integration Points

- Implements `features.base.Feature`/`FeatureContext` exactly as documented in ¬ß0; `hub.py` selects and drives it via `run(ctx)` and only intervenes by setting `ctx.abort` or feeding `ctx.gesture_queue`.
- All server traffic flows through `ctx.link` (`net.client.ServerLink`), tagged with two distinct `feature` values from this one Python file: `"ocr"` (scan/OCR requests) and `"tts"` (speech synthesis requests) ‚Äî meaning the server-side dispatcher routes to (at least) two handlers, inferred as `handlers/ocr.py` (expects `{"type": "scan", "frame": <base64 jpeg>}`, returns `text`/`page`/`chunks`/`chunk_wavs`/`announcement_wav`) and `handlers/tts.py` (expects `{"text": <str>}`, returns `{"ok": bool, "audio": <base64 wav>}`).
- Reuses the shared `orangepi_client` module identically to `money_recognition.py`, including the cross-feature `MoneyRecognition._models_ready` check to avoid double-loading Whisper ‚Äî a direct code-level dependency between the two feature files.

---

### 2. features/money_recognition.py ‚Äî Currency Reader Feature

#### 2.1 Purpose and Role

`MoneyRecognition` (`name="money"`, `title="Money recognition"`) lets a visually-impaired user identify banknote denominations by voice-triggered camera capture. Per its own docstring, it is a "thin orchestration layer" ‚Äî nearly all real logic (VAD, Whisper STT, camera capture, Piper/espeak TTS, earcons) lives in the pre-existing `orangepi_client.py` (`mc`) and is reused unchanged; the only architectural change from a presumably older standalone client is the transport: instead of `orangepi_client.py` owning its own raw socket, messages are routed through the hub's shared `ServerLink`, tagged with the `"money"` feature key so the server dispatches them to its money-recognition helper.

#### 2.2 End-to-End Pipeline Walkthrough

**Activation**: `run(ctx)` first calls `self._ensure_ready()`, a `MoneyRecognition`-class-level (not instance) idempotent initializer using the class attribute `_models_ready` as a guard, invoking `mc.init_cues()` (loads audio earcons), `mc.auto_detect_all()` (auto-detects camera/mic/audio-output devices), and `mc.load_models()` (loads Whisper STT and any local TTS voice) exactly once per process ‚Äî shared state that `ocr_reader.py` checks and reuses.

**Handshake**: sends `link.send("money", {"type": "hello"})`; if a response comes back, it is spoken via `mc._speak_resp(resp)` (reads `resp["tts"]` text and optional `resp["audio"]` base64 WAV, falling back to local espeak if no audio is present) followed by `mc.wait_speaking()` (blocks until the speech finishes playing).

**Main loop** (runs until `abort.is_set()`):
1. `text, _audit = mc.listen()` ‚Äî blocking voice capture + Whisper transcription (with internal retries per `orangepi_client.py`'s `listen(retries=5)` signature); the `_audit` value is discarded here.
2. If `abort` fired during listening, break; if no text was recognized, `continue` (silently loop back to listening).
3. Base payload: `{"type": "voice", "text": text}`.
4. **Conditional frame capture**: only if the transcript contains any of `mc.SCAN_TRIGGERS` (a curated word set ‚Äî `"scan"`, `"rescan"`, `"redo"`, `"capture"`, `"snap"`, `"shoot"`, `"photo"`, `"picture"`, `"frame"`, multi-word variants like `"take picture"`/`"scan again"`/`"do over"`, and even the colloquial `"yalla"` ‚Äî deliberately excluding confirmation words like "yes"/"no"/"ok" so that confirming an amount never accidentally re-fires the camera): speaks "Hold the bill steady. Capturing now.", waits for speech to finish, calls `mc.capture_best_frame_local()` (same OpenCV capture/sharpness-scoring routine described in ¬ß1.2/¬ß1.4 above ‚Äî opens the configured camera device, warms up, samples frames for `CAM_CAPTURE_SEC`, scores by Laplacian variance, rejects below `MIN_SHARPNESS`). On `None` (capture failure), speaks "Camera error. Could not capture a frame. Please try again." and `continue`s the loop without sending anything to the server. On success, plays the shutter earcon `mc.play_cue(mc._CUE_SHOT)`, speaks "Captured. Analyzing now.", and adds `payload["frame"] = jpeg` (raw JPEG `bytes`).
5. **Send to server**: `resp = link.send(self.name, payload)` i.e. `link.send("money", {"type": "voice", "text": <transcript>, "frame": <jpeg bytes, only if scan-triggered>})`. As with OCR, `ServerLink.send()` transparently base64-encodes the `frame` bytes before wire transmission, and always injects `"feature": "money"` into the outgoing JSON.
6. **Response handling**: `resp is None` (connection/transport failure) ‚Üí "Connection lost. Returning to the menu." ‚Üí break out of the feature entirely (return to hub menu). Otherwise `mc._speak_resp(resp)` + `mc.wait_speaking()` speaks whatever `resp["tts"]`/`resp["audio"]` the server supplied (this is the sole mechanism for surfacing the recognized denomination, e.g. presumably "That looks like a twenty dollar bill" style text/audio, though the exact wording is server-generated and not visible in this file). If `resp.get("quit")` is truthy, the loop breaks (server-driven session termination, e.g. after a user says "done"/"exit" and the server acknowledges).
7. **Exit**: if the loop ended because `abort` was set (rather than a server-issued `quit`), speaks "Money recognition aborted." as a final local cue.

**Expected server response shape**: `{"tts": <str, optional>, "audio": <base64 wav, optional>, "quit": <bool, optional>}` ‚Äî consumed uniformly by `mc._speak_resp` for both the initial "hello" handshake and every subsequent voice/scan turn. This is a conversational, multi-turn protocol: the server appears to hold state per-connection (e.g. "did you mean $20, say yes or no") since the same `"money"` feature tag is reused turn after turn with plain `{"type": "voice", "text": ...}` messages for confirmations, and only includes a `frame` when the user's speech contains a scan trigger. This implies a stateful server-side handler, most plausibly `handlers/money.py`, that: on `"hello"` returns a greeting/menu prompt; on `"voice"` without `"frame"` treats `text` as a spoken confirmation/command against its own internal conversation state; on `"voice"` with `"frame"` decodes the base64 image, runs a currency-classification model (likely a CNN/vision model trained on banknote denominations), and returns a natural-language `tts` result (optionally pre-synthesized `audio`), plus `quit` when the interaction is complete.

#### 2.3 External / Third-Party Libraries

- `time` ‚Äî imported but not directly called within this file's visible logic (all timing/sleeping is delegated into `orangepi_client.py`); likely vestigial or reserved for future use in this thin wrapper.
- `orangepi_client` (as `mc`) ‚Äî the real workhorse, supplying: `init_cues`, `auto_detect_all`, `load_models`, `_speak_resp`, `wait_speaking`, `listen`, `SCAN_TRIGGERS`, `capture_best_frame_local`, `play_cue`, `_CUE_SHOT`, `speak`. None of OpenCV/numpy/base64/etc. are imported directly by `money_recognition.py` itself ‚Äî they are encapsulated entirely inside `orangepi_client.py`.
- `features.base` ‚Äî `Feature`, `FeatureContext` (the contract described in ¬ß0).

#### 2.4 Key Classes / Functions

- `MoneyRecognition(Feature)`:
  - Class attributes: `name = "money"`, `title = "Money recognition"`, `_models_ready = False` (class-level flag, shared across instances/invocations within one process ‚Äî deliberately not an instance attribute, matching the "load once per process" comment).
  - `_ensure_ready(self) -> None`: idempotent model/device initializer; no return value; side effects are entirely inside `orangepi_client.py` (loading Whisper into memory, opening/probing audio and camera devices, setting `MoneyRecognition._models_ready = True`).
  - `run(self, ctx: FeatureContext) -> None`: the entire feature loop described in ¬ß2.2; no return value; side effects are speech output, camera capture, and network I/O via `ctx.link`.

#### 2.5 Concrete Scenarios

- **Normal successful currency read**: user says e.g. "scan this bill" ‚Üí capture succeeds ‚Üí server returns a `tts` describing the denomination ‚Üí spoken aloud; loop continues listening for the next command (e.g. "scan another one" or "done").
- **No currency detected / low-confidence**: not explicitly branched in this file ‚Äî entirely delegated to the server's `tts` text (e.g. the server likely returns something like "Could not identify the note, please try again" as ordinary `tts`, handled by the same `mc._speak_resp(resp)` call as a successful read). The client has no special-case logic for this; it is transparent to whatever the server decides to say.
- **Blurry/poor image quality**: handled by the same `mc.capture_best_frame_local()` sharpness-rejection logic as OCR (rejects the whole capture below `MIN_SHARPNESS`, returning `None`), producing the "Camera error. Could not capture a frame. Please try again." message and no server round-trip at all ‚Äî the frame is never sent to the server if too blurry.
- **Camera unavailable**: `capture_best_frame_local()` returns `None` when no `/dev/video*` device opens ‚Üí same "Camera error..." message; the voice-only conversation (non-scan turns) is unaffected since camera is only touched on scan-trigger words.
- **Server timeout/unreachable**: `link.send(...)` returns `None` ‚Üí "Connection lost. Returning to the menu." ‚Üí the feature's `run()` returns, handing control back to the hub (implying the socket/hub layer will need to reconnect before the next feature activation).
- **Repeated triggers/debounce**: `SCAN_TRIGGERS` is deliberately disjoint from confirmation vocabulary (yes/no/ok are excluded), so a user confirming "yes, that's right" mid-conversation never accidentally re-triggers the camera; each loop iteration blocks on a fresh `mc.listen()` call, naturally rate-limiting/debouncing by virtue of requiring a complete new utterance per turn ‚Äî there is no explicit cooldown timer in this file.
- **Abort mid-conversation**: checked both before entering `mc.listen()` and immediately after it returns; a scan-trigger capture is not separately abort-checked mid-capture (relies on `capture_best_frame_local()`'s own internal loop, which is not abort-aware in this file's visible code ‚Äî an abort during active capture would only be honored once capture returns and control returns to the `while not abort.is_set()` loop head).

#### 2.6 Integration Points

- Implements `Feature`/`FeatureContext` identically to OCR; the hub treats it as any other menu-selectable feature.
- Uses `ctx.link.send("money", payload)`; the `"feature": "money"` tag is injected transparently by `ServerLink`. Server-side, this maps to an inferred `handlers/money.py` capable of stateful multi-turn dialogue (`hello` / `voice`-only / `voice`+`frame`), unlike OCR's stateless single-shot `scan` request.
- Shares the `orangepi_client` singleton-style model/device initialization with `ocr_reader.py` via the `_models_ready` class flag ‚Äî `ocr_reader.py`'s `_ensure_mc()` explicitly imports `MoneyRecognition` and checks `MoneyRecognition._models_ready` to skip a redundant Whisper load, making this file a de facto shared initialization owner when Money Recognition is used before Book Reader in the same session.

---

### 3. features/programmable.py ‚Äî Programmable Gestures Feature

#### 3.1 Purpose and Role

`ProgrammableGestures` (`name="programmable"`, `title="Programmable Gestures"`) is a deliberately inert placeholder/registry entry, not a working feature in the conventional sense. Per its docstring, toggling it "on" causes the hub's own state machine to short-circuit directly into a dedicated `PROGRAMMABLE` state that owns all scrolling/re-binding UI logic internally ‚Äî `ProgrammableGestures.run()` is documented as "never called." It exists purely so that: (a) it appears in the gesture-enrollment walkthrough (letting the user assign a physical gesture to open the programmable-gestures panel), and (b) it appears as a selectable row inside the Programmable panel itself, so its own opening gesture can be rebound like any other feature's gesture ‚Äî i.e., it is a self-referential registry citizen enabling the "rebind the gesture that opens gesture-rebinding" use case.

#### 3.2 Pipeline Walkthrough

There is no real pipeline: no camera capture, no server communication, no `ServerLink.send()` call. The `run(self, ctx)` method's entire body is `ctx.feedback.speak("Programmable panel is already open.")` ‚Äî a defensive message that would only ever be heard if the state-machine's short-circuit logic somehow failed and `run()` was invoked while the panel is already open (a guard against a hub-level bug or race, not a normal user-facing flow).

#### 3.3 External Libraries

None beyond the internal `features.base` import (`Feature`, `FeatureContext`). No `cv2`, no `base64`, no networking.

#### 3.4 Key Classes / Functions

- `ProgrammableGestures(Feature)` ‚Äî `name = "programmable"`, `title = "Programmable Gestures"`; `run(self, ctx: FeatureContext) -> None` ‚Äî single-line fallback speech, no other side effects, no return value of consequence.

#### 3.5 Scenario Interpretation

This is the "generic slot" the task asked about ‚Äî but rather than being a user-programmable plugin/scripting sandbox in the sense of user-authored code, it is inferred from the code and comments to be a fixed system feature acting as a menu-registry anchor for the hub's built-in gesture-rebinding UI (referred to elsewhere as the "Programmable panel" / `PROGRAMMABLE` state). Concretely, its scenarios are:
- **Normal use**: user performs the gesture bound to "programmable" ‚Üí hub's state machine detects `feature.name == "programmable"` (or equivalent) and enters `PROGRAMMABLE` state directly, bypassing `run()` altogether, presenting a UI (handled entirely in `hub.py`/state machine, not in this file) for scrolling through and re-binding gestures to features (including to `"programmable"` itself).
- **Degenerate/defensive path**: if `run()` is ever invoked (e.g. a hub dispatch bug, or the panel is reentered while already open), the sole behavior is to speak "Programmable panel is already open." and return immediately ‚Äî no loop, no abort-handling, no camera/server interaction, so there is nothing further to debounce, retry, or error-handle within this file.
- It is explicitly not a slot for arbitrary user scripting or a placeholder for a not-yet-implemented future feature in the plugin sense; it is fully implemented, just implemented elsewhere (in the state machine), with this class serving only as the registry/metadata carrier (`name`/`title`) that the enrollment and rebinding UIs need.

#### 3.6 Integration Points

- Technically satisfies `features.base.Feature` (inherits, defines `name`/`title`, implements `run`) purely so `hub.py`'s feature registry/enumeration (used for enrollment and the Programmable panel's own listing) can treat it uniformly with every real feature ‚Äî the polymorphism is exploited for listing/registration purposes even though the polymorphic `run()` call is intentionally dead code in normal operation.
- Has zero relationship to `net/client.py`/`ServerLink` ‚Äî it never touches `ctx.link`, so there is no corresponding server-side handler at all for the `"programmable"` feature key; unlike `"ocr"`, `"money"`, and `"tts"`, this name would never legitimately appear in a message the server receives.
- Its practical logic lives entirely in `hub.py`'s state machine (the `PROGRAMMABLE` state), which is documented elsewhere but referenced here as the true owner of scrolling/rebinding behavior.

---

### DIAGRAM GENERATION PROMPT ‚Äî OCR Reader, Money Recognition & Programmable Features

Draw three side-by-side vertical swimlane flowcharts sharing a common "Hub / State Machine" entry box at the top, each swimlane representing one feature class from features/base.py's Feature contract (FeatureContext with link, abort, feedback, gesture_queue). Lane 1, "OCRReader.run() ‚Äî name=ocr": show a loop starting at an idle "scan-wait" decision diamond fed by _get_cmd() (voice via mc.listen()/_classify() and gestures via _GMAP), branching to CAPTURE (_capture_frame ‚Üí mc.capture_best_frame_local() or cv2 fallback _capture_jpeg_cv2(), Laplacian-sharpness scoring), then an arrow labeled 'ctx.link.send("ocr", {type:"scan", frame:<jpeg bytes>}) ‚Üí ServerLink base64-encodes frame' pointing to a "handlers/ocr.py (inferred)" box, returning {text, page, chunks, chunk_wavs, announcement_wav} into a _read_pages() sub-loop with PAUSED/READING states and gesture controls (OCR_PAUSE, OCR_FWD, OCR_BWD, OCR_SCAN/NEXT), ending in _save_session() writing to ~/ocr_sessions/*.json; also show a parallel _srvspeak() helper calling ctx.link.send("tts", {text}) against an inferred "handlers/tts.py" box returning {ok, audio}. Lane 2, "MoneyRecognition.run() ‚Äî name=money": show _ensure_ready() (mc.init_cues/auto_detect_all/load_models, guarded by class flag _models_ready) then a loop of mc.listen() ‚Üí text ‚Üí conditional frame capture only if text matches mc.SCAN_TRIGGERS (via mc.capture_best_frame_local()) ‚Üí ctx.link.send("money", {type:"voice", text, frame?}) ‚Üí an inferred "handlers/money.py (stateful)" box returning {tts, audio, quit} ‚Üí mc._speak_resp(resp), looping until resp.get("quit") or ctx.abort. Lane 3, "ProgrammableGestures ‚Äî name=programmable": a small box showing the hub's state machine short-circuiting directly to a PROGRAMMABLE state (bypassing run() entirely) with only a dashed fallback arrow to run() labeled 'ctx.feedback.speak("Programmable panel is already open.")', and explicitly no arrow to any server handler. Use a distinct color for "server-side (inferred)" boxes versus "on-device (OrangePI)" boxes, and label every network arrow with the exact feature string and payload keys shown above.

SECTION 5 ‚Äî LIDAR ADAPTER & SLAM ENGINE

# LiDAR Adapter & SLAM Engine ‚Äî Detailed Technical Documentation

## Scope and Files Reviewed

This section documents two files that together form the perception/mapping core of the OrangePI assistive robot's LiDAR subsystem:

- `c:\Users\user\Desktop\OrangePI\lidar_adapter.py` (305 lines) ‚Äî low-level MS200 LiDAR serial driver and scan assembler.
- `c:\Users\user\Desktop\OrangePI\slam_engine.py` (924 lines) ‚Äî 2D SLAM engine (ICP odometry, Scan Context loop closure, pose-graph optimization, occupancy grid mapping, and a persistent named-room database).

Both files were read in full. A cross-check against recent git history ("voice diagnostics, connected rooms, fix kf.timestamp + remove load_room", "ignore stabilizer housing returns (MIN_OBSTACLE_M = 0.10 m)", "full 360¬∞ polar radar with corrected direction labels") is included, with explicit notes where the referenced constants/behaviors are **not** present in these two files (they evidently live in a consumer module, most likely `lidar_nav.py`).

---

## PART 1 ‚Äî `lidar_adapter.py`

### 1.1 Purpose and Role

`lidar_adapter.py` is the hardware abstraction layer for a Youyeetoo/3iRobotix **MS200** 2D LiDAR unit, communicating over a UART/USB-serial link. Its sole responsibility is converting a raw byte stream into validated, denoised `LaserScan` objects representing one complete 360¬∞ revolution. It performs **no** mapping, localization, or semantic interpretation ‚Äî that is entirely deferred to `slam_engine.py` and higher-level feature modules. It is the lowest layer in the perception pipeline: physical sensor ‚Üí adapter ‚Üí SLAM engine ‚Üí feature/handler code.

### 1.2 Full Pipeline Walkthrough (byte stream ‚Üí LaserScan)

1. **Physical framing (per MS200 manual, documented in the module docstring).** Each UART frame is a fixed 47-byte packet: header `0x54`, type byte `0x2C` (low 5 bits encode "12 points per packet"), 2-byte rotation speed (¬∞/s), 2-byte start angle (√ó0.01¬∞), 12√ó(2-byte distance in mm + 1-byte intensity), 2-byte end angle, 2-byte timestamp (unused/overridden), and a trailing CRC-8 byte computed over bytes 0‚Äì45.

2. **CRC validation ‚Äî `_crc8(data)`.** A precomputed 256-entry lookup table (`_CRC8_TABLE`) implements the manufacturer's CRC-8 polynomial. `_crc8` iterates each byte, XORing with the running CRC and indexing the table ‚Äî a classic byte-wise CRC-8 implementation. Used to reject corrupted frames before parsing.

3. **`MS200Adapter.__init__`** configures: `port`, `baud` (default 230400), an optional `rotation_deg` (mechanical mounting offset, converted to `rotation_rad`), `median_kernel` (forced odd via `max(1, k | 1)`), `max_jump_m` (outlier jump threshold, default 0.5 m), and `use_crc` toggle. It initializes a `bytearray` ring buffer (`_buf`), a `_packets` accumulator list for the in-progress sweep, a `_scan_started` sync flag, and a `_stats` dict tracking `frames_ok`, `frames_bad_crc`, `points_total`, `points_filtered`.

4. **`MS200Adapter.find_port(baud, timeout)`** (static) ‚Äî auto-detection helper. Globs `/dev/ttyUSB*` and `/dev/ttyACM*` (Linux/OrangePI device naming), opens each candidate, and sniffs the raw stream for the `0x54 0x2C` header signature within a timeout window. Returns the first matching port path or `None`. Purely diagnostic/bring-up tooling ‚Äî not used in the hot path.

5. **`start()` / `stop()`** ‚Äî open/close the `pyserial` `Serial` object, reset the input buffer on start, and print final `_stats` on stop for post-run diagnostics.

6. **`get_scan(timeout=2.0)`** ‚Äî the main blocking entry point for consumers. Loops reading up to 2048 bytes at a time from the serial port, appending to `_buf`, and calling `_process_buffer()` after each read until either a complete scan is returned or the timeout elapses (returns `None` on timeout ‚Äî this is the sensor-disconnected/no-data path).

7. **`_process_buffer()`** ‚Äî the frame-synchronization state machine:
   - Searches `_buf` for the `0x54` header byte; if the buffer is too short for a full 47-byte frame, it trims processed bytes and waits for more data.
   - Validates `frame[1] == TYPE_BYTE (0x2C)`, then (if `use_crc`) validates the CRC-8, incrementing `frames_bad_crc` and discarding on mismatch.
   - Unpacks rotation speed, start/end angle (with wraparound handling: `if end_angle < start_angle: end_angle += 360.0`), converts speed to `rpm = speed_dps / 6.0`.
   - Per-point loop (12 points/packet): computes `dist_m`, interpolates each point's exact angle by linear interpolation between start/end angle across the 12 samples, and applies **per-point validity filtering** ‚Äî a point is zeroed (`dist_m = 0.0`, treated as "invalid/no return") if `dist_m < MIN_DIST_M (0.03 m)`, `dist_m > MAX_DIST_M (12.0 m)`, or `intensity < MIN_INTENSITY (16)`. The comment notes intensity codes 0‚Äì15 are manufacturer-reserved error codes, not real low-confidence returns.
   - **Sweep synchronization**: until the first packet with `start_angle < 5.0¬∞` arrives, the adapter discards data (`_scan_started` gate) to align to a consistent revolution boundary. Once synced, it accumulates packets into `_packets` until a *new* near-zero-angle packet arrives with more than 20 packets already collected ‚Äî this signals a completed 360¬∞ revolution, triggering `_build_scan()`.

8. **`_build_scan(packets, rpm)`** ‚Äî assembles and cleans the full-revolution point set:
   - Flattens all packets into angle/range/intensity numpy arrays, sorts by angle (`np.argsort`).
   - **Median filtering**: applied only to points with `rng > 0.0` (valid points), using `scipy.signal.medfilt` with the configured odd kernel size (default 5), shrinking the kernel if the valid subset is smaller than the kernel.
   - **Jump/outlier filtering**: computes forward and backward absolute differences (`np.diff` with `append`/`prepend` to preserve array length) and zeroes any point where *both* the forward and backward jump exceed `max_jump_m` (0.5 m default) ‚Äî i.e., an isolated spike with no continuity to either neighbor is treated as noise. Increments `points_filtered` stat.
   - Applies the mechanical `rotation_rad` offset and wraps angles into `[0, 2œÄ)`.
   - Returns a `LaserScan` dataclass with `timestamp=time.time()` (wall-clock capture completion time) and the measured `rpm`.

9. **`MS200Adapter.to_xy(scan)`** (static) ‚Äî the final hand-off function to SLAM/consumers: filters out invalid (`ranges_m == 0.0`) points and converts polar `(r, Œ∏)` to Cartesian `(x, y)` sensor-frame coordinates via `r¬∑cos(Œ∏), r¬∑sin(Œ∏)`, returning an `(N, 2)` float32 numpy array (empty array, not `None`, if no valid points ‚Äî a "degraded/empty scan" case handled gracefully).

### 1.3 Third-Party / Standard Libraries

- `serial` (pyserial) ‚Äî UART communication: opening the port, setting baud rate, `reset_input_buffer()`, non-blocking-ish reads with a 0.05 s inter-read timeout.
- `struct` ‚Äî binary unpacking of little-endian uint16 fields (`struct.unpack_from("<H", frame, offset)`) for speed, angles, and per-point distances directly from the raw byte frame.
- `math` ‚Äî `radians()` for the mounting rotation offset; used alongside numpy for angle math.
- `time` ‚Äî `time.time()` for `LaserScan.timestamp` default and for `find_port`'s timeout deadline.
- `dataclasses` (`dataclass`, `field`) ‚Äî defines `LaserScan` as a lightweight typed record with `field(default_factory=time.time)` to avoid the classic mutable/stale-default pitfall.
- `typing` (`List`, `Optional`, `Tuple`) ‚Äî static type hints only, no runtime effect.
- `numpy` ‚Äî vectorized array storage/manipulation for angles, ranges, intensities; `argsort`, `diff`, `column_stack`, trig functions for XY conversion.
- `scipy.signal.medfilt` ‚Äî 1D median filter for range-noise suppression on valid points.
- `glob` (imported locally inside `find_port`) ‚Äî filesystem globbing for `/dev/ttyUSB*` / `/dev/ttyACM*` device discovery (Linux-only; consistent with OrangePI deployment).

### 1.4 Key Data Structures

- **`LaserScan`** (dataclass): `angles_rad` (float32 ndarray, radians in `[0,2œÄ)`), `ranges_m` (float32 ndarray, metres; `0.0` sentinel = invalid/filtered), `intensities` (uint8 ndarray), `timestamp` (float, sweep-completion wall clock), `rpm` (float, measured rotation speed). This is the canonical "one full scan" object.
- **Raw point tuple** (internal only): `(angle_deg, dist_m, intensity)` per LiDAR sample, held transiently in `_packets` before array-ification.
- **`(N,2)` XY point cloud**: the sensor-frame Cartesian representation returned by `to_xy()`, consumed directly by `slam_engine.py`'s `update()` and internally by ICP/occupancy-grid code.

### 1.5 Concrete Scenarios

- **Normal 360¬∞ scan (happy path)**: `get_scan()` reads chunks until `_process_buffer()` detects a sync boundary crossing after ‚â•20 packets, builds, filters, and returns a `LaserScan` typically containing on the order of a few hundred points (12/packet √ó dozens of packets per revolution, minus filtered invalid ones).
- **Very close return (near/below `MIN_DIST_M`)**: Any measured distance under 3 cm is zeroed at the per-point filtering stage in `_process_buffer` ‚Äî this is the adapter's *only* built-in proximity gate, and it is a hardware-rated minimum-range cutoff, not a robot-housing occlusion filter (see ¬ß3 "Cross-File Note" below regarding `MIN_OBSTACLE_M`).
- **Sensor disconnected / no data**: `get_scan(timeout)` simply times out and returns `None` if no valid full sweep assembles within the window; `_ser.read()` returning empty bytes repeatedly does not raise ‚Äî the caller must handle `None` (a natural "signal lost" indicator surfaced to `slam_engine.py`/consumers).
- **Noisy/erratic readings**: Handled by two independent mechanisms ‚Äî median filtering (smooths random single-sample jitter) and jump filtering (drops points that disagree sharply with *both* neighbors, e.g. specular reflections or interference spikes), each recorded in `_stats["points_filtered"]`.
- **Degraded/partial scans**: If CRC failures or bad framing drop many packets, `_build_scan` still executes on whatever packets were collected; if intensity/range filtering zeroes most points, `to_xy()` returns a small or empty XY array, which downstream code (`len(points) < 10` guard in `SLAMEngine.update`) treats as a skip-frame condition rather than a crash.
- **Bad frame types/misaligned bytes**: A header byte found mid-stream that isn't followed by `TYPE_BYTE (0x2C)` is silently skipped (`continue`), and buffer resynchronization naturally recovers on the next header occurrence.

### 1.6 Interface Exposed to the Rest of the Codebase

- `MS200Adapter.get_scan()` ‚Üí `LaserScan` is the primary handoff to whatever orchestration loop drives the robot (very likely `lidar_nav.py`, not read here).
- `MS200Adapter.to_xy(scan)` ‚Üí `(N,2)` float32 array is the direct input expected by `SLAMEngine.update(points, rpm)` in `slam_engine.py`.
- `LaserScan.rpm` is passed through to `SLAMEngine.update(rpm=...)` and stored in `SLAMResult.rpm`, presumably for diagnostics/telemetry (e.g., detecting motor stall) surfaced to voice/diagnostics features.
- No networking, JSON, or server-facing code exists in this file ‚Äî nothing here talks to the TCP feature server directly. Everything is consumed in-process by SLAM or navigation code, which in turn presumably serializes results toward `handlers/lidar.py` on the server side (not read, per instructions, but architecturally this is the natural boundary: adapter ‚Üí SLAM ‚Üí feature module ‚Üí server transport layer).

---

## PART 2 ‚Äî `slam_engine.py`

### 2.1 Purpose and Role

`slam_engine.py` implements a full 2D LiDAR SLAM stack: **scan-matching odometry (ICP)**, **Scan-Context-based loop closure**, **pose-graph optimization**, an **occupancy-grid map**, and a **persistent named-room database** enabling "return to a previously mapped room" behavior. It consumes `(N,2)` XY point clouds (as produced by `MS200Adapter.to_xy`) and produces a running robot pose estimate, an occupancy grid, and room-recognition results. It is a scan-matching / graph-SLAM system ‚Äî **not** a Kalman-filter-based SLAM (EKF-SLAM). This is an important clarification given the git history phrase "fix kf.timestamp": in this codebase, the token `kf` universally refers to **KeyFrame** instances (`self.keyframes`, `KeyFrame` dataclass, debug category `"KF"`), not "Kalman Filter." There is no Kalman filter class anywhere in either file. Motion estimation instead comes from Iterative Closest Point (ICP) alignment against a rolling submap.

### 2.2 Full Pipeline Walkthrough (points ‚Üí pose/map/room result)

**Entry point: `SLAMEngine.update(points, rpm=0.0)`**, called once per full scan, returns a `SLAMResult`.

1. **Frame bookkeeping**: increments `_frame_id`; pre-populates `result` with current pose/map/keyframes before any processing, so even an early-return path yields a valid (if unchanged) result object.

2. **Degenerate-scan guard**: `if len(points) < 10: return result` ‚Äî too few valid points (e.g., from a filtered/degraded adapter scan) causes the frame to be skipped entirely, logged via `DebugLog` category `"DBG"`.

3. **Bootstrap (first frame)**: On the very first accepted scan (`_initialized == False`), no ICP is attempted (nothing to align against). The scan is transformed to world frame via `_sensor_to_world(points, self.pose)` (pose is identity at start) and pushed into the submap ring buffer via `_push_submap`. This seeds the reference cloud for frame 2.

4. **Odometry via ICP against a submap** (all subsequent frames):
   - Current scan is projected into world frame using the *current* pose estimate.
   - `_get_submap()` merges the last `SUBMAP_KF_COUNT` (6) keyframe clouds into one array, randomly downsampling to `SUBMAP_MAX_PTS` (2500) points if larger ‚Äî this submap-vs-single-previous-scan design is explicitly called out in the code comments as a fix for "single-frame noise... causing cascading yaw drift."
   - `ICP.align(world_pts, submap)` returns a transform `T`, RMSE, and convergence flag, recorded into `result.icp_rmse` / `result.icp_converged`.
   - **Acceptance gating (two layers)**: first, `ok and rmse < ICP_ODOM_RMSE_MAX (0.12 m)`; second, even if ICP reports success, the recovered pose delta must pass **physical plausibility limits** ‚Äî `ICP_MAX_TRANS_M = 0.20 m` and `ICP_MAX_ROT_DEG = 6.0¬∞` per frame (calibrated for "a person walking ~1.5 m/s at an 80 ms frame period," per in-code comment). Deltas exceeding these are **clamped/rejected** (pose not updated) rather than applied, protecting against ICP mismatches causing teleportation.
   - If accepted, `self.pose` is updated additively and `result.pose` refreshed; the scan is re-projected to world frame with the corrected pose for subsequent map painting.

5. **Keyframe decision**: a new `KeyFrame` is added if none exist yet, or if translation since the last keyframe exceeds `KF_DIST_M (0.30 m)`, or rotation exceeds `KF_ANGLE_RAD (0.20 rad ‚âà 11.5¬∞)`. This throttles keyframe density ("less KF spam = cleaner graph," per header comment; this threshold was raised from 0.30 in a prior version already ‚Äî the note refers to a value already baked into `KF_DIST_M`).

6. **`_add_keyframe(points, result)`**:
   - Builds a Scan-Context descriptor (`self.sc.make(points)`), constructs a `KeyFrame(kid, pose, points, desc)` ‚Äî this is where the `timestamp` field is populated via its dataclass `default_factory=time.time`, i.e., each `KeyFrame` gets a fresh capture-time timestamp at construction with no possibility of stale/shared defaults.
   - Appends to `self.keyframes`, updates `_prev_kf`, pushes the keyframe's world-frame cloud into the submap buffer (enriching future ICP references).
   - Adds a **sequential pose-graph edge** between consecutive keyframes (`PoseEdge` with a diagonal information matrix `[100, 100, 50]` weighting x/y/yaw confidence).
   - If enough keyframes exist (`kid > LC_WINDOW`), triggers `_detect_loop`.

7. **`_detect_loop(query, result)`** ‚Äî Scan-Context (Kim, IROS 2018) loop closure:
   - Computes the query keyframe's ring-key (`sc.ring_key`, column-mean of the SC descriptor) and compares it against all keyframes *except* the most recent `LC_WINDOW (5)` (to avoid trivially matching very recent, still-overlapping frames).
   - **Ring-key pre-filter gate**: `RING_KEY_GATE = 0.50` (L2 distance) ‚Äî cheap coarse filter before the expensive full SC comparison.
   - **Full SC distance** (`ScanContext.distance`) computed for gate-passing candidates; accepted as a loop *candidate* if `d < SC_DIST_THRESH (0.25)`.
   - Best (lowest-distance) candidate is chosen, then **verified geometrically** via ICP alignment in world frame; loop accepted only if `ok and rmse <= ICP_LOOP_RMSE_MAX (0.30 m)`.
   - On acceptance: derives a refined relative pose, adds a high-confidence `PoseEdge` (info matrix `[200, 200, 100]`, i.e. loop edges are trusted twice as strongly as sequential odometry edges), and populates `result.loop_closed/from_kf/to_kf/sc_dist/icp_rmse`.
   - Triggers **`PoseGraphOptimizer.optimize()`** ‚Äî a nonlinear least-squares solve (`scipy.optimize.least_squares`, Levenberg-Marquardt) over all keyframe poses given all accumulated edges, minimizing Cholesky-weighted residuals of relative pose consistency. The first pose is held fixed (`x0[:3]` excluded from the optimization vector) as the graph's anchor/gauge fix. Corrected poses are written back into every `KeyFrame.pose`, and `self.pose` is snapped to the last (most recent) corrected pose.
   - **Map rebuild** (`_rebuild_map`): after any loop closure, the entire occupancy grid is zeroed and **repainted from scratch** using all keyframes' now-corrected poses, and the submap ring buffer is refilled from keyframe clouds. This is explicitly the fix for the "opening new rooms for the same place" / duplicated-room artifact mentioned in the module's changelog docstring ‚Äî without a full repaint, pre-correction wall traces at the old (wrong) angle would remain permanently baked into the grid alongside the corrected ones.

8. **Occupancy grid update** (every frame, independent of loop closure): `OccupancyGrid.update(pose, points)` performs log-odds ray tracing (Bresenham's line algorithm) from the robot's grid cell to each observed point's world-frame cell, decrementing free-space cells by `L_FREE (-0.40)` and incrementing the terminal (occupied) cell by `L_OCC (+0.85)`, clamped to `[L_MIN=-5.0, L_MAX=5.0]` log-odds. `to_image()` thresholds the grid into a 3-level 8-bit image (255=occupied `>0.5`, 0=free `<-0.5`, 128=unknown).

9. **Room re-entry check** (every `ROOM_CHECK_INTERVAL (5)` frames, only if rooms exist in the database):
   - Builds a fresh Scan-Context descriptor for the *current* raw scan (not just at keyframe time ‚Äî this is explicitly the second bug-fix mentioned in the header docstring: previously only keyframe-time checks were done, missing re-entry between keyframes).
   - `RoomDatabase.match_scan()` compares against every saved room's fingerprint set (ring-key gate at 0.50, then full SC distance against a mean fingerprint) using `ROOM_SC_THRESH (0.28)`.
   - Requires **3 consecutive matches to the same room name** (a small ring buffer `_room_match_buf`, capped at length 3) before confirming ‚Äî this debounces false positives from single noisy matches.
   - On confirmation, populates `result.room_match`, `result.room_match_score` (mean of the 3 scores), and `result.direction_to_room` (via `RoomDatabase.direction_to`), and logs a "RE-ENTRY CONFIRMED" message only on the *first* frame the match changes (`if room != self._last_room_match`), avoiding log spam on sustained matches.
   - Any non-match clears the buffer and the "last matched room" state.

### 2.3 Third-Party / Standard Libraries

- `json` ‚Äî serializing/deserializing `RoomDatabase`'s `index.json` (room metadata: name, origin pose, map file path, save timestamp).
- `math` ‚Äî trig for pose composition/inversion, Bresenham stepping, bearing normalization (`atan2`/`cos`/`sin` throughout).
- `os` ‚Äî imported but not directly invoked in visible logic beyond incidental path handling (superseded largely by `pathlib`).
- `time` ‚Äî `time.time()` for keyframe/room timestamps and ICP/optimization timing diagnostics (`dt = time.time() - t0`).
- `dataclasses` (`dataclass`, `field`) ‚Äî defines `Pose2D`, `KeyFrame`, `PoseEdge`, `RoomRecord`, `SLAMResult`.
- `pathlib.Path` ‚Äî `ROOMS_DIR = Path("slam_rooms")`, directory creation (`mkdir(exist_ok=True)`), and file path construction for room grid/fingerprint files.
- `typing` (`Dict`, `List`, `Optional`, `Tuple`) ‚Äî type hints only.
- `numpy` ‚Äî the computational backbone: point-cloud transforms, SVD (`np.linalg.svd`) for ICP's rigid-transform solution, Cholesky (`np.linalg.cholesky`) for pose-graph residual weighting, occupancy grid array, Scan-Context descriptor construction (`np.maximum.at` for scatter-max binning), array save/load (`np.save`/`np.load`) for persisted rooms.
- `scipy.optimize.least_squares` ‚Äî Levenberg-Marquardt nonlinear solver for pose-graph optimization.
- `scipy.spatial.KDTree` ‚Äî nearest-neighbor lookup for CPU-based ICP correspondence search.
- `cupy` (**optional**, guarded by `try/except`) ‚Äî GPU-accelerated array operations mirroring the numpy ICP/Scan-Context code paths; a real GPU array allocation (`cp.array([1.0])`) is attempted at import time to confirm actual CUDA availability, not just import success, before setting the global `_GPU` flag. Falls back cleanly to CPU-only (`cp = None`) if unavailable ‚Äî relevant since the OrangePI target may or may not have a usable CUDA GPU.

### 2.4 Key Classes/Functions

- **`Pose2D(x, y, yaw)`** ‚Äî SE(2) pose as a dataclass with `as_matrix()` (3√ó3 homogeneous transform), `compose(other)` (transform chaining via matrix multiply, extracting yaw via `atan2`), `inverse()` (closed-form SE(2) inverse), `distance_to(other)` (Euclidean).
- **`KeyFrame(id, pose, points, sc_desc, timestamp)`** ‚Äî a saved scan snapshot: sequential integer `id`, `Pose2D` at capture time, raw sensor-frame `points` (copied, not referenced, to prevent aliasing bugs), its Scan-Context descriptor, and a `time.time()`-stamped capture time via `default_factory`.
- **`PoseEdge(i, j, rel_pose, info)`** ‚Äî a pose-graph constraint between keyframe indices `i`,`j`: relative `Pose2D` and a 3√ó3 information (inverse-covariance-like) matrix controlling optimizer trust weighting.
- **`RoomRecord(name, origin_pose, sc_fingerprints, map_file, saved_at)`** ‚Äî a persisted named room: the pose at save time, a list of representative SC descriptors ("fingerprints"), and the path to its `.npy` occupancy grid file.
- **`SLAMResult`** ‚Äî the per-frame output contract: current `pose`, reference to the live `OccupancyGrid`, `keyframes` list, ICP stats (`icp_rmse`, `icp_converged`), loop-closure stats (`loop_closed`, `loop_from_kf`, `loop_to_kf`, `loop_sc_dist`, `loop_icp_rmse`), room stats (`room_match`, `room_match_score`, `direction_to_room`), and frame stats (`frame_id`, `n_points`, `rpm`).
- **`ICP`** ‚Äî `align(source, target, init=None)` returns `(T, rmse, converged)`; dispatches to `_icp_cpu` (KDTree correspondence + SVD rigid-fit, iterated to convergence or `max_iter=50`) or `_icp_gpu` (CuPy brute-force pairwise distance matrix instead of a tree, since CuPy has no KDTree). `_svd_step` is the shared Kabsch-algorithm rigid transform solver (mean-centering, SVD of cross-covariance, reflection correction via determinant check).
- **`ScanContext`** ‚Äî `make(points)` bins points into a `(nr=20, ns=60)` polar histogram (max radius 10 m) using scatter-max (`np.maximum.at`); `ring_key` reduces to a rotation-invariant descriptor (row means); `distance` finds the minimum cosine-similarity-style distance over all `ns` circular shifts (rotation-invariant matching), normalized by active-column count rather than fixed size ‚Äî the code comment explicitly frames this as a "fix" for sparse-scan bias; `mean_descriptor` averages multiple descriptors into one room fingerprint.
- **`PoseGraphOptimizer.optimize(nodes, edges, n_iter=20)`** ‚Äî builds residuals per edge (translation error in the edge-origin's local frame, plus wrapped angular error), Cholesky-weights them by the edge's information matrix, and solves via Levenberg-Marquardt, holding the first node fixed as the anchor.
- **`OccupancyGrid`** ‚Äî `update(pose, scan_xy)` (Bresenham ray-casting log-odds update), `to_image()`, `save`/`load` (`.npy` persistence). Class constants `L_OCC=0.85`, `L_FREE=-0.40`, `L_MIN=-5.0`, `L_MAX=5.0`.
- **`RoomDatabase`** ‚Äî `save_room` (subsamples up to 20 spread-out keyframes as fingerprints, persists grid + SC stack + index), `list_rooms`, `get_room`, `match_scan` (ring-key gated, mean-fingerprint SC distance, threshold default 0.28), `direction_to` (returns `(dx, dy, dist_m, bearing_deg)` in robot-relative frame, with explicit convention "0=forward, 90=left, -90=right").
- **`SLAMEngine`** ‚Äî top-level orchestrator; public API: `save_room(name)`, `load_room(name)`, `list_rooms()`, `direction_to_room(name)`, and the core `update(points, rpm)`.
- **Module-level helpers**: `_T_to_pose2d(T)` (extract x, y, yaw from a homogeneous transform), `_sensor_to_world(points, pose)` (rotate+translate a sensor-frame cloud into world frame).

### 2.5 The "kf.timestamp" Commit ‚Äî Analysis

No literal Kalman filter exists in this codebase; `kf` denotes `KeyFrame`. The most plausible reading of "fix kf.timestamp" against the current code is that `KeyFrame.timestamp` now correctly uses `field(default_factory=time.time)` (evaluated fresh per instance at construction) rather than a bare default value (which in a dataclass would be evaluated once at class-definition time and shared/stale across all instances ‚Äî a common dataclass pitfall). This is consistent with `LaserScan.timestamp` in `lidar_adapter.py` using the identical `field(default_factory=time.time)` pattern. Also notable: when `_detect_loop`/pose-graph optimization corrects a `KeyFrame.pose` in place, `KeyFrame.timestamp` is **not** touched ‚Äî which is correct, since timestamp should reflect original capture time, not pose-correction time. No other timestamp-consuming logic (e.g., velocity estimation, time-delta-based ICP weighting) exists in this file, so there is no live "clock issue" scenario beyond ensuring each keyframe's timestamp is accurate at creation.

### 2.6 The "remove load_room" Commit ‚Äî Analysis

The current file **still contains** `SLAMEngine.load_room(name)` (lines 634‚Äì642) as an explicit, manually-invokable method. Since it is present, "remove load_room" almost certainly refers to removing an **automatic** call to `load_room` (e.g., previously auto-loading a default/most-recent room at `__init__` time), not the method itself ‚Äî `__init__` currently only lists known rooms via `self.db.list_rooms()` for a log message, with no automatic grid load. This shifts room loading to be an explicit, presumably voice/command-triggered action from a consumer module (`lidar_nav.py` or a voice handler), rather than implicit startup behavior ‚Äî likely to avoid loading a stale/wrong room map on boot.

### 2.7 Data Structures Summary

- **Scan** (as consumed here): raw `(N,2)` float64/float32 XY array in sensor frame (from `MS200Adapter.to_xy`); no wrapper object ‚Äî `slam_engine.py` works directly on ndarray inputs.
- **Obstacle**: not modeled as a discrete object in this file at all ‚Äî obstacles are implicit in the occupancy grid's log-odds cells (`grid > 0.5` = occupied) and in the raw point cloud used for ICP/mapping. There is no `Obstacle` class or explicit obstacle-list output; any "nearest obstacle" or "obstacle direction" semantics used by `lidar_nav.py` would have to be derived externally from `SLAMResult.map` or from `LaserScan.ranges_m` directly.
- **Room**: `RoomRecord` ‚Äî name, origin pose, list of SC fingerprint arrays, path to grid file, save time; persisted as `slam_rooms/index.json` + `slam_rooms/<name>.npy` (grid) + `slam_rooms/<name>_sc.npy` (stacked fingerprints).
- **Map**: `OccupancyGrid` ‚Äî a square float32 log-odds array (`size_m/resolution` cells per side, default 30 m / 0.05 m = 600√ó600), with `orig` as the metric offset mapping world coordinates to array indices; `to_image()` renders it as a standard 3-tone occupancy-grid image.

### 2.8 Concrete Scenarios

- **Normal 360¬∞ scan + mapping happy path**: `update()` receives a fresh XY cloud each revolution, ICP-aligns it to the submap, accepts the pose delta, conditionally adds a keyframe, paints the occupancy grid, and periodically checks for room re-entry ‚Äî steady-state behavior with no loop closures or room matches until revisiting known territory.
- **Very close obstacle below the minimum-distance threshold**: This file has **no explicit stabilizer-housing filter or `MIN_OBSTACLE_M` constant**. Any close-range self-return filtering must happen upstream in `lidar_adapter.py` (`MIN_DIST_M = 0.03 m`, a much smaller hardware-rated cutoff) or in a consumer not reviewed here. See cross-file note below.
- **Sensor disconnected / no data**: Not directly handled inside `slam_engine.py` ‚Äî it assumes it is always handed a points array. If the adapter's `get_scan()` times out and returns `None`, the caller (likely `lidar_nav.py`) must skip calling `SLAMEngine.update()` altogether that cycle; `SLAMEngine.update([])` would hit the `len(points) < 10` skip-guard safely if an empty array were passed instead.
- **Noisy/erratic readings**: Multiple layers of defense ‚Äî ICP's `ICP_ODOM_RMSE_MAX (0.12 m)` rejects poor alignments outright; the physical plausibility clamp (`ICP_MAX_TRANS_M`/`ICP_MAX_ROT_DEG`) rejects individually-converged-but-implausible jumps; the submap (merged multi-keyframe reference) dilutes single-frame noise; loop-closure candidates require both an SC-distance threshold *and* independent ICP geometric verification before acceptance, preventing false loop closures from noisy scan matches alone.
- **Multiple rooms / room-switching / mapping persistence**: `save_room` snapshots the *current* live occupancy grid and a spread of keyframe fingerprints under a name; `load_room` swaps the live grid's contents to a previously saved one (but does not reset `self.pose` or `self.keyframes` ‚Äî loading only affects `occ_map.grid`, meaning pose/keyframe state and the loaded historical map are not fully reconciled by this method alone). Room re-entry detection runs continuously in the background regardless of which room was last explicitly loaded, using the persistent fingerprint database ‚Äî this is what would power "you are now near/in the kitchen" type voice diagnostics in a consumer module.
- **Timestamp/clock issues**: As discussed, `KeyFrame.timestamp` is set once at creation via `default_factory` and never mutated, including through pose-graph corrections ‚Äî this is the correct, bug-free behavior; no other clock-dependent computation (e.g., dead-reckoning integration by elapsed time) exists in this engine, since motion estimation is purely scan-matching-based.
- **Degraded/partial scans**: Handled uniformly by the `< 10` point count guard at the top of `update()`; a scan with too few valid points contributes neither odometry, keyframes, nor map updates for that frame, but does not corrupt the running pose/map state.

### 2.9 Interface Exposed to the Rest of the Codebase

- **Primary API surface** for `lidar_nav.py` (or equivalent navigation feature): `SLAMEngine.update(points, rpm)` ‚Üí `SLAMResult` per scan cycle; `save_room(name)`, `load_room(name)`, `list_rooms()`, `direction_to_room(name)` for voice-driven room commands ("save this room as kitchen," "where is the kitchen").
- `SLAMResult.map` (an `OccupancyGrid`) and its `.to_image()` output are the natural payload for any visualization or server-side transmission (e.g., a "send current map" feature in a `handlers/lidar.py` server endpoint) ‚Äî though no networking/serialization to the TCP server occurs inside this file itself; that responsibility belongs to the consumer/handler layer.
- `SLAMResult.room_match` / `room_match_score` / `direction_to_room` are the structured signals a voice/diagnostics feature would consume to announce "you are back in the kitchen, 2.3 m northeast" style feedback.
- `DebugLog.tail(n)` exposes a rolling buffer of the last N log lines (categorized `ICP/KF/SC/LC/ROOM/MAP/POSE/DBG`) ‚Äî a natural hook for a diagnostics/voice-debug feature to surface "what is SLAM currently doing" without needing to parse stdout.
- Persisted room files under `slam_rooms/` are the only on-disk artifacts produced by this subsystem, and are the mechanism by which mapping state survives process restarts.

### 2.10 Cross-File Note: `MIN_OBSTACLE_M` Not Found

The recent commit "lidar: ignore stabilizer housing returns (MIN_OBSTACLE_M = 0.10 m)" references a constant and filtering concept that **does not appear verbatim in either `lidar_adapter.py` or `slam_engine.py`**. The closest related constant actually present is `MS200Adapter.MIN_DIST_M = 0.03` (3 cm), which filters returns below the sensor's physically rated minimum range ‚Äî a hardware-limit cutoff, not a robot-body/stabilizer self-occlusion filter. A dedicated 0.10 m housing-ignore threshold, and the "full 360¬∞ polar radar with corrected direction labels" feature, are therefore most likely implemented in `lidar_nav.py` (the consumer feature module explicitly mentioned in the task context but not reviewed here), which would post-filter or angularly mask `LaserScan`/`SLAMResult` data before rendering a polar radar display or computing obstacle-avoidance decisions. Documentation of that exact logic should be sourced from `lidar_nav.py` directly.

SECTION 6 ‚Äî SERVER CORE, WIRE PROTOCOL & CLIENT-SERVER INTERFACE LAYER
================================================================================

# Server Core, Wire Protocol & Client-Server Interface Layer

## 1. Overview and Scope

This section documents the interface backbone of the Smart Glove system's laptop-side "feature server": the TCP entry point (`feature_server.py`), the wire-level framing protocol (`protocol.py`), the handler contract (`handlers/base.py`, `handlers/__init__.py`), and the built-in text-to-speech infrastructure (`tts.py`, `handlers/tts_handler.py`). Together these files form the layer that every feature (money recognition, OCR, LiDAR navigation, TTS) plugs into, and they define ‚Äî jointly with `OrangePI/net/client.py`'s `ServerLink` on the robot side ‚Äî the single authoritative wire contract for the whole system.

Architecturally, the server is a single-process, multi-threaded, blocking-socket TCP dispatcher. It holds one long-lived TCP connection per OrangePi "hub," demultiplexes a stream of JSON messages tagged with a `feature` key, routes each to a per-connection, per-feature handler object, and returns a JSON reply that is automatically enriched with synthesized speech audio before being sent back down the same socket.

## 2. protocol.py ‚Äî Framed JSON-over-TCP Transport

### 2.1 Purpose

`protocol.py` is the lowest layer of the stack: a minimal, dependency-free (stdlib only) implementation of length-prefixed JSON message framing over a raw TCP stream. Its docstring is explicit that it "matches the OrangePi ServerLink and the original client/server wire format exactly" ‚Äî i.e., it is not an independent design, it is the server-side mirror of a wire format whose canonical definition is shared with `OrangePI/net/client.py`. It contains no business logic, no threading, and no state; it is called once per message send/receive by `feature_server.py`.

### 2.2 Wire Format

Every message, in either direction, is encoded as:

1. A 4-byte unsigned integer, big-endian (`struct.pack(">I", len(data))`), giving the exact byte length of the JSON payload that follows.
2. That many bytes of UTF-8-encoded JSON text (`json.dumps(...).encode("utf-8")`).

There is no delimiter, no checksum, and no protocol version field ‚Äî message boundaries exist purely because the receiver reads exactly 4 bytes, decodes the length, then reads exactly that many more bytes. This is a classic length-prefixed framing scheme chosen because raw `recv()` on a TCP stream socket has no message boundaries of its own (TCP is a byte stream, not a datagram protocol) ‚Äî this framing recreates discrete messages on top of it.

### 2.3 Functions

**`recv_exact(sock, n: int) -> bytes | None`**
Loops calling `sock.recv(n - len(buf))` until exactly `n` bytes have been accumulated in `buf`, or the peer closes the connection. If `sock.recv()` ever returns an empty bytes object (`b""`), that is TCP's signal that the peer has performed an orderly shutdown (FIN) ‚Äî `recv_exact` immediately returns `None` rather than looping forever or raising. This is the single most important primitive in the file: it converts TCP's stream semantics (partial reads are normal and expected) into an all-or-nothing read, and it turns "peer disconnected" into a sentinel value (`None`) rather than an exception, which the caller can check cheaply.

**`recv_msg(sock) -> dict | None`**
Composes on top of `recv_exact`:
1. Reads exactly 4 bytes for the length prefix. If `recv_exact` returns `None` (disconnect during the length read), `recv_msg` propagates `None` immediately.
2. Unpacks the length with `struct.unpack(">I", raw_len)[0]`.
3. Reads exactly `n` bytes for the body. If that returns `None` (disconnect mid-body), propagates `None`.
4. Attempts `json.loads(raw.decode("utf-8"))`. If decoding fails with `json.JSONDecodeError` or `UnicodeDecodeError`, it does **not** raise up to the caller ‚Äî it prints a diagnostic (`"[PROTO] recv_msg: malformed payload (...) ‚Äî dropping message"`) and returns `None`. This is a deliberate design choice: from the dispatch loop's point of view, a malformed message is indistinguishable from a clean disconnect ‚Äî both simply return `None`, and the caller's `if msg is None: break` treats both as "stop serving this connection."

**`send_msg(sock, payload: dict) -> None`**
Serializes `payload` with `json.dumps(...).encode("utf-8")`, prepends the 4-byte big-endian length via `struct.pack(">I", len(data))`, and writes the whole framed buffer in a single `sock.sendall(...)` call (guaranteeing the complete frame is transmitted or an exception is raised ‚Äî `sendall` will not silently partial-write). Any `OSError` raised by the socket layer (broken pipe, connection reset, etc.) is caught and re-raised as a `ConnectionError` with a descriptive message, using Python's exception chaining (`raise ... from e`) so the original `OSError` remains visible in the traceback. This function has no return value; success is defined as "no exception raised."

### 2.4 Error-Handling Philosophy

The module intentionally does two different things with two different failure classes:
- **Read-side failures** (short read / disconnect / malformed JSON) are turned into a `None` return value ‚Äî a soft, expected condition that the dispatch loop treats as "the peer is gone, wind down this connection."
- **Write-side failures** (socket-level `OSError` during `send_msg`) are turned into a raised `ConnectionError` ‚Äî because the server has already committed to producing a reply and cannot silently swallow a failed reply.

### 2.5 External Dependencies

`protocol.py` imports only two modules, both Python standard library:
- `json` ‚Äî for `dumps`/`loads`, serializing Python dicts to/from UTF-8 JSON text.
- `struct` ‚Äî for `pack`/`unpack` with format string `">I"` (big-endian unsigned 32-bit integer), implementing the 4-byte length prefix.

No third-party packages are used in this file.

## 3. handlers/base.py and handlers/__init__.py ‚Äî The Handler Contract and Registry

### 3.1 handlers/base.py ‚Äî The Interface

This file defines the single abstract contract every feature must satisfy:

```
class FeatureHandler:
    name: str = "base"
    def handle(self, msg: dict) -> dict:
        raise NotImplementedError
```

Key facts about this contract, drawn directly from the module docstring and code:
- It is a plain Python class, not an `abc.ABC`/`abstractmethod` ‚Äî `NotImplementedError` is the enforcement mechanism, checked only at call time, not at class-definition or instantiation time.
- `name` is a class attribute intended as a self-documenting label matching the dispatch key (though the actual dispatch key used by `feature_server.py` is the dictionary key in `FEATURE_HANDLERS`, not this attribute ‚Äî `name` is descriptive/cosmetic, not functionally load-bearing for routing).
- **Lifecycle contract**: "One handler instance is created PER CONNECTION PER FEATURE, so each handler can hold its own session state." This is a critical architectural detail ‚Äî a handler is not stateless/functional; it is instantiated once when a given feature is first invoked on a given TCP connection, and that same instance receives every subsequent message for that feature on that connection until the feature signals `"quit": true`. This lets a feature (e.g., money recognition) hold multi-turn state (e.g., "last detected currency," "awaiting rescan confirmation") across several request/response round trips without any session ID being threaded through messages ‚Äî the socket identity + feature name is the session key.
- **Method contract**: `handle(self, msg: dict) -> dict`. Input is the fully decoded message dictionary (including the `feature` key, since nothing strips it before dispatch). Output must be a dictionary containing at minimum `{"tts": str, "quit": bool}`. `tts` is the text the server will speak/synthesize back to the user; `quit` tells the dispatcher whether this ends the feature's session.
- No `__init__` is defined in the base class, so subclasses are free to define their own constructors for per-session state, invoked with zero arguments (`cls()` in `feature_server.py`).

### 3.2 handlers/__init__.py ‚Äî Empty Package Marker

This file was read and confirmed to be **completely empty** (0 bytes). Contrary to a plausible assumption, it does **not** contain any registry, `__all__` list, or re-export logic ‚Äî it exists solely so that `handlers/` is importable as a Python package (`import handlers`, `from handlers import money, ocr`, `from handlers.tts_handler import TTSHandler`, `from handlers.lidar import LidarHandler`). All actual registry/wiring logic lives in `feature_server.py` itself, in the module-level `FEATURE_HANDLERS` dict (see ¬ß4.4). This is an important correction to note for documentation accuracy: the "registry" is not a separate indirection layer inside the `handlers` package ‚Äî it is a flat dict literal maintained directly in the server's entry-point file, and the README explicitly instructs future feature authors to "register its class in `FEATURE_HANDLERS`" in `feature_server.py`, not in `handlers/__init__.py`.

### 3.3 How Concrete Handlers Plug In

Every concrete handler module (`handlers/tts_handler.py`, and by the same pattern `handlers/money.py`, `handlers/ocr.py`, `handlers/lidar.py`, documented in other report sections) follows an identical shape:
1. `from handlers.base import FeatureHandler`
2. `class XHandler(FeatureHandler): name = "x"` ‚Äî a subclass overriding `name` and implementing `handle(self, msg) -> dict`.
3. The class (not an instance) is imported into `feature_server.py` and inserted into the `FEATURE_HANDLERS` dict under its feature-name string key.

This is a textbook "class registry" pattern, but implemented with a hand-maintained dict rather than a decorator-based auto-registration mechanism (there is no `@register("tts")` decorator or metaclass magic anywhere in this codebase) ‚Äî adding a feature requires an explicit one-line edit to `FEATURE_HANDLERS` in `feature_server.py`, as the module docstring and README both state plainly ("Add a feature: 1. write handlers/<name>.py with a FeatureHandler subclass, 2. register its class in FEATURE_HANDLERS below. No change to this loop is needed.").

## 4. feature_server.py ‚Äî The TCP Server Entry Point

### 4.1 Purpose

`feature_server.py` is the process entry point (`if __name__ == "__main__": main()`) for the laptop-side server. Its docstring calls it "THE GENERAL SERVER on the laptop." It owns: CLI argument parsing, TTS engine configuration, model pre-loading, the listening socket lifecycle, per-connection thread spawning, per-message feature dispatch, response audio synthesis, and graceful shutdown on SIGINT/SIGTERM.

### 4.2 Startup Sequence (`main()`)

1. Parses CLI arguments via `argparse`: `--host` (default `0.0.0.0`), `--port` (default `9000`), TTS options (`--tts {auto,piper,sapi}`, `--piper-model`, `--sapi-voice` default `Zira`, `--sapi-rate`), and money-feature tuning options (`--model`, `--detect-conf`, `--box-conf`, `--reliable-conf`, `--imgsz`, `--tta`, `--blur-radius`).
2. Calls `tts.configure(...)` to set module-level TTS globals, then `tts.init_tts()` to select/validate the SAPI voice and print engine readiness.
3. Spawns a **daemon background thread** running `ocr.preload` so the OCR model loads asynchronously and does not block server startup or the first client connection.
4. Calls `money.configure(...)` to push CLI-tuned thresholds into the money-recognition module (lazy YOLO model load happens later, on first scan, per the README).
5. Prints a startup banner listing registered features and money-model configuration.
6. Installs a `threading.Event` (`_stop`) and signal handlers for `SIGINT`/`SIGTERM` (`_request_stop`) that set the event ‚Äî this is the graceful-shutdown mechanism.
7. Creates the listening socket: `socket.socket(AF_INET, SOCK_STREAM)`, sets `SO_REUSEADDR`, `bind((host, port))`, `listen(5)` (backlog of 5 pending connections), and `settimeout(1.0)` on the **listening** socket itself.
8. Speaks "Feature server ready." on the server's local speaker via `tts.local_speak`.
9. Enters the accept loop (¬ß4.3).
10. On loop exit (stop event set), closes the listening socket and prints a stop message.

### 4.3 Accept Loop and Concurrency Model

The concurrency model is **thread-per-connection**, using plain OS-level `threading.Thread` (not asyncio, not a thread pool/executor, not `socketserver`). The accept loop:

```
while not _stop.is_set():
    try:
        conn, addr = srv.accept()
        threading.Thread(target=handle_client, args=(conn, addr), daemon=True).start()
    except socket.timeout:
        continue
```

The 1-second timeout on the listening socket exists purely so the loop can periodically re-check `_stop.is_set()` between blocking `accept()` calls ‚Äî this is the standard pattern for making a blocking-accept loop interruptible without asyncio or `select`. Each accepted connection gets its own daemon thread running `handle_client`; because threads are daemonic, the process can exit even with hub threads still blocked on `recv()`, and an unlimited number of concurrent hub connections is supported (bounded only by OS thread/socket limits ‚Äî there is no connection cap enforced by the server itself, aside from the `listen(5)` backlog which only bounds *pending, not-yet-accepted* connections).

### 4.4 Per-Connection Message Loop (`handle_client(conn, addr)`)

1. Logs connection, registers the peer in `GloveState` (see ¬ß4.5).
2. Maintains a **local** `handlers: dict[str, object]` mapping feature name ‚Üí handler instance, scoped to this connection/thread only (this is what implements the "one handler instance per connection per feature" contract from `handlers/base.py`).
3. Loops calling `msg = recv_msg(conn)`. If `None` (disconnect or malformed frame), breaks out of the loop.
4. Extracts `feature = msg.get("feature", "money")` ‚Äî note the **default fallback is `"money"`** if the key is absent, not an error condition.
5. Calls `GloveState.touch(addr, feature)` to update session/metrics tracking.
6. Looks up `cls = FEATURE_HANDLERS.get(feature)`. If `None` (unregistered feature name), immediately replies with `{"tts": f"Unknown feature {feature}.", "quit": False}` via `_send_with_audio` and `continue`s the loop **without** touching the `handlers` dict ‚Äî the connection stays open and can still be used for other/valid features.
7. If the handler for this feature doesn't yet exist for this connection, instantiates it (`cls()`) and caches it in the local `handlers` dict, logging `"[ROUTE] new {feature} session for {addr}"`.
8. Invokes `handler.handle(msg)` inside a `try/except Exception`. On any exception: prints a full traceback (`traceback.print_exc()`), records an error count via `GloveState.error(addr, feature)`, and synthesizes a **graceful fallback response** `{"tts": f"{feature} error: {he}", "quit": False}` ‚Äî critically, **an exception inside a handler does not crash the connection or the server**; it is caught, converted into a spoken error message, and the loop continues, keeping the session and socket alive.
9. Sends the response via `_send_with_audio(conn, resp)` (¬ß4.6).
10. If `resp.get("quit")` is truthy, removes the handler instance from the local `handlers` dict (ending that feature's session while the socket itself remains open for future features) and logs the session end.
11. On any exception escaping the whole loop (e.g., a network-level failure not caught by the inner try, or an unexpected error in `GloveState`/`_send_with_audio`), the outer `try/except Exception as e` catches and logs it, and the `finally` block unconditionally calls `GloveState.disconnect(addr)`, `conn.close()`, and logs disconnection ‚Äî guaranteeing socket and state cleanup regardless of how the loop terminated.

### 4.5 GloveState ‚Äî Server-Side Session/Metrics Tracker

A `classmethod`-only class (used as a namespaced global singleton, not instantiated) protected by a single `threading.Lock` (`_lock`) shared across all connection threads. It tracks:
- `_hubs: dict` keyed by `"ip:port"` string ‚Üí per-hub dict with `connected_at`, current `feature`, `feature_at` (timestamp of last feature switch), and `msg_count`.
- `_counts: dict` keyed by feature name ‚Üí `{"scans": int, "errors": int}`, incremented on every successful dispatch (`touch`) and every handler exception (`error`).
- `connect`/`disconnect`/`touch`/`error` mutate this state under the lock; `snapshot()` returns a deep-ish copy (per-hub dict copies plus computed `uptime_s` and `feature_age_s`) for external inspection (e.g., a status/monitoring feature, though no HTTP/status endpoint is present in this file itself ‚Äî it appears to exist for introspection by another part of the system, possibly a status feature elsewhere).

This is pure in-memory, non-persistent bookkeeping ‚Äî it does not survive server restart and has no file or database backing.

### 4.6 Response Assembly and TTS Injection (`_send_with_audio`)

Before any reply is written to the socket, `_send_with_audio(conn, resp)` performs cross-cutting TTS enrichment shared by **every** feature, not just the `tts` feature:
1. Reads `text = resp.get("tts", "")` from the handler's returned dict.
2. If non-empty: calls `tts.local_speak(text)` (spoken on the server operator's own machine/speaker, synchronous fire-and-forget), then `tts.synth_wav(text)` to render a WAV byte buffer plus the engine name actually used (`"piper"`, `"sapi"`, or `"none"`).
3. If synthesis succeeded, base64-encodes the WAV and attaches it as `resp["audio"]`, logs a `[TTS]` line with size, and appends a metrics record (chars, engine, wav_kb, latency_ms, timestamp) to `handlers/tts_metrics.jsonl` via `_log_tts_metric`, itself protected by a separate `threading.Lock` (`_tts_metrics_lock`) to serialize concurrent file appends from multiple connection threads.
4. If synthesis failed (no engine available), logs that the client (OrangePi) will fall back to on-device `espeak`.
5. Finally calls `send_msg(conn, resp)` ‚Äî this is the **only** place any handler's response actually reaches the wire; individual handlers never call `send_msg` themselves.

This means every single feature response, regardless of which handler produced it, is uniformly passed through the shared TTS pipeline before transmission ‚Äî this is the concrete mechanism behind the README's claim that "the general server voices every feature's reply through the shared tts module."

### 4.7 External / Third-Party Library Usage in feature_server.py

Standard library: `argparse` (CLI parsing), `base64` (encoding synthesized WAV bytes for JSON transport), `signal` (SIGINT/SIGTERM handlers for graceful shutdown), `socket` (listening/accepting TCP connections), `threading` (per-connection threads, locks, the stop `Event`), `time` (timestamps for `GloveState` and TTS latency measurement), `json` (aliased `_json`, for the TTS metrics JSONL log), `os` (aliased `_os`, for building the metrics file path), `traceback` (imported locally inside the exception handler, for full stack trace logging on handler errors).

Local/project modules: `tts` (the shared synthesis module, ¬ß5), `protocol` (`recv_msg`, `send_msg`), `handlers.money`, `handlers.ocr`, `handlers.tts_handler.TTSHandler`, `handlers.lidar.LidarHandler` ‚Äî these four are the concrete feature implementations wired into `FEATURE_HANDLERS`.

No third-party networking, serialization, or concurrency libraries are used ‚Äî the entire server transport/concurrency stack is Python standard library.

## 5. tts.py ‚Äî Shared Text-to-Speech Rendering

### 5.1 Purpose and Role

`tts.py` is infrastructure shared by every feature handler, not a feature itself. Per its docstring: it renders any reply string to a natural-voice WAV, "lifted from the original server.py so the voice is identical," using two possible engines with a preference order ‚Äî Piper (neural TTS, cross-platform, external CLI) preferred, Windows SAPI (via COM automation) as fallback, plus a separate "local speak" path for audibly announcing text on the server operator's own machine (independent of what gets sent to the client).

### 5.2 Configuration State

Module-level globals, set once at startup via `configure()` (called from `feature_server.py main()` before `init_tts()`):
- `TTS_ENGINE` (`"auto" | "piper" | "sapi"`, default `"auto"`)
- `PIPER_MODEL` (filesystem path to a `.onnx` Piper voice model; empty string disables Piper)
- `SAPI_VOICE` (substring used to select a Windows SAPI voice by name, default `"Zira"`)
- `SAPI_RATE` (SAPI speech rate, -10 to 10, default 0)
- `_sapi_lock`, a module-level `threading.Lock`, because SAPI's COM object rendering is explicitly documented as "not thread-safe across clients." Since `handle_client` runs one thread per connection and every reply passes through `_send_with_audio` ‚Üí `tts.synth_wav` ‚Üí potentially `sapi_to_wav`, this lock serializes all concurrent SAPI renders across all client threads.

### 5.3 SAPI Path (Windows-only, best-effort import)

The whole SAPI block is wrapped in a top-level `try/except Exception` around `import win32com.client` and `win32com.client.Dispatch("SAPI.SpVoice")`. If this import/dispatch fails (e.g., non-Windows platform, or `pywin32` not installed), `_sapi_available` stays `False` and three no-op/stub fallback functions are defined instead (`_select_sapi_voice` becomes a no-op, `sapi_to_wav` always returns `None`, `local_speak` just prints instead of speaking) ‚Äî this makes the module importable and degrade gracefully on non-Windows systems, even though the README and requirements file frame this as a Windows-targeted deployment (`pywin32>=306 ; platform_system == "Windows"` is an environment-marker-gated dependency).

Key functions in this block:
- `_select_sapi_voice(substr)`: enumerates `_speaker.GetVoices()`, does a case-insensitive substring match against each voice's `GetDescription()`, and sets `_speaker.Voice` to the first match; logs all available voice names if no match is found, and keeps the OS default voice in that case.
