    `"Could not send the WiFi details to the relay board. Your WiFi has been
    restored."` ‚Äî the user is never left stranded off their home network.
  - **ESP32 loses its saved WiFi entirely** (router replaced, password
    changed): the firmware's `connectStation()` times out after 20 s and
    falls back to re-opening the `RelayCtrl-Setup` provisioning AP
    automatically ‚Äî the same pairing flow above simply runs again with a
    freshly generated (or reused) QR code.
  - **Two relay boards**: giving each board a distinct `device_id` in its
    provisioning payload (`relay01`, `relay02`, ...) lets `handlers/home.py`
    track them as separate registry entries; `HomeAutomation`/`RelaySwitch`
    as written target a single default board (the current 2-relay
    prototype), so a second board would need its `device_id` passed
    explicitly in the toggle payload ‚Äî a small, clearly-scoped extension
    point (`_resolve_device()` already accepts an explicit `device_id`).

8.6 DIAGRAM GENERATION PROMPT ‚Äî Home Automation (Relays + QR Provisioning)

Draw a three-column architecture diagram. Column 1 "OrangePi (features/home_automation.py)": show `HomeAutomation` (voice menu: pair/status/close) and two `RelaySwitch(1)`/`RelaySwitch(2)` boxes, each with their own bindable gesture via the existing `FeatureRegistry`/`GestureStore` (`FEAT:Relay 1`, `FEAT:Relay 2` keys in gestures.json ‚Äî no gesture_hub changes). Show a `_pair()` flow: camera capture -> `cv2.QRCodeDetector` decode -> `nmcli device wifi connect RelayCtrl-Setup` -> `POST http://192.168.4.1/provision` -> `nmcli connection up <original-profile>`. Column 2 "Feature Server (handlers/home.py)": a `HomeHandler` box with actions `toggle`/`status`/`list_devices`, an HTTP dashboard on port 8090 with routes `/`, `/qr/<device_id>` (PNG, calls `_generate_qr_png` using the `qrcode` package), `POST /esp/register`, `/metrics`; a device registry `home_devices.json` (device_id -> ip, relay_count, fw, last_seen). Column 3 "ESP32 (esp_relay_firmware/relay_controller.ino)": two states ‚Äî UNPROVISIONED (SoftAP `RelayCtrl-Setup`, `GET /info`, `POST /provision` saving to NVS via `Preferences` then rebooting) and CONNECTED (`GET /relay?ch=1&state=on|off|toggle` driving GPIO 26/27, `GET /status`, periodic `POST /esp/register` heartbeat every 30s). Draw arrows: Column1 <-> Column2 over the existing TCP ServerLink tagged `feature="home"`; Column2 <-> Column3 over plain HTTP on the home LAN; a dashed one-time arrow Column1 -> Column3 labeled "provisioning POST (only during pairing, bypasses the server entirely)". Annotate the QR JSON schema (`type, ssid, password, server_host, server_home_port, device_id, relay_count`) next to the QR PNG box since it is the single shared contract across all three columns.

================================================================================
SECTION 9 ‚Äî PERFORMANCE METRICS: LOAD TIME, LATENCY, RESPONSE TIME (ALL FEATURES)
================================================================================

SECTION 9 ‚Äî PERFORMANCE METRICS: LOAD TIME, LATENCY, RESPONSE TIME (ALL FEATURES)
===================================================================================

9.1 Goal

Every feature should have measurable, on-disk evidence of three numbers, so
the report can be filled in with real figures rather than estimates:

  - **Time to load** ‚Äî one-time cost of initializing a feature's heavy
    dependencies (Whisper/voice stack, YOLO model, OCR engine) the first time
    it's used in a process lifetime.
  - **Latency** ‚Äî wall-clock time between the OrangePi sending a request and
    the server receiving it (network + any queueing).
  - **Response time** ("processing time") ‚Äî time the server actually spends
    inside the feature's own handler producing a reply.

All of this is captured **on the server**, as newline-delimited JSON
(`.jsonl`) files under `server_app/handlers/`, and surfaced together on the
existing live dashboard's `/metrics` page (already used for OCR/Money/TTS ‚Äî
see Section 7 ‚Äî now extended, not replaced).

9.2 How Latency + Response Time Are Captured ‚Äî One Change Point for Every Feature

Rather than instrument OCR, Money, LiDAR, Home, and TTS individually (five
separate, easy-to-forget edits), the timing is captured **once**, centrally,
in `feature_server.py`'s `handle_client()` dispatch loop ‚Äî the single place
every feature's message already passes through:

  1. `OrangePI/net/client.py`'s `ServerLink.send()` now stamps
     `payload["_t_sent"] = time.time()` on every outgoing message, right next
     to where it already injects the `"feature"` key. This is a client-clock
     timestamp riding along inside the existing envelope ‚Äî no new message,
     no new round trip.
  2. `feature_server.py`'s `handle_client()` records `t_recv = time.time()`
     the instant a message is decoded, and computes
     `latency_ms = (t_recv - msg["_t_sent"]) * 1000` ‚Äî this captures network
     transit plus any time the message spent waiting in the OS socket buffer.
     (`latency_ms` is `None` if the sender didn't stamp the message ‚Äî keeps
     this backward-compatible with anything that predates the change.)
  3. It times the `handler.handle(msg)` call itself ‚Äî
     `processing_ms = (time.time() - t_recv) * 1000` ‚Äî this is the feature's
     true server-side response time, independent of network conditions.
  4. Both numbers, plus `feature`, `type`/`action`, and `ok` (whether the
     handler raised), are appended as one JSON line to
     `handlers/feature_metrics.jsonl` ‚Äî **for every single feature**, with
     zero code changes required inside `handlers/money.py`, `handlers/ocr.py`,
     `handlers/lidar.py`, `handlers/home.py`, or `handlers/tts_handler.py`.

This means the moment this change shipped, `feature_metrics.jsonl` started
filling in with real `latency_ms`/`processing_ms`/`total_ms` rows for OCR
scans, money scans, LiDAR map/pose/report messages, relay toggles, and TTS
requests alike ‚Äî a single, uniform, comparable table across every feature,
which is exactly the "for all features" requirement.

Client-side clock caveat worth noting in the report: `latency_ms` depends on
the OrangePi and server system clocks being reasonably in sync (no NTP sync
is enforced anywhere in this codebase); on a LAN with both clocks
free-running from the same recent boot this is normally a non-issue, but a
large or negative `latency_ms` value is a clock-skew symptom, not necessarily
a real network delay, and should be filtered/flagged before being quoted in
the report.

9.3 How "Time to Load" Is Captured ‚Äî Now Wired for Every Feature

Load time is inherently feature-specific (it's whatever expensive
one-time setup that feature does), so it's measured at the exact places on
each side that do this loading. As of this pass, every feature that has a
non-trivial load step reports it:

  Server-side (heavy ML models, load once per process):
    - `handlers/money.py`'s `_get_model()` (YOLO currency detector) now times
      the `from ultralytics import YOLO` + `YOLO(MODEL_PATH)` block and calls
      a local `_log_load_metric(ms, ok, device=...)` helper, which appends
      `{"feature":"money","type":"model_load","processing_ms":...,"ok":...,
      "device":"cuda"|"cpu"}` to `handlers/feature_metrics.jsonl` ‚Äî the same
      consolidated file `feature_server.py` writes per-request latency into
      (Section 9.2), so model-load rows and per-request rows sit side by side
      for the same feature.
    - `handlers/ocr.py`'s `_get_ocr()` (EasyOCR engine) does the identical
      thing under `"feature":"ocr"`.
    - Both wrap the import/construction in `try/except`: a load failure is
      logged with `ok: false` and the exception message under `error`,
      *then re-raised* ‚Äî the caller (a scan request) still sees the original
      exception and surfaces its normal error path; the metrics write never
      swallows or changes existing error behavior, it only observes it.

  Client-side (Whisper/voice stack, camera/mic auto-detection, Gemini client):
    - The shared helper `OrangePI/metrics.py` exposes
      `report_load(link, feature_name, ms, **extra)` and
      `report_action(link, feature_name, action, ms, **extra)`. Both are
      thin, best-effort wrappers around `link.send("metrics", {...})` ‚Äî
      wrapped in `try/except Exception: pass` so a metrics failure can never
      break the feature itself (mirrors `features/env_awareness.py`'s
      "server is optional" posture documented in Section 3).
    - `features/money_recognition.py`'s `_ensure_ready()` times the
      `mc.init_cues() / mc.auto_detect_all() / mc.load_models()` block and
      reports under `"money"`, only on the first real load per process
      (`MoneyRecognition._models_ready` short-circuits repeats correctly).
    - `features/ocr_reader.py`'s `_ensure_mc()` does the same under `"ocr"`.
    - `features/env_awareness.py`'s `_ensure_mc()` does the same under
      `"env"` for its shared voice-stack init, **and** `EnvAwareness.run()`
      separately times `genai.Client(api_key=...)` construction and reports
      it under `"env"` with `component="genai_client"` ‚Äî this isolates
      "how long does it take to stand up the Gemini client" from "how long
      does the voice stack take to load," since they can fail and degrade
      independently.
    - `features/lidar_nav.py`'s `_LidarVoice` (used by all four LiDAR
      feature classes) now accepts the active `ServerLink` and times its
      `WhisperModel("tiny", ...)` load, reporting under `"lidar"` with
      `component="whisper_tiny"` ‚Äî this only happens once per process since
      `_LidarVoice` loads its own Whisper instance per feature activation,
      so repeated LiDAR sessions in one boot will show one load entry per
      session (unlike Money/OCR/Env's process-wide singleton flags); this is
      a known asymmetry worth noting when comparing LiDAR's numbers against
      the other features' "loads once per process" figures.
    - `features/home_automation.py`'s `HomeAutomation.run()` reports its own
      `_ensure_mc()` load time under `"home"`, and additionally reports the
      **pairing** flow's total duration via `report_action(..., "pair", ms,
      ok=..., device_id=...)` ‚Äî the same helper used for a one-off timed
      action rather than a load event.

  Server-side sink for all of the above:
    - `handlers/metrics_handler.py` ‚Äî a tiny generic `FeatureHandler`
      (`name="metrics"`) that accepts any `{"event", "source_feature", "ms",
      ...}` payload and appends it, timestamped, to
      `handlers/client_metrics.jsonl`. It always replies silently
      (`{"tts": "", "quit": False}` ‚Äî never spoken) and is registered in
      `feature_server.py`'s `FEATURE_HANDLERS` exactly like every other
      feature.

9.3.1 Related Fix: Gemini Connectivity Reliability (Environmental Awareness)

While wiring `env_awareness.py`'s load-time metric, the Gemini integration
was hardened, since it had been unreliable:

  - `GEMINI_API_KEY_HARDCODED` ‚Äî a new constant at the top of
    `features/env_awareness.py` that, if non-empty, takes priority over the
    `GEMINI_API_KEY` environment variable and the `~/.env`/`~/keys.env` file
    lookup in `_load_api_key()`. This exists specifically for the case where
    `hub.py` runs as a systemd service (or any non-interactive launcher) that
    does not inherit the user's shell environment, so `export
    GEMINI_API_KEY=...` in `~/.bashrc` silently never reaches the process ‚Äî
    pasting the key directly into source guarantees it's always present. The
    constant is documented in-line with an explicit security note: a key
    committed to source control is exposed to anyone with repo access, so it
    should only be used on a private/local repo, and rotated immediately if
    the repo is ever made public.
  - **One-time self-test on startup**: right after `genai.Client(api_key=...)`
    is constructed (and timed for the load-time metric), `EnvAwareness.run()`
    now sends one throwaway `generate_content(model=GEMINI_MODEL, contents="Reply
    with the single word OK.")` call before the main loop starts. If this
    fails, the feature speaks the *actual* exception message (bad key, no
    network route, model name rejected, quota exceeded, etc.) immediately ‚Äî
    rather than only failing silently later on the user's first real scan ‚Äî
    and returns without entering the loop.
  - **Full tracebacks on every Gemini failure path**: the client-init,
    self-test, scan, and follow-up-question error handlers all now call
    `traceback.print_exc()` before speaking a (now more detailed) error
    message, so the OrangePi's console/systemd journal shows the complete
    stack trace for whatever `google-genai` exception occurred ‚Äî essential
    for diagnosing auth vs. network vs. quota vs. SDK-version problems, none
    of which were distinguishable from the previous generic "Gemini init
    error." wording alone.

9.4 Where the Numbers End Up (report-ready)

Four files under `server_app/handlers/` now exist specifically to answer
"how fast is each feature":

  | File | Written by | Contains |
  |---|---|---|
  | `feature_metrics.jsonl` | `feature_server.py` (central dispatch) | latency_ms, processing_ms, total_ms, ok ‚Äî **every** feature, every message |
  | `client_metrics.jsonl` | `handlers/metrics_handler.py` | client_load / client_action events from the OrangePi (model load times, pairing duration, etc.) |
  | `home_metrics.jsonl` | `handlers/home.py` | relay toggle/status esp_latency_ms, ok, stale_registration |
  | `ocr_metrics.jsonl` / `money_metrics.jsonl` / `tts_metrics.jsonl` | existing per-handler code (Section 7) | feature-specific detail (word counts, confidence, WAV size, etc.) already in place before this change |

All of them are now listed together on `handlers/lidar.py`'s `/metrics` HTTP
page (`http://<server>:8080/metrics`), which already existed as the shared
dashboard for OCR/Money/TTS (Section 7) and now also renders
`feature_metrics.jsonl`, `client_metrics.jsonl`, and `home_metrics.jsonl` as
the same kind of auto-generated HTML table (last 50 rows, generic
key-agnostic rendering ‚Äî no per-feature HTML template needed). This is the
single page to screenshot or scrape for the report's performance-results
section once real usage data has accumulated.

9.5 Filling In Actual Numbers for the Report

To populate the report with real measured figures rather than placeholders:
  1. Run the server normally for a session covering every feature at least
     once (a scan, a money read, a relay toggle, a lidar map save, a TTS
     request).
  2. Open `http://<server-lan-ip>:8080/metrics` and read off the
     `feature_metrics.jsonl` table ‚Äî this alone gives per-feature
     `latency_ms`/`processing_ms`/`total_ms` samples suitable for an
     average/min/max table.
  3. Read `client_metrics.jsonl` for the one-time load costs (expect
     Whisper/model loads to dominate ‚Äî typically several seconds ‚Äî versus
     sub-second or tens-of-milliseconds steady-state request latency).
  4. `home_metrics.jsonl` gives the relay round-trip time specifically,
     useful as a concrete "home automation responsiveness" figure separate
     from the ML-heavy features.

9.6 DIAGRAM GENERATION PROMPT ‚Äî Metrics Instrumentation Pipeline

Draw a data-flow diagram titled "Cross-Feature Performance Metrics". Left side: an "OrangePi feature (any of: money_recognition.py, ocr_reader.py, home_automation.py, ...)" box calling two things ‚Äî (1) `ServerLink.send(feature, msg)` which stamps `payload["_t_sent"] = time.time()` before framing/sending over TCP, and (2) an optional `metrics.report_load()` / `metrics.report_action()` call (from OrangePI/metrics.py) which fires a fire-and-forget `link.send("metrics", {...})` message. Center: "feature_server.py handle_client()" receiving a message, recording `t_recv`, computing `latency_ms = t_recv - _t_sent`, calling `handler.handle(msg)` while timing it as `processing_ms`, then writing one JSON line to `handlers/feature_metrics.jsonl` ‚Äî label this box "single instrumentation point covering every registered handler (money/ocr/lidar/home/tts)". A parallel small box "handlers/metrics_handler.py" receiving `feature="metrics"` messages and appending to `handlers/client_metrics.jsonl`. Right side: "handlers/lidar.py HTTP dashboard, /metrics page" reading and rendering `feature_metrics.jsonl`, `client_metrics.jsonl`, `home_metrics.jsonl`, `ocr_metrics.jsonl`, `money_metrics.jsonl`, `tts_metrics.jsonl` as generic auto-generated HTML tables. Use small clock icons on the `_t_sent`/`t_recv`/timing arrows to emphasize this is a timing-focused diagram, and annotate the clock-skew caveat near the `latency_ms` computation.
